zacharyrichard_cms - reports:(158)
ID,online,description_en,description_fr,foto,foto_type,foto_name,last_update
1 y <h3>On the road again.&nbsp; Tour journal October 2011.</h3>
<p><strong>October 21</strong>.&nbsp;  Dartmouth, Nova  Scotia.&nbsp;  Under grey skies, we  arrived in Halifax.&nbsp; Airport  hee-haw  and rental of our black Tahoe X.&nbsp;  Everybody in good spirits:&nbsp;  me,  Nicolas Fiszman, guitarist extraordinaire (from Brussels),&nbsp; Paul Lepage  front of house, Mathieu  Pontbriand backline and my darling Claude  Thomas keeping it all together.&nbsp; The <a href="http://www.fane.ns.ca/">FANE</a> (F&eacute;d&eacute;ration Acaidenne de la  Nouvelle-&Eacute;cosse) convention is in town and  the house is sold out, delegates  from all around the province.&nbsp;   Dinner in the dressing room of baked chicken take out.&nbsp; One of the most  difficult things in the  road is getting a decent healthy meal, that and  the travel.&nbsp;&nbsp; One of the things that does make  touring easier is  making time every day for a romp in the park.&nbsp; I always seek out a green  space which  is never very hard to find touring Canada.&nbsp; Behind the  hall was a football field behind which were the  woods.&nbsp; I found a path  and headed  out, returning as the light grew dim.&nbsp;  Good show with a  very enthusiastic crowd.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>October  22</strong>.&nbsp;  Beautiful fall day.&nbsp; On the lake across the road from the  hotel is a  flock of ducks, their migration begun.&nbsp; We are moving too,&nbsp;  headed west  across Nova Scotia.&nbsp;  The fall colors are dazzling.&nbsp;  An hour out of  Halifax, we stop at the Nova Scotia Visitor&rsquo;s  Center.&nbsp; I always get a  strange  feeling passing through the M&eacute;sagouche valley.&nbsp; Behind the  Visitor&rsquo;s Center is a stone monument alongside an  Acadian flag.&nbsp;&nbsp; On  the stone  are written the names of the last inhabitants of Beaubassin.&nbsp;  In 1750, in an attempt to force the  neutral Acadians into the French  camp, the missionary priest <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean-Louis_Le_Loutre">Le Loutre</a> and his  Mi&rsquo;kmaq allies burned the village, driving the Acadians west  and presumably  into the French camp.&nbsp;&nbsp; This  is one of the most bizarre  episodes of the Deportation.&nbsp; For years, Le Loutre had struggled to   raise money to build a church at Beaubassin.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; After incessant effort,  he prevailed.&nbsp; It is hard to imagine how he must have  felt when he  instructed his Mi&rsquo;kmaq friends to burn the church and the entire   village with it.&nbsp; Even after the treaty of  Utrecht in 1713 and the  establishment of a permanent British presence at Port  Royal, the  Acadians believed that they would be able to negotiate their   neutrality.&nbsp; They were wrong and  this illusion would cost them dearly:&nbsp;   the forced Deportation of the entire Acadian population.&nbsp; Le Loutre  was a bitter enemy of the  British, and the leader of a fifth column  made up  of Mi&rsquo;kmaq  warriors.&nbsp;&nbsp; My Richard  ancestors were at  Beaubassin in 1750 and would have seen their homes  destroyed.&nbsp; Sitting  and the  Visitor&rsquo;s Center with a view of the French fort Beaus&eacute;jour in  the distance , I  was seized by the same strange feeling that I get  every time that I pass  through here.&nbsp; It has been over 250  years since  the Deportation, but I am still troubled when I come to this spot. &nbsp;Oh  Canada.</p>
<p>Passing  through Sackville and  Memramcook, we arrive at Monkeytown (Moncton) and arrive  at the  Beaus&eacute;jour Hotel for&nbsp;  seafood chowder.&nbsp; A few  years ago, the  restaurant was renovated.&nbsp;&nbsp; The new look is neo-postmodern.&nbsp; Gone is the  old regular looking d&eacute;cor  replaced by bright and shiny bathroom tiles  and deco style lighting.&nbsp; I miss the old d&eacute;cor which was nothing   special but had the feel of an old pair of slippers.&nbsp; More disturbing to  me is that the recipe of the seafood  chowder changed as well.&nbsp; The old   Beaus&eacute;jour chowder was the best in the Maritimes.&nbsp; The new chowder is  good but not sensational.&nbsp;&nbsp; Another surprise was awaiting  me.&nbsp;</p>
<p>The  swimming pool at the Beaus&eacute;jour  was a treat for swimmers like me.&nbsp; Spacious and wide, it afforded  pleasure  and relaxation.&nbsp; Imagine my  disappointment to find that it  has been reduced by half to make room for a  &hellip;&hellip;.water slide.&nbsp; The hotel  proudly  proclaims that it&rsquo;s water slide is the &ldquo;Longest in the  region&rdquo;.&nbsp;&nbsp; In fact it is quite long,  twisting on itself like an  intestine.&nbsp;  The construction of the water slide is a frontal attack on  Moncton&rsquo;s  other major hotel, the Crystal Palace.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; That hotel has an  amusement park right in its  middle, fake pirate ships and tropical  islands accessible to each room.&nbsp;&nbsp; But now the Crystal Palace has a   competitor.&nbsp;  In it defense, the  Beaus&eacute;jour is still the best hotel in  town with comfortable rooms and a&nbsp; beautiful view of the Petit  Codiac.&nbsp;  I watched in wonder as the "tidal bore" came up the river.&nbsp; Ever since I  have been coming here, the tidal bore has been a featured attraction.&nbsp;  Due to the tides of the Bay of Fundy (the highest in the world), water  rushes up the river at high tide.&nbsp; Due to the silting caused by the  Riverview causeway, the tidal bore was quite boring, a few inches of  water moving up stream.&nbsp;After years of struggle by environmental groups,  the causeway was finally opened last year, restoring health to the  eco-system.&nbsp;From the window of the Beaus&eacute;jour, I watched in amazement as  a two foot wave of water moved up river.&nbsp; Persistence in righteous  course brings reward.&nbsp;</p>
<p>The show  tonight was at the  Weslayan Center, a mega-church in the American style.&nbsp; Not the best spot  for an acoustic show,  but it has the advantage of holding 1000 seats.&nbsp;  Above the stage is a whirlpool bath which serves as the  baptismal  pool.&nbsp; It was from just  above the  pool that I was able to watch Danny  Boudreau open the  show.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>23  October</strong>.&nbsp; Long  drive to Saint  Quentin.&nbsp; There are two ways to go:  along the coast, or  through the woods.&nbsp;  We decide to hug the coast, although you can only  see the ocean for a few  kilometers.&nbsp; Nonetheless, the fall  colors are  magnificent.&nbsp; We stop at  Bathurst in a little park for lunch.&nbsp;  My good  friend, Denis Landry, had fixed us a picnic basket with lobster  rolls  and fruit.&nbsp; We enjoy our  lunch in the open air, the weather chilly, but  not cold.&nbsp; We finally arrive in Saint Quentin and  check into the  hotel, l&rsquo;&Eacute;vasion de R&eacute;ve (the Dream Escape).&nbsp;&nbsp; Our room is decorated in a  golf  theme which is not surprising since the golf course is just next  door.&nbsp;&nbsp; Claude and I go for a walk in the  woods.&nbsp; The weather is autumn   style, and comfortable.&nbsp; Across the  road from the hotel is a huge  field with recently cut hay rolls.&nbsp; Nicolas is intrigued.&nbsp; They must not  have hay rolls in Belgium.&nbsp;</p>
<p>The show is  in Kedgwick in a small  theater amazingly well equipped for this spot.&nbsp; It is a great pleasure  to play with  Nicolas every night.</p>
<p><strong>October  24</strong>.&nbsp; On the road to <a href="http://www.tracadie-sheila.ca/">Tracadie</a>.&nbsp;&nbsp;  With Mathieu &ldquo;Road Warrior&rdquo;  Pontbriand at the wheel, the trip goes  quick and easy.&nbsp; We stop in at the Caf&eacute; Tazza, the local  health food  caf&eacute;.&nbsp; We run into my  good friend Oneal Comeau.&nbsp; Oneal  was the  promoter of my very first show in Tracadie in 1975!&nbsp; We have remained  friends ever  since.&nbsp; Oneal was a professional  diver and is now working  for the protection of the coast.&nbsp;&nbsp; The Bay of Tracadie is suffering   from a serious erosion problem caused by the rise in sea level (global   warming).&nbsp; Oneal is monitoring the  loss and attempting to raise  consciousness.</p>
<p>Checking in  at the <a href="http://www.deuxrivieres.ca/">Auberge Deux Rivi&egrave;res</a>.&nbsp;  The  crew chose one of the cabins which line the shore while the band  (Nicolas and  me) chose the comfort of the hotel.&nbsp;&nbsp;  Claude and I got  the royal treatment in the &ldquo;grande suite&rdquo; with a  beautiful view of the  bay and the old convent on the other shore.&nbsp; The suite is big enough to  hold the  crew, our truck and half of the population of Tracadie.&nbsp; The  personnel at the Auberge were very  charming and the director, Daniel  Chiasson, stopped by with a bushel of oysters  (Beausoleil, my favorite)  and a bottle of champagne.</p>
<p>The show  was in the studios of  Cin&eacute;-Atlantique.&nbsp;  I had already worked in this studio, taping a  television show.&nbsp; Tonight, the studio was converted to  concert  seating.&nbsp; Marie-Philippe  Bergeron was the opening act.&nbsp; I  was  delighted to discover this young singer, talented and energetic.&nbsp; I was  very very happy to see some old  friends:&nbsp; Raynald Basque, Anna and   Normand Th&eacute;riault and the very lovely Isabelle Th&eacute;riault.</p>
<p><strong>October  25</strong>.&nbsp; Day  off.&nbsp; Taking long walks along the shore.&nbsp; I take advantage of the spa  next door  for a massage.&nbsp; Time well  spent.&nbsp; On the grass, black  bellied  plovers in winter plumage.&nbsp; This  evening we are invited by the  crew to dinner in their cabin:&nbsp; baked haddock and a big green  salad.&nbsp;&nbsp;  It is a treat on the  road to be able to enjoy home cooking.&nbsp;  And the  oysters.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>October  26</strong>.&nbsp; This little tour is now half  over.&nbsp; Headed to Petit Rocher.&nbsp; We check in to the <a href="http://www.relaxseaside.com/">Toutes Saisons  B&amp;B</a>,  Phil and Barb Thibodeau our hosts.&nbsp; Originally from the area, Phil  spent his professional life  in Ontario where Barb is from.&nbsp; A  few  years ago they built this home on the shores of Baie des Chaleurs.&nbsp; The  sun is shining bright and we can  easily see Gasp&eacute;sie in the distance.</p>
<p>We have  dinner at <a href="http://www.finegrobe.com/welcome_en.htm">La Fine Grobe</a>.&nbsp;  Georges  Frachon greets us with his friendly smile.&nbsp; Halibut with  morilles.&nbsp;  Delicious. Georges is from the French alps but has had his  restaurant for many years, specializing in local seafood with a French  touch.&nbsp; Worth the trip.&nbsp;</p>
<p>The show is  in the Canadian Legion  Hall.&nbsp; I am  wary about the sound, but Paul Lepage works his usual  magic.&nbsp; Marie-Philippe Bergeron opens  again.&nbsp; The hall is packed and  very  hot.&nbsp; Great time.</p>
<p><strong>October  27</strong>.&nbsp;&nbsp; Barb  Tibodeau lets me  know about a local birder of some repute and this  morning, Roger Guitare comes  to fetch me for a little expedition.&nbsp;   Searching for <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horned_Grebe">Horned Grebes</a>.&nbsp;   We follow the coast north, passing through Belle Dune and the  industrial  plant which looms on this tranquil coast like a big ugly  sore.&nbsp; Several years ago, an American company  planned to build another  plant, this one to dispose of hazardous waste.&nbsp; The local population  organized and the  project was stopped.&nbsp; We continue  on to Benjamin  River.&nbsp; Thanks to Roger&rsquo;s  expertise and his telescope, I am able to  spot the grebes off shore.&nbsp; Also a common loon and what used to be   called Old Squaws (I don&rsquo;t remember the new name, in French, they are  called  Hareld Hakawi) all in winter plumage, white and black shapes  floating in the  waves.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Back at the  Fine Grobe for a lunch  of Marseille style bouillabaisse.&nbsp; Stomachs pleasantly full, we are on  the  road to Miramichi, arriving in the middle of the afternoon at the  Robbs  Inn.&nbsp; I take a little dip in the  pool to get the kinks out.&nbsp; We  play  at the Beausoleil Center.&nbsp;&nbsp;  The French speaking Acadian  population of the Miramichi is a small  minority, but is proclaiming its  presence with confidence.&nbsp; The Beausoleil is the epicenter of this   relatively new found assurance.&nbsp;  The first Acadian from Acadie that I  ever met (1973) was my good friend  Donald Doiron.&nbsp; Donald is from the   Miramichi.&nbsp; He explained to me that  during his childhood, the Acadians  here were very reluctant to proclaim their  identity.&nbsp; English was the  language  of commerce and there was great social pressure on the  Acadians to  assimilate.&nbsp; This is all the more ironic  since the  Miramichi was the site of the Camp de l&rsquo;Esp&eacute;rence (Camp of Hope)  during  the Deportation.&nbsp;&nbsp;  Fleeing the British, several thousand Acadians  would pass through the  Miramichi.&nbsp; Abb&eacute; le Geurne  describes their  plight during the first winter of 1755-1756: reduced to eating  their  shoes and bark from the trees, approximately 600 would die that winter   with a similar number passing away the next.</p>
<p>Donald told  me about the  &ldquo;Enclosure&rdquo;.&nbsp; When he  was young, he would swim at Wilson&rsquo;s Point, a  provincial park.&nbsp;&nbsp; In the park was a fenced area,  called the  &ldquo;Enclosure&rdquo; .&nbsp;&nbsp;  Human bones were uncovered here, exposed by erosion.&nbsp;  There has never been any archeological  digging done in this area, but I  believe that the &ldquo;Enclosure&rdquo; is a mass Acadian  grave and the site of  the &ldquo;Camp de l&rsquo;Esp&eacute;rence&rdquo;.&nbsp; This part of the local history is too  troubling, and  therefore has been left unexplored.&nbsp;  Like that of <a href="http://beaubearsisland.ca/">Beaubear Island</a>.&nbsp;   Charles Deschamps de Boish&eacute;bert was the French military commander in   this region during the Seven Years war.&nbsp;  The name of his stronghold,  l&rsquo;&Icirc;le de Boish&eacute;bert, has been Anglicized to  Beaubear, and the history  of his operations on the Miramichi erased by an  indifferent if not  hostile population.</p>
<p>But I have  not come here to dwell  on the past, but to celebrate the present through  music.&nbsp; The sold out  crowd is very  excited, due in part to the fact that French language  singers are few and far  apart in the Miramichi.</p>
<p><strong>October  28</strong>.&nbsp; The trip from Miramichi to  Memramcook is blessed by sunshine.&nbsp;  It is chilly, but beautiful weather.&nbsp; We check in to the <a href="http://www.monumentlefebvre.ca/">Institut Lefebvre</a>,  the birthplace of  modern Acadie.&nbsp; It is here in 1881,  that the first  Acadian Congr&egrave;s was held.&nbsp;  The Acadian flag (French flag with god star  on the blue field) was  designed and the Acadian National Holiday  proclaimed to be August 15.&nbsp;&nbsp; Today, Memramcook is a tranquil  village  with nothing to suggest its illustrious history if not for the Institut   itself.&nbsp; Built in 1897 of New  Brunswick sandstone, the building is  typical of the victorian architecture of  the time.&nbsp;&nbsp; The auditorium is   a jewel.&nbsp; It has 360 seats with the  original wood walls and floors.&nbsp;   The acoustics are perfect for a two guitar show.</p>
<p>Before the  show, we took advantage  of the invitation of our friend Denis Landry to visit  his new  restaurant in Moncton, Catch 22 (22 ways to fix lobster).&nbsp; I was not  very sociable, being tired  from the road and saving up my energy for  the show, but we all enjoyed the  lobster and the hospitality.</p>
<p>It is  always inspiring to play at  the Monument Lefebvre.&nbsp; I was very happy to see some old friends,  Hermance and Ralph  LeBlanc, their charming daughter Denise and my  bird-watching guru Alain  Clavette.&nbsp; They all gave me good  energy.&nbsp; It  was a special  night.&nbsp; Paul H&eacute;bert opened the  show.&nbsp; I am his biggest  fan and it  is always with great joy that I hear him sing.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>October  29</strong>.&nbsp; I was  reluctant to play at  Saint Jean (Saint John).&nbsp; The town  is in Anglo  territory and I am always prey to my Frenchie paranoia.&nbsp; Once again, I  was over-reacting.&nbsp; We arrived at the Hilton and were given  the &ldquo;royal&rdquo;  treatment, checking into the royal suite with a great view of the   harbor.&nbsp; Claude and I took a little  stroll in town.&nbsp; I discovered the   history of the <a href="http://website.nbm-mnb.ca/CAIN/english/sj_fire/index.asp?browse=true">Great Fire of 1877</a>.&nbsp;   As much as &frac34; of the town of Saint John was destroyed that year.&nbsp; Back  at the hotel for a little  swim.&nbsp; In spite of my trepidation,  the  evening was delightful.&nbsp; Sold  out show and a very excited crowd.&nbsp;&nbsp;   Paul H&eacute;bert opened the show again and I joined him for &ldquo;La Tourterelle&rdquo;   (the Dove).&nbsp; He repaid me the favor  by joining us for &ldquo;Au bord de Lac  Bijou&rdquo;.</p>
<p><strong>October  30</strong>.&nbsp;  Back to Montr&eacute;al.&nbsp; It is snowing in Saint Jean when we  left.&nbsp; The view  from the hotel was  beautiful.&nbsp; The river was dark  grey.&nbsp; The sky was  light grey with  snow flakes falling on the window to melt and trickle  down in rivulets colored  grey.&nbsp;</p> <h3>Sur la route.&nbsp; Voici le compte rendu de la r&eacute;cente tourn&eacute;e en Acadie.&nbsp;</h3>
<p><strong>21 Octobre</strong>.&nbsp;  Dartmouth,  Nouvelle-&Eacute;cosse.&nbsp;  Sous un ciel gris, on arrive &agrave; Halifax.&nbsp; Location de  v&eacute;hicule et d&eacute;part sur Dartmouth.&nbsp; L&rsquo;&eacute;quipe est en forme&nbsp;: moi,  Nicolas  Fiszman qui m&rsquo;accompagne &agrave; la guitare, Paul Lepage au son, Mathieu   Pontbriand backline et Claude Thomas.&nbsp;  La convention de la <a href="http://www.fane.ns.ca/">F&eacute;d&eacute;ration Acadienne de la Nouvelle-&Eacute;cosse</a> se tient  au m&ecirc;me moment et la salle est comble gr&acirc;ce en partie aux  d&eacute;l&eacute;gu&eacute;s qui arrivent  de partout.&nbsp; Souper dans la loge de  baked  chicken (la malbouffe est un des plus grands inconv&eacute;nients de la  tourn&eacute;e,  pius le voyage incessant).&nbsp; Comme  d&rsquo;habitude, je me prom&egrave;ne  dans la nature tant que possible.&nbsp; Je trouve une piste derri&egrave;re le  terrain  de football qui se trouve derri&egrave;re la salle&nbsp;&nbsp; Public tr&egrave;s  enthousiaste.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>22 Octobre</strong>.&nbsp;   Magnifique journ&eacute;e.&nbsp; Sur le  lac en face de l&rsquo;h&ocirc;tel des canards en route  pour le sud.&nbsp; Et nous vers l&rsquo;ouest.&nbsp; Traversant la Nouvelle-&Eacute;cosse, les   couleurs d&rsquo;automne sont magnifiques.&nbsp;  On arr&ecirc;te au Nova Scotia  visitor&rsquo;s center.&nbsp; &Ccedil;a me fait toujours bizarre de passer par ici.&nbsp;  Derri&egrave;re le bureau de tourise est un  monument, une pierre sur laquelle  est inscrit les noms des derniers habitants  de Beaubassin.&nbsp; La pierre   accompagn&eacute;e de drapeau acadien.&nbsp; On  explique qu&rsquo;en 1750, <a href="http://cyberacadie.com/index.php?/deracinement_biographie/Jean-Louis-Le-Loutre.html">Abb&eacute; le Loutre</a> et ses alli&eacute;s Mi&rsquo;qmac ont br&ucirc;l&eacute; le village  pour obliger les Acadiens  de s&rsquo;installer &agrave; l&rsquo;ouest en territoire fran&ccedil;ais.&nbsp; Peut-&ecirc;tre l&rsquo;histoire  le plus &eacute;trange de  la D&eacute;portation, ce missionnaire et chef de guerre, a  mis le feu &agrave; l&rsquo;&eacute;glise de  Beaubassin, &eacute;glise pour laquelle il avait  recueilli des fonds pendant des  ann&eacute;es et pour la construction de  laquelle il avait travaill&eacute;  incessamment.&nbsp; Voyant que la guerre   s&rsquo;approchait, Le Loutre d&eacute;cide de provoquer les choses et obliger les  Acadiens  de s&rsquo;engager du c&ocirc;t&eacute; des Fran&ccedil;ais.&nbsp;  Depuis le trait&eacute;  d&rsquo;Utrecht de 1713, les Acadiens avaient cru &agrave; leur  ind&eacute;pendance et &agrave; la  possibilit&eacute; de n&eacute;gocier avec les Britanniques.&nbsp; Ils se trompaient et  allaient payer un  prix tr&egrave;s cher pour cette erreur&nbsp;: la D&eacute;portation  forc&eacute;e.&nbsp; Le Loutre &eacute;tait l&rsquo;ennemi implacable des  Britanniques et bien  que tr&egrave;s proche des Acadiens, il n&rsquo;h&eacute;site pas de prendre  des moyens  tr&egrave;s durs dans la d&eacute;fense de la cause fran&ccedil;aise.&nbsp; Mes anc&ecirc;tres Richard  habitaient  Beaubassin &agrave; l&rsquo;&eacute;poque.&nbsp; Assis au  visitor center avec la vu  sur l&rsquo;emplacement du fort Beaus&eacute;jour d&rsquo;un c&ocirc;t&eacute; et la  voix ferr&eacute;e qui  coupe &agrave; travers le coeur de Beaubassin de l&rsquo;autre, je suis  envahi par  un sentiment &eacute;trange comme &agrave; chaque fois que je passe par ici.&nbsp; &Ccedil;a fait  plus de 250 ans, mais je suis  toujours choqu&eacute; par ce qui s&rsquo;est pass&eacute;.&nbsp;   Oh Canada.</p>
<p>On passe  par Sackville, MemRamCook et arrive &agrave; Monkeytown  (Moncton) pour manger  une chaudr&eacute;e de fruits de mer &agrave; l&rsquo;h&ocirc;tel Beaus&eacute;jour.&nbsp; Il y a quelques  ann&eacute;es, on a tout  refait le restaurant de l&rsquo;h&ocirc;tel.&nbsp;  Dans un style  neo-post-modernoide on a install&eacute; une ambiance froide de  bain douche o&ugrave;  avant on avait une ambiance anodine, mais confortable comme une  veille  paire de pantouffles.</p>
<p>Ce  n&rsquo;est pas que l&rsquo;ambiance qui a souffert.&nbsp; L&rsquo;h&ocirc;tel Beaus&eacute;jour servait la  meilleure  chaudr&eacute;e de palourdes aux Maritimes.&nbsp;  Quand on a chang&eacute; le  d&eacute;cor, on a aussi chang&eacute; la recette de la  chaudr&eacute;e.&nbsp; Aujourd&rsquo;hui elle  est  bonne, mais sans plus.&nbsp; Une autre  mauvaise surprise m&rsquo;attendait.&nbsp;  Un  des grands atouts de l&rsquo;h&ocirc;tel &eacute;tait sa piscine.&nbsp; Grande et belle,  elle offrait d&eacute;tente et plaisir aux  nageurs.</p>
<p>Imaginez ma  d&eacute;ception quand je d&eacute;couvre que la piscine est  diminu&eacute;e par sa moiti&eacute;  pour faire de la place &agrave; un ........water slide  (glissade d&rsquo;eau).&nbsp; J&rsquo;ai  d&eacute;couvert  ensuite plusieurs publicit&eacute;s se vantant de la &laquo;&nbsp;plus grande  glissade de la  r&eacute;gion&nbsp;&raquo;.&nbsp; Ceci est une  attaque &agrave; visage d&eacute;couvert &agrave;  l&rsquo;h&ocirc;tel&nbsp;  Crystal Palace qui est un endroit horrible, les chambres  construites  autour un parc d&rsquo;attractions rempli de faux bateaux pirates  et &icirc;lots  tropicales, etc.&nbsp; Et maintenant le  Beaus&eacute;jour le rivalise.&nbsp;  Du  &laquo;&nbsp;progr&egrave;s&nbsp;&raquo;.&nbsp; C&rsquo;est  toujours le meilleur h&ocirc;tel &agrave; Monkeytown avec  des chambres spacieuses et des  couettes douces.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Le spectacle est dans le Centre  Wesleyan, une mega-&eacute;glise  dans le style n&eacute;o-Am&eacute;ricain.&nbsp; De  l&rsquo;&eacute;tage au  dessus du bain tourbillon qui sert de baptist&egrave;re, je regarde avec   plaisir Danny Boudreau faire la premier partie.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>23 Octobre</strong>.&nbsp; La   Grande Route vers Saint Quentin.&nbsp;  Il y a deux fa&ccedil;ons d&rsquo;aller, soit par  les terres ou par la c&ocirc;te.&nbsp; On choisi la c&ocirc;te, mais on ne voit la  mer  que pour quelques kilom&egrave;tres.&nbsp;  On est apais&eacute;, cependant, par les  magnifiques couleurs d&rsquo;automne.&nbsp; On arr&ecirc;te &agrave; Bathurst dans un petit parc   pour d&eacute;jeuner.&nbsp; Mon cher ami Denis  Landry, propri&eacute;taire de l&rsquo;Auberge  Gabrielle &agrave; Sh&eacute;diac et maintenant le Catch 22  &agrave; Moncton, nous avait  pr&eacute;par&eacute; un bon petit lunch le qu&eacute;dilles d&rsquo;homard (lobster  roll) qu&rsquo;on  consomme en plein air.&nbsp;  Arrivant finalement &agrave; Saint Quentin, on  s&rsquo;installe &agrave; l&rsquo;h&ocirc;tel Evasion de  R&ecirc;ve.&nbsp; L&rsquo;&eacute;quipe n&rsquo;arr&ecirc;te pas de se   moquer en chuchotant &laquo;&nbsp;Evasion de R&ecirc;ve&nbsp;&raquo; d&rsquo;une voix faut sexy.&nbsp; Notre  chambre est d&eacute;cor&eacute;e avec un th&egrave;me  golfe, ce qui n&rsquo;est pas &eacute;tonnant vu  que l&rsquo;h&ocirc;tel se trouve &agrave; c&ocirc;t&eacute; d,,,,,,,,un  terrain de golfe.&nbsp; Claude et  moi  prenons une marche dans le bois.&nbsp;  Il fait frais mais agr&eacute;able.&nbsp;   En face de l&rsquo;h&ocirc;tel est un grand champ tr&egrave;s rempli de grands rouleaux de   foin, chose qui &eacute;merveille Nicolas.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Le spectacle est &agrave; Kedgwick dans un  petit th&eacute;&acirc;tre  extr&ecirc;mement bien &eacute;quip&eacute; pour cet endroit au bout du  monde.&nbsp; Tous les soirs c&rsquo;est un plaisir  d&eacute;licieux d&rsquo;entendre Nicolas  jouer.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>24 Octobre</strong>.&nbsp; La  Route pour <a href="http://www.tracadie-sheila.ca/">Tracadie</a>.&nbsp;  Avec Mathieu  &laquo;&nbsp;Road Warrior&nbsp;&raquo; au volant, le voyage &agrave; Tracadie se fait  facilement.&nbsp; On se dirige sur le Caf&eacute; Tazza, le spot  sant&eacute; de la  ville.&nbsp; J&rsquo;ai le grand  plaisir de retrouver mon ami Oneal Comeaux.&nbsp;  C&rsquo;est Oneal qui a produit mon premier spectacle &agrave; Tracadie  en 1975!&nbsp;  C&rsquo;est un plongeur  professionnel qui se d&eacute;die maintenant &agrave; la protection  du littoral.&nbsp; Menac&eacute; par l&rsquo;&eacute;rosion caus&eacute;e par  l&rsquo;augmentation du niveau  de la mer (r&eacute;chauffement de la plan&egrave;te), les plages de  la Baie de  Tracadie s&rsquo;&eacute;rodent &agrave; vu d&rsquo;oeil.</p>
<p>&nbsp;Arriv&eacute; &agrave;  l&rsquo;<a href="http://www.deuxrivieres.ca/index.php/fr">Auberge des Deux Rivi&egrave;res</a> pour se reposer.&nbsp; L&rsquo;&eacute;quipe technique se loge dans un des chalets,  pendant que  les musiciens (moi et Nicolas) logent dans ce qu&rsquo;on appelle   &laquo;&nbsp;l&rsquo;h&ocirc;tel&nbsp;&raquo;.&nbsp; On nous  offre la grande suite avec magnifique vu sur la  Baie de Tracadie et le vieux  couvent de l&rsquo;autre c&ocirc;t&eacute;.&nbsp; La suite  est  assez grande pour contenir l&rsquo;&eacute;quipe enti&egrave;re, notre v&eacute;hicule et la moiti&eacute;  de  la population de Tracadie.&nbsp; Les  gens de l&rsquo;auberge sont tr&egrave;s  accueillants, et Daniel Chiasson, un ami de longue  date, arrive avec  bourriche d&rsquo;hu&icirc;tres <a href="http://www.maisonbeausoleil.ca/fr/index.htm">Beausoleil</a> (mes pr&eacute;f&eacute;r&eacute;es) et une  bouteille de champagne.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Le spectacle a lieu dans le studio  de Cin&eacute;-Atlantique.&nbsp; J&rsquo;ai d&eacute;j&agrave; travaill&eacute; sur une &eacute;mission de  t&eacute;l&eacute;vision  dans ce m&ecirc;me studio converti ce soir en salle de spectacle.&nbsp;  Marie-Philippe Bergeron fait la  premi&egrave;re partie.&nbsp; Je la d&eacute;couvre,  un  jeune talent avec toute sa carri&egrave;re devant elle.&nbsp; Je suis tr&egrave;s tr&egrave;s  heureux de retrouver de mes chers  amis&nbsp;: Raynald Basque, Anna et  Normand Th&eacute;riault et la tr&egrave;s jolie Isabelle  Th&eacute;riault.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>25 Octobre</strong>.&nbsp;   Journ&eacute;e libre.&nbsp; On la passe  &agrave; l&rsquo;Auberge se promenant sur la gr&egrave;ve.&nbsp;  Je  profite du spa pour m&rsquo;offrir un massage.&nbsp; Du temps bien pass&eacute;.&nbsp;  Sur la  pelouse, une vol&eacute;e de pluviers argent&eacute;s en plumage d&rsquo;hiver.&nbsp; Le soir  c&rsquo;est un souper avec l&rsquo;&eacute;quipe  dans le chalet de Paul et Matieu&nbsp;:&nbsp;   Haddock au four et grande salade verte.&nbsp; Pour une fois on mange bien.&nbsp;  Et les hu&icirc;tres.&nbsp;  Nous allons en manger pour plusieurs jours encore.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>26 Octobre</strong>.&nbsp; La  moiti&eacute; de la tourn&eacute;e maintenant derri&egrave;re nous, on se dirige vers Petit  Rocher.&nbsp; On est log&eacute; au <a href="http://www.relaxseaside.com/">B&amp;B  Toutes Saisons</a>,  accueilli avec sympathie par Phil et Barb Thibodeau.&nbsp; Originaire de la  r&eacute;gion, Phil a pass&eacute;  sa vie professionnelle en Ontario d&rsquo;o&ugrave; vient sa  femme. Il y a quelques ann&eacute;es,  ils se sont install&eacute;s ici sur la Baie  des Chaleurs.&nbsp; Le soleil est lumineux et on voit bien la Gasp&eacute;sie au   large.&nbsp;</p>
<p>On va manger au restaurant<a href="http://www.finegrobe.com/welcome_fr.htm"> La Fine Grobe</a>.&nbsp; Georges Frachon nous accueille avec sa  sympathie habituelle.&nbsp; Je prend le  fl&eacute;tan aux morilles.&nbsp;  D&eacute;licieux.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Le spectacle a lieu dans la salle de  la L&eacute;gion  Canadienne.&nbsp; J&rsquo;anticipe le pire du  point de vue technique,  mais Paul Lepage est un ma&icirc;tre et il nous assure un son  soyeux.&nbsp;&nbsp;  Marie-Philippe  Bergeron fait de nouveau la premi&egrave;re partie.&nbsp; Petit  Rocher est son village natal.&nbsp; La salle est tr&egrave;s tr&egrave;s pleine et il y   fait tr&egrave;s tr&egrave;s chaud.&nbsp; Bon moment.</p>
<p><strong>27 Octobre</strong>.&nbsp;  Barb  Thibodeau me parle d&rsquo;un miroiseur local tr&egrave;s chevronn&eacute;.&nbsp; Avec beaucoup  de plaisir je pars avec  Roger Guitare &agrave; la recherche des <a href="http://www.oiseaux.net/oiseaux/grebe.esclavon.html">gr&egrave;bes esclavons</a>.&nbsp;  On suit la c&ocirc;te, passant &agrave; c&ocirc;t&eacute; de l&rsquo;usine de Belle Dune,  esp&egrave;ce de  cauchemar industriel plant&eacute; au milieu de cette c&ocirc;te autrement   tranquille, pour arriver &agrave; Benjamin River.&nbsp; Au large, on trouve les  gr&egrave;bes dans leur plumage  hivernal.&nbsp; Il y a aussi har&egrave;lde  hakawi et  huard plongeon, tous en plumage d&rsquo;hiver, des petites taches blanches  et  noires au large, que je vois gr&acirc;ce &agrave; l&rsquo;expertise de Roger et &agrave; son   t&eacute;lescope.</p>
<p>D&eacute;part  de nouveau sur la Fine Grobe o&ugrave; Georges nous attend  avec une  bouillabaisse style marseillais.&nbsp;  La pense bien remplie, on prend la  route pour Miramichi, arrivant au  milieu de l&rsquo;apr&egrave;s-midi au Robbs Inn.&nbsp;   Une baignade dans la piscine pour me d&eacute;gourdir de la route.&nbsp;</p>
<p>On joue au <a href="http://www.ccbmiramichi.com/">Centre Beausoleil</a>.&nbsp;  La population acadienne francophone est tr&egrave;s minoritaire  dans la  Miramichi, mais elle se manifeste avec de plus en plus de  confiance.&nbsp;  Le Centre Beausoleil  est l&rsquo;endroit o&ugrave; &ccedil;a se passe.&nbsp; Mon  cher ami,  Donald Doiron, le premier Acadien du nord ,que j&rsquo;ai jamais rencontr&eacute;   (1973) est originaire de Miramichi.&nbsp;  Donald m&rsquo;explique que pendant sa  jeunesse, les Acadiens ont subi une  assimilation assez difficile.&nbsp; Le   travail se passait en Anglais et on &eacute;tait assez r&eacute;ticent de manifester  son  identit&eacute; acadienne.&nbsp; Ce qui est  tr&egrave;s ironique car pendant la  D&eacute;portation, le Camp de l&rsquo;Esp&eacute;rence se trouve dans  la Miramichi.&nbsp;  Plusieurs milliers  d&rsquo;Acadiens y sont r&eacute;fugi&eacute;s pendant l&rsquo;hiver  1755-1756.&nbsp; Abb&eacute; le Guerne a bien d&eacute;cri la p&eacute;nurie des Acadiens, r&eacute;duit   &agrave; manger leurs chaussures ou bien l&rsquo;&eacute;corce des arbres. On estime  qu&rsquo;environ 600  sont morts ce premier hiver et autant l&rsquo;hiver suivant.</p>
<p>Donald me parlait de Wilson&rsquo;s Point,  un parc provincial, o&ugrave;  il allait se baigner et o&ugrave; l&rsquo;on trouve.  &laquo;&nbsp;L&rsquo;&nbsp;enclosure&nbsp;&raquo;.&nbsp; Dans cet enclos renferm&eacute;, il y a des ossements  qu&rsquo;on  trouve gr&acirc;ce &agrave; l&rsquo;&eacute;rosion.&nbsp; Il  n&rsquo;y a jamais eu de fouille  arch&eacute;ologique, mais il est tr&egrave;s possible voir  probable que  &laquo;&nbsp;L&rsquo;enclosure&nbsp;&raquo; est un charnier acadien de l&rsquo;&eacute;poque de  la D&eacute;portation.&nbsp;  C&rsquo;est histoire,  comme celle du Camp de l&rsquo;Esp&eacute;rence a &eacute;t&eacute; effac&eacute;e.&nbsp;  Comme celle de l&rsquo;&icirc;le de Boish&eacute;bert.&nbsp; Charles Dechamps de Boish&eacute;bert est  le  commandant fran&ccedil;ais&nbsp; qui dirige les  op&eacute;rations militaires &agrave;  l&rsquo;&eacute;poque de la D&eacute;portation.&nbsp; Aujourd&rsquo;hui on appelle son &icirc;le &laquo;&nbsp;<a href="http://beaubearsisland.ca/">Beaubear  Island</a>&nbsp;&raquo;,  sans savoir d&rsquo;o&ugrave; vient le nom.&nbsp; Son origine, comme la pr&eacute;sence  acadienne de la r&eacute;gion  effac&eacute;e par le temps et une population  indiff&eacute;rente ou m&ecirc;me hostile &agrave; cette  partie de l&rsquo;histoire.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Le public est encore tr&egrave;s  enthousiaste, leur enthousiasme  attis&eacute; par le fait qu&rsquo;on ne voit pas  tr&egrave;s souvent artistes francophones passer  par ici.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>28 Octobre</strong>.&nbsp; Le   voyage de Miramichi &agrave; Memramcook se fait sous un beau ciel.&nbsp; Il fait un  peu frais, mais autrement  une journ&eacute;e splendide.&nbsp; On  s&rsquo;installe &agrave; l&rsquo;<a href="http://www.monumentlefebvre.ca/">Institut Lefebvre</a>,  berceau de l&rsquo;Acadie.&nbsp; C&rsquo;est ici en 1881 se tient le premier  Congr&egrave;s  Acadien.&nbsp; Pour la premi&egrave;re  fois, depuis la D&eacute;portation les Acadiens se  rassemblement ouvertement pour  revendiquer leur identit&eacute;.&nbsp; On  dessine  le drapeau (drapeau fran&ccedil;ais avec &eacute;toile or sur le champ bleu) et on  d&eacute;clare  le 15 ao&ucirc;t comme F&ecirc;te Nationale de l&rsquo;Acadie.&nbsp; Aujourd&rsquo;hui le  village est plut&ocirc;t bucolique, rien pour  rappeler son histoire  mouvement&eacute;e.&nbsp;  L&rsquo;auditorium est un bijou.&nbsp;  Construit en 1897, l&rsquo;&eacute;difice  en gr&egrave;s est typique de l&rsquo;architecture  victorienne.&nbsp; Le th&eacute;&acirc;tre  contient  360 places.&nbsp; Tout en bois, il a une  acoustique  particuli&egrave;rement bien adapt&eacute;e &agrave; un spectacle &agrave; deux guitares.&nbsp;</p>
<p>On a profit&eacute; de l&rsquo;invitation de Denis Landry et nous avons  descendu &agrave; Monkeytown pour manger au <a href="https://www.facebook.com/catch22lobsterbar?sk=wall">Catch 22</a>.&nbsp;  Homard et homard et homard.&nbsp; Je n&rsquo;&eacute;tait pas tr&egrave;s sociable, &eacute;tant un peu  fatigu&eacute;,  r&eacute;servant mon &eacute;nergie pour le spectacle, mais &ccedil;a n&rsquo;a pas  d&eacute;rang&eacute; personne, ou  bien me semblait.</p>
<p>C&rsquo;est toujours tr&egrave;s inspirant de  jouer dans ce petit th&eacute;&acirc;tre  vu son histoire et son acoustique.&nbsp;  Mon  plaisir a &eacute;t&eacute; augment&eacute; par les retrouvailles.&nbsp; Hermance et Ralph LeBlanc  accompagn&eacute; de  leur tr&egrave;s charmante fille, Denise, et mon cher ami et  oiseau-guru Alain  Clavette m&rsquo;ont tous donn&eacute; de l&rsquo;&eacute;nergie.&nbsp;  Une belle  soir&eacute;e.&nbsp; Paul  H&eacute;bert assure la premi&egrave;re partie.&nbsp;  Je suis son plus  grand fan et c&rsquo;est toujours un vrai plaisir de  l&rsquo;entendre chanter.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>29 Octobre</strong>.&nbsp;   J&rsquo;ai &eacute;t&eacute; assez r&eacute;ticent de jouer &agrave; Saint Jean (Saint John).&nbsp; Cette  ville est en territoire anglo et  je suis toujours proie de ma parano&iuml;a  Frenchie.&nbsp; On est arriv&eacute; est install&eacute; &agrave; l&rsquo;Hilton dans la suite dite   royale avec magnifique vue sur le port.&nbsp;  Petite promenade dans la  veille ville, apprenant sur l&rsquo;histoire du <a href="http://website.nbm-mnb.ca/CAIN/francais/sj_fire/index.asp">feu  de 1877</a> qui a d&eacute;truit les 3/4 de la ville.&nbsp; Il fait froid.&nbsp;  Retour &agrave; l&rsquo;h&ocirc;tel  pour une baignade dans la piscine.&nbsp; Souper dans le restaurant.&nbsp; Filet de  sole trop sal&eacute;.</p>
<p>J&rsquo;anticipe  le pire, mais comme c&rsquo;est souvent le cas, la  soir&eacute;e est enchant&eacute;e.&nbsp;  Salle comble  et un public tr&egrave;s enthousiaste, peut-&ecirc;tre encore d&ucirc; au  fait que les chanteurs  de langue fran&ccedil;aise sont assez rares dans cette  ville.&nbsp; En plus Paul H&eacute;bert fait de nouveau la  premi&egrave;re partie.&nbsp; Je  vais le  rejoindre pour une version de &laquo;&nbsp;La Tourterelle&nbsp;&raquo;.&nbsp; Il me repaie  le compliment en venant  chanter sur &laquo;&nbsp;Au bord du Lac Bijou&nbsp;&raquo;.</p>
<p><strong>30 Octobre</strong>.&nbsp; De   retour &agrave; Montr&eacute;al.&nbsp; &Agrave; Saint Jean,  il neige, la vue de l&rsquo;h&ocirc;tel est  magnifique de grisaille.&nbsp; La rivi&egrave;re est gris fonc&eacute;, le ciel gris   claire, les flocons de neige frappent la fen&ecirc;tre et fendent.&nbsp;</p> ÿØÿà JFIF      ÿş ;CREATOR: gd-jpeg v1.0 (using IJG JPEG v80), quality = 85

2 y <p>Back&nbsp; at the studio early in the afternoon, Nick  and Francis soldering irons in hand repairing wiring connections.&nbsp; My  own connection has been repaired, the connection with a part of my life  missing for nearly a year now.&nbsp;&nbsp; Studio recording is both a trial and a  pleasure.&nbsp; It always begins for me insecurely.&nbsp; Are the songs good  enough?&nbsp; Do I have the right tempos?&nbsp; The right keys?&nbsp; Are the  arrangements good?&nbsp;&nbsp; And most importantly, will I be able to deliver?&nbsp;</p>
<p>We started the session on a chilly  and rainy Sunday afternoon, October 2.&nbsp; It always takes a long time to  get settled.&nbsp; Searching for the &ldquo;sweet spot&rdquo;.&nbsp; Establishing the right  relationships:&nbsp; between the different players, the engineers, the room,  the console, &nbsp;the universe.&nbsp;&nbsp; Nicolas Fiszman and I had played the night  before in Ottawa, driving back in the wee hours of the morning.&nbsp; Tired  from the road.&nbsp; The fatigue is harder to overcome when one is trying  hard to get something going.</p>
<p>The day was long.&nbsp; Everybody was  happy when suppertime rolled around and we were able to get out of the  studio and sit around the long table.&nbsp; Indian food.&nbsp; Papadum and curry&hellip;  and conviviality.&nbsp;&nbsp; The evening was also long and laborious.&nbsp; It took a  long to get everything in place.&nbsp; Nothing surprising here.&nbsp;&nbsp; It&rsquo;s always  better to let things find their natural level rather than trying to  force everything.&nbsp; We stayed well past midnight, trying to get  everything right, even though these things take their own sweet time,  and it is always better to let them have their own way.</p>
<p>The next morning,&nbsp; I woke up in a  roomful of doubt.&nbsp; Had we made the right choices?&nbsp; Tempos?&nbsp; Keys? Did I  know what I was doing?&nbsp; Etc. etc.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Arriving at the studio, it was  discussion time.&nbsp; Everybody was worried, frustrated.&nbsp; Everybody had  something to say.&nbsp; And so we spent an hour turning things around and  looking at everything from every possible angle.&nbsp;&nbsp; But once we started  to play, the worries and uncertainly dissipated like clouds leaving a  blue sky.&nbsp; &nbsp;There was a flourish of good vibes, and smiles erupted all  around.&nbsp; At such a time, it is easy to remember why I love this job.</p>
<p>The afternoon of the second day of  recording was filled with good feeling and pleasure.&nbsp; It is a true  delight to play music and to make a living at it.&nbsp; It is a privilege to  be able to express oneself via this most noble of the arts.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Music has a very special place in my  life.&nbsp; It brings me joy and solace in hard times.&nbsp;&nbsp; To find joy in  singing, to celebrate life through music played with musician friends is  one of the great treasures of my life.&nbsp;&nbsp; I am fortunate be surrounded  by generous friends with whom I share the love of music and the chance  to make it together.&nbsp; Last night marked a turning point in a long and  difficult recovery.&nbsp;&nbsp; For the first time in a long while, I was singing  and dancing&hellip;&hellip;and smiling.</p>
<p>I am anxious to get back to the  studio,&nbsp; anxious to continue this exploration of celebration and  humanity.&nbsp; It&rsquo;s work, certainty, but it is also a great pleasure and a  great good fortune.&nbsp;&nbsp; There is not much in my life that I love as much  and that gives me as much pleasure.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; There is one thing: to love and  to be loved&nbsp;&nbsp; When we can have them both, love AND music, then we can  truly say that life is good.</p> <p>De retour</p>
<p>Arriver au studio t&ocirc;t dans  l&rsquo;apr&egrave;s  midi, Nick et  Francis avec les fers &agrave; souder entre les mains en train   de r&eacute;parer  des connections.&nbsp; Ma  connexion enfin bien r&eacute;tablie avec  cette partie  de moi-m&ecirc;me perdu de vue depuis  bien t&ocirc;t un an.&nbsp;  L&rsquo;enregistrement  est  une &eacute;preuve et aussi un d&eacute;lire de plaisir.&nbsp; &Ccedil;a  commence avec  l&rsquo;ins&eacute;curit&eacute;, la recherche, le doute.&nbsp; Est-ce que les  chansons sont   bonnes?&nbsp; Est-ce que les  arrangements sont bons?&nbsp; Est-ce  que  je vais  pouvoir livrer la marchandise?&nbsp;</p>
<p>Nous avons commenc&eacute; dimanche, 2  octobre.&nbsp;  l&rsquo;installation est toujours un long  proc&egrave;s, trouver  l&rsquo;emplacement,  chercher le bon endroit.&nbsp; Comment se placer, Comment se  tenir.&nbsp; Nous  avons jou&eacute; la veille, revenu dans  la nuit.&nbsp; Fatigu&eacute; par la  route, le   dimanche a &eacute;t&eacute; un peu hasardeux.&nbsp;  La fatigue est d&rsquo;autant  plus sentie  quand on a tr&egrave;s envie que &ccedil;a se  passe.</p>
<p>La journ&eacute;e a &eacute;t&eacute; longue.&nbsp; Rendu le  soir, on &eacute;tait  tous contents d&rsquo;arr&ecirc;ter pour  s&rsquo;assoire &agrave; table.&nbsp;  Livraison d&rsquo;un   restaurant indien.&nbsp; Papadum et  cari., et convivialit&eacute;.&nbsp;  La soir&eacute;e  a  &eacute;t&eacute; &eacute;galement longue.&nbsp; Les choses  ne se pla&ccedil;aient pas  trop.&nbsp; On &eacute;tait   frustr&eacute;. mais il n&rsquo;avait rien de surprenant.&nbsp; On ne  peut pas forcer  les choses.&nbsp; On a rester bien apr&egrave;s minuit, essayant  d&rsquo;arranger des   choses qui allaient imposer leur propre &eacute;ch&eacute;ance.</p>
<p>Le lendemain matin. je me suis  r&eacute;veill&eacute; avec la   doute.&nbsp; Avon nous pris les bonnes  d&eacute;cisions?&nbsp; Est-ce  que les tempos   sont bons?&nbsp; Est-ce que les  tonalit&eacute;s sont bonnes?&nbsp;  Est-ce je  sais ce  que je fais?&nbsp; Etc. Etc.</p>
<p>Arriv&eacute; au studio, c&rsquo;est le temps de  la  discussion.&nbsp; Tous sont &agrave; vif, concern&eacute;s, un peu  frustr&eacute;.&nbsp; Mais   l&rsquo;incertitude se  dissipe au fur et &agrave; mesure que le travail avance, et &agrave;   moment donn&eacute;, comme les  nuages qui se dissipent, c&eacute;dant le ciel au   soleil, les sourires commencent &agrave;  sortir et on se rappellent pour quoi   on aime ce m&eacute;tier tant.</p>
<p>L&rsquo;apr&egrave;s midi de la deuxi&egrave;me journ&eacute;e  se distingue  par le  bonne humeur et le plaisir.&nbsp; C&rsquo;est  avant tout un  tr&egrave;s grand  plaisir de faire la musique, de pouvoir s&rsquo;exprimer &agrave;  travers  cet art  noble.&nbsp;</p>
<p>La musique prend une place de choix  dans ma vie.&nbsp;  Elle m&rsquo;apporte la joie et me soulage  dans les p&eacute;riodes  difficiles.&nbsp;  De  chanter &agrave; coeur joie, de c&eacute;l&eacute;brer la vie en compagnie  d&rsquo;amis  musiciens est pour  moi un grand privil&egrave;ge.&nbsp; Je suis  tr&egrave;s  chanceux  d&rsquo;avoir autour de moi des amis talentueux et g&eacute;n&eacute;reux.&nbsp; Hier au  soir  j&rsquo;ai tourn&eacute; le cap dans  une convalescence longue.&nbsp;</p>
<p>J&rsquo;ai  h&acirc;te de recommencer,  de  continuer cette exploration.&nbsp; Je  vais au  studio comme un enfant au  cour de jeux.&nbsp; Je vais travailler, certes,  mais c&rsquo;est un travail qui est   aussi un plaisir.&nbsp; Je ne sais pas  s&rsquo;il y  a meilleur dans la vie&nbsp;: de  faire quelque chose qu&rsquo;on aime et qui   nous donne autant de plaisir.&nbsp;  Oui,  il y a mieux&nbsp;: d&rsquo;aimer et de se  sentir aim&eacute;.&nbsp; Quand on conna&icirc;t les  deux, on peut se dire que la vie est   bonne.</p> ÿØÿà JFIF      ÿş ;CREATOR: gd-jpeg v1.0 (using IJG JPEG v80), quality = 85

4 y <p>The  first time that I toured France was in the summer of 1973.&nbsp; Thanks to my friend, the guitar builder  <a href="http://www.jamestrussart.com/">James Trussart</a>,  I played two festivals, Vierzon in Berri and Kertalg in  Britanny.&nbsp; I  have a very strong  memory of the festival in Vierzon.&nbsp;  It was there  that I first encountered the French folk scene and met  Gabriel Yacoub  and his group <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZR1rAWWH9OY">Malicorne</a>.&nbsp;   But it was in Kertalg that I got rocked, for it was there that I   discovered &ldquo;la musique bretonne&rdquo;, the Celtic musical tradition of <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brittany">Britanny</a>.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; I  was immediately seduced by the sound and especially by the melodies of Breton  music.&nbsp; <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=lYFWyQggIa0&amp;feature=related">Alan Stivell</a> was in his  prime and I was profoundly impressed by him and his harp.&nbsp;  That influence is evident in the melody  of &ldquo;R&eacute;veille&rdquo;, a tribute to the  Acadian struggle, which I composed shortly  after returning to the  USA.. I am surprised and pleased to see that it has  become an anthem to  a new generation of Acadians.&nbsp; It&nbsp; was recently  covered by a young  Anglo band from Nova Scotia, Fused for Tonight, in what I  consider to  be a very positive sign of reconciliation.&nbsp;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;  What  I did not understand in 1973 was that the music of Britanny, la  musique  bretonne, was undergoing a renaissance, or rather the second  phase of its  renaissance.&nbsp; That movement had  begun after the Second  World War in 1945, and&nbsp; when I arrived in 1973 was enjoying a surge as a  new  generation of musicians came on the scene integrating elements of  contemporary  rock music into the tradition.&nbsp;  That was what I  encountered at Kertalg.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The  &ldquo;bagad&rdquo; became the vehicle of Britanny musical culture after the war.&nbsp; The <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bagad">bagad</a> is a formation inspired by  the Scottish pipe band.&nbsp; It is  composed of  three sections, binou (bagpipe), percussion and bombarde, a wind   instrument of the oboe family.&nbsp;&nbsp;  The musical structure of the Scottish  pipe bands is relatively  formal.&nbsp; The bagadou, on the other  hand,  enjoys a greater freedom of expression and a wider diversity of   repertoire as well as style.&nbsp; This  diversity is enhanced by the  bombarde which has a broader musical scale than  the bagpipe allowing  for more polyphony.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Beginning  in 1965, a specifically Breton music scene evolved which was militant  culturally and politically.&nbsp; <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Stivell">Alain  Stivell</a> was the leader of the pack&nbsp;  with <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YRRrmDVOLBo">Tri Yann</a> and <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=SezRf_8vI94">Gilles Servat</a> following his lead.&nbsp; Traditional themes were melded with a   contemporary style through the inclusion of amplified instruments.&nbsp;&nbsp;  Different elements were included  in a &ldquo;cross-over&rdquo; typical of the  time.&nbsp;&nbsp; Artists did not hesitate to create new compositions  such as the  Symphonie Celtique of Alan Stivell and this brought Breton music to  a  wider audience.&nbsp; This movement  was supported by a multitude of groups  playing locally in the Fest-Noz, or  country dances.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;  This  was the music that I discovered at Kertalg in 1973.&nbsp;&nbsp; Breton  music was in full expansion and there was an  evident desire to expand  the style beyond the strict confines of the  tradition.&nbsp; This was also  typical  of the period.&nbsp; English folk bands  such as Fairport Convention  were pushing the bounds of traditional music,  creating a sub-genre of  rock.&nbsp;&nbsp;  But the foundation of Breton music, the melodic character and  the basic  rhythm, remained unchanged.&nbsp; This  was the model that I used  for the work I was beginning with Cajun music.&nbsp; Inspired by what I  discovered in  Britanny, I sought to combine a contemporary approach,  using electric guitar,  drums and bass, with a traditional Cajun root.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;  My  relationship with Cajun music was then and remains today tributary  of what I  learned from the music of Britanny in the early 70s.&nbsp; Always  with respect for the tradition, I have attempted to  modernize the style  by using rock instrumentation as well as cross-over  rhythms, such as  reggae and New Orleans second-line.&nbsp; It seemed to me then and seems to  me still that if  traditional music is to remain vital, it must  incorporate contemporary  elements.&nbsp; I have often been  criticized for  having &ldquo;betrayed&rdquo; or at least &ldquo;polluted&rdquo; the tradition.&nbsp; I am not sure  that my attempts at  &ldquo;m&eacute;tissage&rdquo; were successful, but I am convinced  that they were worth  trying.&nbsp;&nbsp; If there is a fault  to be found with  the new generation Cajun bands it is that experimentation has  given way  to conformity, and the richness of the tradition has suffered. What   ever happened to the hard rock traditional trio Mamou?&nbsp; And where are  the Cajun rap bands?&nbsp; The early stages of Cajun music were  defined by  cross-cultural pollination.&nbsp;  Afro-Caribbean, American, Irish, Spanish,  French, Acadian and German  ingredients went into the melting pot to  create the gumbo known as Cajun music.&nbsp; It is unfortunate that Cajun  music  today is strictly defined stylistically and seems to have no  place for any  thing other than a limited version of itself.&nbsp;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;  On  the other hand, it is interesting to see that the Festival  Interceltique de  Lorent has been including artists in the Acadian  tradition over the last few  years.&nbsp; This is not so surprising  since  the fiddle style of most Acadian (Canada) bands is evolved from the   Scots-Irish tradition.&nbsp; What is  surprising is that the festival is now  including Louisiana artists as  well.&nbsp; In its 41st  edition, the  Festival Interceltique included performances by <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BC1yOZ2nIoI">Danny Boudreau</a>, an  Acadian (New Brunswick) songwriter and my friend from Opelousas Louisiana,  <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=UGsiX5a9Zb8&amp;feature=related">Hadley Castille</a>.&nbsp;&nbsp;  They were  only 2 artists among well over&nbsp; one  hundred, but their  inclusion indicates that the organizers of the festival  consider that  Acadian and Cajun music are part of the Celtic tradition of  Britanny,&nbsp; I  could not agree  more.&nbsp;</p> <p>La  premi&egrave;re fois que je suis all&eacute; en France en tourn&eacute;e c&rsquo;est en 1973.&nbsp; Gr&acirc;ce &agrave; mon ami, le luthier <a href="http://www.jamestrussart.com/">James  Trussart</a>,  j&rsquo;ai particip&eacute; &agrave; deux festivals, Vierzon dans le Berri et Kertalg en   Bretagne.&nbsp; J&rsquo;ai un tr&egrave;s beau souvenir  du festival de Vierzon.&nbsp; J&rsquo;ai   d&eacute;couvert le folk fran&ccedil;ais et j&rsquo;ai rencontr&eacute; Gabriel Yacoub et son  groupe  <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZR1rAWWH9OY">Malicorne.</a>&nbsp; Mais c&rsquo;est &agrave; <a href="http://www.kemener.com/bretagnemusique/les-fetes-bretonnes-festival-kertalg.htm">Kertalg</a> que j&rsquo;ai &eacute;t&eacute; vraiment secou&eacute;.&nbsp;</p>
<p>C&rsquo;est  &agrave; Kertalg que j&rsquo;ai d&eacute;couvert la musique bretonne.&nbsp; Ces m&eacute;lodies et cette sonorit&eacute;&nbsp; m&rsquo;ont tout de suite s&eacute;duit.&nbsp; <a href="http://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Stivell">Alan Stivell</a> &eacute;tait dans sa p&eacute;riode de gloire.&nbsp; Il m&rsquo;a profond&eacute;ment touch&eacute;.&nbsp;&nbsp; Son influence est &eacute;vidente dans  la m&eacute;lodie de &laquo;<a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=3_AescSs6GA">&nbsp;R&eacute;veille</a>&nbsp;&raquo;,  chanson de revendication acadienne que  j&rsquo;ai compos&eacute;e &agrave; mon retour aux  USA, et qui allait m&rsquo;indiquer la trace &agrave; suivre  que je suis encore.&nbsp;  Cette chanson  est devenue, &agrave; ma surprise, l&rsquo;hymne de l&rsquo;identit&eacute; moderne  acadienne.&nbsp; Elle a &eacute;t&eacute; enregsitr&eacute;e par plusieurs,  mais plus r&eacute;cemment  par le groupe anglo nouvelle-&eacute;cossais, Fused for Tonight.&nbsp; Peut-il y  avoir un hommage plus  &eacute;loquent de la r&eacute;conciliation Anglo-acadienne?</p>
<p>J&rsquo;ignorais &agrave; l&rsquo;&eacute;poque  que la  musique bretonne &eacute;tait au d&eacute;but de sa renaissance, ou plut&ocirc;t la deuxi&egrave;me   phase de sa renaissance. C&rsquo;est &agrave; partir de la fin de la deuxi&egrave;me  guerre (1945)  que commence cette renaissance, mais elle a connu un  nouvel essor au d&eacute;but des  ann&eacute;es 1970 avec l&rsquo;arriv&eacute;e d&rsquo;une nouvelle  g&eacute;n&eacute;ration de musiciens.&nbsp;</p>
<p>&Agrave;pres la guerre, le bagad devient le v&eacute;hicule de la culture musicale  bretonne.&nbsp; Un <a href="http://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bagad">bagad</a> est une  formation musicale&nbsp; inspir&eacute;e du pipe-band &eacute;cossais. Le  bagad  comprend cornemuses et percussions mais en plus un pupitre de <a href="http://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bombarde_%28instrument%29">bombardes</a>,  un instrument  de la famille des hautbois.&nbsp; La  musique des pipe-bands  est structur&eacute;e d'une fa&ccedil;on assez formelle.&nbsp; Les bagadou, par contre,  profitent  d&rsquo;une structure plus libre et cela donne une diversit&eacute; plus  importante &agrave; la  fois dans les airs interpr&eacute;t&eacute;s et dans les styles de  jeu. La pr&eacute;sence des bombardes contribue  &eacute;galement &agrave; cette diversit&eacute;.&nbsp;  Ayant  une tessiture plus &eacute;tendue que  celle des cornemuses, la pr&eacute;sence  des bombardes ouvre plus largement les voies  de la polyphonie.</p>
<p>&Agrave; partir de 1965, se d&eacute;veloppe une sc&egrave;ne musicale ouvertement bretonne  et souvent militante.&nbsp;Alan Stivell d'abord, puis  au d&eacute;but des ann&eacute;es 70, <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m5hBpFaVroI">Tri Yann</a>, <a href="http://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilles_Servat">Gilles Serva</a>t  et bien  d'autres&nbsp; actualisent des th&egrave;mes  anciens par des sonorit&eacute;s  contemporaines (guitare &eacute;lectrique, basse,  batterie).&nbsp; Ces artistes  combinent  diff&eacute;rentes musiques ("cross-over")  et n'h&eacute;sitent pas &agrave;  cr&eacute;er de nouvelles compositions (la Symphonie Celtique d'Alan  Stivell, par exemple).&nbsp; Cette modernisation permet la diffusion  d&rsquo;une  musique bretonne &eacute;largie et diversifi&eacute;e. Ce mouvement musical est  soutenu  et relay&eacute; localement par une multitude de petits groupes qui  jouent dans les  festo&ugrave;-noz.</p>
<p>C&rsquo;est cette musique que je rencontre  &agrave; Kertalg en 1973.&nbsp; Il y avait une effervescence et une  volont&eacute;  d&rsquo;exp&eacute;rimentation tr&egrave;s caract&eacute;ristique de la musique dite  &laquo;&nbsp;rock&nbsp;&raquo; de  l&rsquo;&eacute;poque.&nbsp; Ce  jumelage de la musique traditionnelle et le rock a  commenc&eacute; en Angleterre avec  des&nbsp; groupes comme Fairport  Convention,  mais n&rsquo;a pas tard&eacute; &agrave; traverser la Manche.&nbsp;&nbsp; N&eacute;anmoins, le caract&egrave;re  fondamental m&eacute;lodique ainsi  que rythmique de la musique de la rel&egrave;ve en  Bretagne, reste profond&eacute;ment  breton. &nbsp;C&rsquo;est le mod&egrave;le que j&rsquo;ai   utilis&eacute; pour le travail que je commen&ccedil;ais avec la musique traditionnelle   cadienne, c&rsquo;est-&agrave;-dire de greffer une branche contemporaine issue du   &laquo;&nbsp;rock&nbsp;&raquo; sur une racine traditionnelle.</p>
<p>Ma relation avec la musique dite  cadienne a toujours &eacute;t&eacute; et reste  encore aujourd&rsquo;hui tributaire de ce  que j&rsquo;ai appris en Bretagne &agrave;  l&rsquo;&eacute;poque.&nbsp; Toujours en gardant un  grand  respect pour la tradition, j&rsquo;ai tent&eacute; de la moderniser, en utilisant des   sonorit&eacute;s contemporaines, guitares &eacute;lectriques par exemple, et des  rythmes  d&rsquo;ailleurs, reggae ou &laquo;&nbsp;New Orleans second-line&nbsp;&raquo;.&nbsp; Il me  semblait et me semble encore que  la musique traditionnelle doit  toujours &eacute;voluer et que l&rsquo;int&eacute;r&ecirc;t de cette  musique est augment&eacute; par le  m&eacute;tissage.&nbsp;  J&rsquo;ai &eacute;t&eacute; souvent critiqu&eacute; pour avoir &laquo;&nbsp;trahi&nbsp;&raquo; la  tradition,  ou du moins de l&rsquo;avoir corrompue.&nbsp;  Je ne pense pas toujours  avoir r&eacute;ussit mes tentatives de m&eacute;tissage, mais  je crois que  l&rsquo;exp&eacute;rience valait la peine.&nbsp;&nbsp; S&rsquo;il y a un d&eacute;faut de la &laquo;&nbsp;Cajun music&nbsp;&raquo;  de  nos jours, c&rsquo;est qu&rsquo;elle est souvent monotone. L&rsquo;exp&eacute;rimentation a  c&eacute;d&eacute; sa  place &agrave; la conformit&eacute;, ce qui rend le tout assez semblable.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Par contre, il est tr&egrave;s int&eacute;ressant de voir que le <a href="http://www.festival-interceltique.com/">Festival  Interceltique de Lorient</a> donne une place &agrave; la musique acadienne du Canada ainsi  qu&rsquo;&agrave; la musique  cadienne de Louisiane.&nbsp;&nbsp; La 41e &eacute;dition du festival en 2011 a vu sur   sc&egrave;ne <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NIh0XjLXBRY">Danny Boudreau</a>, le songwriter acadien et <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hadley_Castille">Hadley Castille</a> de  Louisiane.&nbsp;&nbsp; Ils ne sont que  deux artistes parmi des centaines,  mais leur pr&eacute;sence indique que, au moins du  point de vue des  organisateurs du festival,&nbsp; la musique acadienne et la musique cadienne  font partie de  la tradition celtique bretonne.&nbsp; Je  ne pourrais pas  &ecirc;tre plus d&rsquo;accord.&nbsp;</p> 2011-09-07 00:00:00
3 y <p>On October 17, I suffered right ischemic stroke and spent five days in the<br /> hospital.  I am re-evaluating my life, in light of which, I am returning to<br /> poetry for this report, in an attempt to spread some beauty in the world.</p>
<p>My recovery will be good and my purpose strong and I will re-emerge like the<br /> phoenix from the ashes with new and brilliant feathers for my wings.</p>
<p><strong>Blue Naked</strong></p>
<p><em>Awoken in the middle </em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Of the seventh night,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Needle piercing</em><br /><em> My left eye,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Rimmed in red cage,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The dreams of</em><br /><em> Marie Laveau,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; woman in naked blue.</em></p>
<p><em>Rising at 5 AM,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Grey dawn, calling</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The secret words</em><br /><em> Falling into coma</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Near hold to woman tied </em></p> <p>Le 17 octobre, j'ai &eacute;t&eacute; victime d'une AVC dite isch&eacute;mique.  J'ai pass&eacute; cinq<br /> jours &agrave; l'h&ocirc;pital.  Je suis bien oblig&eacute; de r&eacute;&eacute;valuer ma vie, et dans ce<br /> contexte je retourne &agrave; la po&eacute;sie pour ce rapport dans l'espoir de r&eacute;pandre<br /> un peu de beaut&eacute; dans ce monde.</p>
<p>Je vais r&eacute;cup&eacute;rer compl&egrave;tement et je vais revenir tel le ph&eacute;nix des cendres<br /> avec des nouvelles plumes brillantes pour mes ailes.</p>
<p>Esprits animaux</p>
<p><em>Esprits des animaux la nuit&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; grattant &agrave; mon ch&acirc;ssis,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; d&eacute;chirant le moustiquaire,</em><br /><em> Leurs yeux rouges</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; brillant comme les phares</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; d&rsquo;un gros camion sur</em><br /><em> La 138 entre Sept Iles et</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Havre St. Pierre.</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Mes fr&egrave;res, mes cousins,</em><br /><em> Chats, ours, loups,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; me chantant leurs veilles chansons,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; me tra&icirc;nant par la nuque.</em></p>
<p><em>La chasse du shaman</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; autour du feu sacr&eacute;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; cherchant le pont</em><br /><em> Pour traverser perception senti</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; avant mammif&egrave;re, avant reptile,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; avant baleine, avant poisson,</em><br /><em> Avant pierre, avant roche,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; avant montagne, avant colline,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; avant froid,</em><br /><em> Avant connaissance,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; avant &ccedil;a,&nbsp; avant.</em></p>
<p><em>Je suis voyageur jaguar</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; de griffe et de dent,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; mes yeux qui voient </em><br /><em> Claire la nuit comme</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &agrave; la clart&eacute; du jour,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; capable de voir dans le noir,</em><br /><em> Capable de tuer.</em></p>
<p><em>Chassant la v&eacute;rit&eacute;,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; plus loin, plus loin</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; infiniment plus loin,</em><br /><em> D&eacute;pass&eacute; plus loin,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; mes mains devenues pattes</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; devenues nageoires,</em><br /><em> Devenues ailes, devenues fragiles </em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; et majestueuses.</em></p>
<p><em>On sent l&rsquo;hiver s&rsquo;en venir.</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; on sent l&rsquo;odeur de la mort,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; des vagues sur le fleuve,</em><br /><em> Chuchotant un nom noir,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Y&rsquo;a rien qui dure.</em></p>
<p><em>Appelant les esprits</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; demandant de leurs conseilles,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; demandant de leur compassion.</em><br /><em> Dans cette nuit au bord de l&rsquo;hiver</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; le sommeille vol&eacute; par des corbeaux</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; et emmen&eacute; loin.</em><br /><em> Dans mon coeur une petite douleur</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; qui se fait grande,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; et la peur, la peur</em><br /><em> D&rsquo;&ecirc;tre seul.&nbsp; Et j&rsquo;appel,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; j&rsquo;appel ours et&nbsp; hiboux</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; li&egrave;vre et serpent,</em><br /><em> Renard et caribou,</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; mes fr&egrave;res, mes soeurs.</em></p>
<p><em>Dans cette petite chambre triste</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; au milieu d&rsquo;une nuit p&eacute;rilleuse</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; au bout du monde</em><br /><em> une femme dort.&nbsp; Elle voyage</em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; dans ses r&ecirc;ves, </em><br /><em> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; soupirant</em><br /><em> Pendant que je guette.</em></p> 2010-11-04 00:00:00
5 y <p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; In the last Canadian election, the Bloc Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois took a shelacking.   The Bloc is a national political party whose raison d&rsquo;&ecirc;tre is the  separation of Qu&eacute;bec from Canada, and whose appeal is limitied solely to  that province.  Even its leader Gilles Duceppe was not re-elected.   In  many ridings in Qu&eacute;bec, it was the New Democratic Party, left of  center, that made considerable gains.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; In the last few weeks, the Parti Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois, the provincial  version of the Bloc, has been rocked by scandal.  One after another,  figureheads of the partry, Louise Beaudoin and Pierre Curzi to name two,  have resigned.  The party&rsquo;s leader, Pauline Marois, is standing on  shakey ground.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Not since the gound swell of support for Qu&eacute;bec sovreignty in the  mid 1970s has the separatist movement seen darker days.  There were the  referendums of 1981 and 1995.  The first was a very very slim (.5%)  defeat of sovreignty.  The second was a more convincing defeat,  provoking an embittered and tipsy Jacque Parizeau to castigate the &laquo;  ethnic &raquo; meaning immigrant i.e. non-French Canadian vote.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; It seems the idea of Qu&eacute;bec sovreignty has now become obsolete.   This is a far cry from the heady days when I first arrived in Qu&eacute;bec in  the mid 70s.  At that time, the political atmosphere was electric.  On  November 15, 1976, I was at a restaurant on Prince Arthur street when  the news came that the Parti Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois had won the provincial election.   The supporters of the Parti Qu&eacute;becois could hardly believe that their  candidate, a soft spoken ex-journalist from the Gasp&eacute; peninsula, Ren&eacute;  L&eacute;vesque, had been elected prime minister.  After years of second class  economic and political status in their own province, the French speaking  Qu&eacute;becois were in the driver&rsquo;s seat.  The entire restaurant erupted.   Spilling into the street, we danced and sang and hugged and cried.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The late 1970s were an amazing time in Qu&eacute;bec. There was a real  notion that Qu&eacute;bec could indeed become an independent political state.   That notion was not diminished by the squeeky tight referendum of 1981.   Anglophone Quebeckers left the province in droves creating a real  estate market crash.  The spectre of an independent Qu&eacute;bec sent the  Canadian dollar spinning, knocking 25% of its value viz-&agrave;-viz the U.S.  currency.  It would take 30 years to recover.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Those years have not been kind to the separatist movement.  In  sp&icirc;te of real social gains, and official linquistic equality, the  Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois themselves no longer seem to care about becoming an indepedant  state. The appeal of the Parti Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois seem to be a thing of the  past.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Qu&eacute;b&eacute;c will always have a particular status in the Canadian  conferderation.  It is and will remain the second most populous  province.  But its demographics have shifted significantly in the last  decades.  With French Canadian birth rates dropping the population  increase in Qu&eacute;bec depends largely on immigration.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; I have just taken a trip to NDG, Notre Dame de Grace, a  neighborhood in the west of the island of Montreal.  In spite of its  name, the neighborhood is a multi-ethnic melting pot. In the street one  as likely to hear Hindi as French.  As Montreal becomes more and more  multi-ethnic, the importance of the French Qu&eacute;becois population is  diminished and the relative dominance of the English language is  enhanced.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The result is an intriguing mix of culture, although it is clear  that there is little crossing of ethnic lines.  The traditional contrast  between English Quebecker and the French Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois, is very nuanced by  the ethnic diversity.  In spite of the language protection laws,  arguably the most important legaacy of the Parti Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois.  English is  becoming more and more prevalent,  as a trip to the airport  confirms.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Will the notion of sovreignty ever enjoy a resurgence?  Gone is  the notion of second class status.   The major impetus for the  separatist movement was the notion, amongst its supporters, that they,  the French, had been oppressed socially, politically and economically by  the English.  Until the election of the Parti Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois and the passage  of Bill 101, the official language act, there were no French language  signs in downtown Montreal.  The city was split in two by the Boulevard  St. Laurent (the Main to the Anglos) and there was no real French  presence west of the Main.  With the success of C&eacute;line Dion, Cirque du  Soleil, Bombardier and others, the notion that French Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois are  confined to a second class status no longer holds water.  And there is  no desire to rock the boat.  Things are going well for Qu&eacute;bec.  The  standard of living compares with that of any developed country.  The  quality of life is appreciable.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Given the indifference of the moment, one must wonder whether the  Parti Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois will ever regain the status it enjoyed in the 1970s and  1980s or will it continue to erode, to become an interesting but  otherwise unimportant  chapter in the history of the province?   Will  the legacy of the Parti Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois be linguistic equality rather than  political independence? &nbsp; Likely. <br /> Ever since 1759, the French of Qu&eacute;bec have struggled to maintain their  linguistic and cultural idenity.   Economic power until the 1960s has  been in the hands of Anglos.  Political power is another story.&nbsp; Since  the 1970s there has been a tug of war in the province between those  intent on separation and those, including French Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois, for whom  sovreignty represents a insecurity and the dreadful end of the Canadian  federation.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; I will never forget the night of November 15, 1976  when, to  everyone&rsquo;s surprise Ren&eacute; L&eacute;vesque and the Parti Qu&eacute;bcois swept to power.   For a decade it seemed possible and even likely that Qu&eacute;bec would  become an independant state.  Today that seems unlikely. But who knows  what the future will bring.&nbsp; Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois have achieved an economic and  linguistic status unimaginable not so long ago.&nbsp; The notion that only an  independent Qu&eacute;bec could satisfy the ambitions of its population no  longer seems to be true, or at least no longer resonates as it did in  the 1970s.&nbsp;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; These are interesting times.  The Arab world is afire with  democracy while in Qu&eacute;bec, the French Qu&eacute;b&eacute;ois seem content enough of  their status not to rock the boat.  After all, C&eacute;line is playing Vegas.</p> <p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Aux derni&egrave;res &eacute;lections f&eacute;d&eacute;rales au Canada, &agrave; la surprise g&eacute;n&eacute;rale le  Bloc Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois a pris une grosse claque.  M&ecirc;me son chef, Gilles Duceppe  n&rsquo;a pas r&eacute;ussi &agrave; garder son si&egrave;ge.  Dans plusieurs circonscriptions au  Qu&eacute;bec, c&rsquo;est le NDP, parti centre gauche qui a marqu&eacute; des gains.<br /> Dans les derni&egrave;res semaines, le Parti Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois est secou&eacute; par le  scandale.  Un apr&egrave;s l&rsquo;autre, plusieurs de ses piliers, Louise Beaudoin  et Pierre Curzi entre autres, ont donn&eacute; leurs d&eacute;missions.  Le chef du  parti, Pauline Marois est attaqu&eacute;e &agrave; tout bord.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;                   Le mouvement souverainiste n&rsquo;a pas connu d&rsquo;un tel  d&eacute;sarroi depuis son &eacute;lan des ann&eacute;es 1970.   On se souvient des  r&eacute;f&eacute;rendums de 1981 et 1995.   On se souvient d&rsquo;un Ren&eacute; L&eacute;vesque en 1981  tr&egrave;s &eacute;mu disant &laquo; Si je vous ai bien compris, vous dites &agrave; la prochaine  fois. &raquo;  On se souvient d&rsquo;un Jacques Parizeau en 1995, un peu ivre et  col&eacute;reux en plus accusant le &laquo; vote ethnique &raquo; d&rsquo;avoir saboter les  chances pour un Qu&eacute;bec ind&eacute;pendant.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;                   Il semble que l&rsquo;id&eacute;e d&rsquo;un Qu&eacute;bec souverain est  d&eacute;pass&eacute;e.  On est tr&egrave;s loin des ann&eacute;es 1970.  Il y a 35 ans,  l&rsquo;atmosph&egrave;re politique &eacute;tait &eacute;lectrique.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; J&rsquo;ai mis les pieds au Qu&eacute;bec pour la premi&egrave;re  fois en 1974 et j&rsquo;ai &eacute;t&eacute; propuls&eacute; dans le courant du mouvement  s&eacute;paratiste aussi t&ocirc;t.  J&rsquo;ai dans&eacute; avec tout le monde dans la rue Prince  Arthur la nuit du 15 novembre, 1976 quand le Parti Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois a pass&eacute; au  pouvoir.   On ne croyait &agrave; peine que ce petit souri d&rsquo;homme qui  s&rsquo;appelait Ren&eacute; L&eacute;vesque, ancien journaliste originaire de la Gasp&eacute;sie,  est devenu le premier ministre du Qu&eacute;bec.  Son programme &eacute;tait clair :  la souverainet&eacute; du Qu&eacute;bec.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;                   La fin des ann&eacute;es 70 est un moment incroyable au  Qu&eacute;bec.  Il y avait une vraie confiance parmi les souverainistes, et  l&rsquo;id&eacute;e d&rsquo;un Qu&eacute;bec libre, selon le terme de Charles de Gaulle, &eacute;tait  tellement plausible que nombreux sont les anglophones qui vendent leurs  biens et d&eacute;m&eacute;nagent ailleurs.  Cette inqui&eacute;tude n&rsquo;est pas diminu&eacute;e par  le r&eacute;f&eacute;rendum de 1981.  Bien qu&rsquo;une victoire pour le &laquo; non &raquo;, la  justesse de la victoire (.5%) n&rsquo;&eacute;tait pas pour calmer les esprits. Le  dollar canadien a chut&eacute; face &agrave; la possibilit&eacute; que le Qu&eacute;bec se s&eacute;pare du  reste du Canada.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;                   Les ann&eacute;es n&rsquo;ont pas &eacute;t&eacute; trop douces avec le mouvement  s&eacute;paratiste.  Il y aura toujours une partie de la population qui va  soutenir la s&eacute;paration, mais en 2011, il semble que personne n&rsquo;y croit  vraiment.  Avec les taux de naissance des Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois de souche en baisse,  la province doit attirer les immigrants pour maintenir sa d&eacute;mographie,  et les communaut&eacute;s immigrantes n&rsquo;ont aucune sensibilit&eacute; envers la  question s&eacute;paratiste.</p>
