<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;                   J&rsquo;arrive d&rsquo;un petit tour  NDG, Notre Dame de Gr&acirc;ce, un  quartier dans l&rsquo;ouest de l&rsquo;&icirc;le.  Malgr&eacute; son nom, c&rsquo;est un quartier  multiethnique.  Dans la rue, on est sujet d&rsquo;entendre parler le hindi  autant que le fran&ccedil;ais.   Au fur et &agrave; mesure que Montr&eacute;al devient de  plus en plus un &laquo; melting-pot &raquo;, l&rsquo;importance de la population qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois  fran&ccedil;aise ainsi que la langue fran&ccedil;aise diminue.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;                   Cette vague d&rsquo;immigration cr&eacute;e un m&eacute;lange int&eacute;ressant  de culture bien qu&rsquo;il n&rsquo;y ait pas trop de m&eacute;tissage.   Elle penche la  balan&ccedil;oire sociale d&eacute;finitivement sur le bord des Anglos.  La  confrontation anglo-franco traditionnelle est forc&eacute;ment modifi&eacute;e par  l&rsquo;infusion d&rsquo;une multitude de gens de pays divers, les fameux allophones  qui ne souhaite pas apprendre le fran&ccedil;ais.  Malgr&eacute; les lois sur la  protection de la langue fran&ccedil;aise, l&rsquo;anglais est de plus ne plus  dominant.  Il faut tout simplement aller &agrave; l&rsquo;a&eacute;roport pour comprendre  l&rsquo;ampleur du ph&eacute;nom&egrave;ne.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;                   Est-ce que le mouvement s&eacute;paratiste connaitra un  r&eacute;surgence?  Il me semble peu probable.  Ce qui a donn&eacute; beaucoup de  r&eacute;sonnance au mouvement &eacute;tait le statu de deuxi&egrave;me zone dans laquelle le  fran&ccedil;ais et les Canadiens fran&ccedil;ais furent rel&eacute;gu&eacute;s.  De ne pas trouver  du fran&ccedil;ais affich&eacute; dans le centre ville de Montr&eacute;al dans les ann&eacute;es  1960 renfor&ccedil;ait la notion que les Anglophones dominaient la vie sociale,  politique et &eacute;conomique de la province, et que par cons&eacute;quent, les  Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois de souche fran&ccedil;aise se sentaient opprim&eacute;s.<br /> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;                   Aujourd&rsquo;hui &ccedil;a va plut&ocirc;t bien pour la Qu&eacute;bec.  Avec le  succ&egrave;s de C&eacute;line, du Cirque du Soleil et de Bombardier, les Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois  n&rsquo;ont rien &agrave; envier &agrave; personne sur le plan international.   La qualit&eacute;  de vie au Qu&eacute;bec se compare favorablement aux pays du monde d&eacute;velopp&eacute;.   Sa culture est enrichie par une sensibilit&eacute; particuli&egrave;rement fran&ccedil;ais  qui se manifeste par une vision assez ouverte sur le monde, et une  cuisine raffin&eacute;e.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;                   Est-ce que le Parti Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois retrouvera le soutien  populaire qu&rsquo;il a connu dans les ann&eacute;es 1970 ou bien est-ce que son  influence va continuer &agrave; s&rsquo;&eacute;roder jusqu&rsquo;&agrave; devenir insignifiant?   L&rsquo;h&eacute;ritage du Parti Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois semble &ecirc;tre une &eacute;galit&eacute; linguistique  n&rsquo;emp&ecirc;che officiel, plut&ocirc;t que l&rsquo;ind&eacute;pendance politique.<br /> J&rsquo;ai un tr&egrave;s grand souvenir de la nuit du 15 novembre,  1976 quand, &agrave; la surprise g&eacute;n&eacute;rale, Ren&eacute; L&eacute;vesque et son Parti  Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois sont pass&eacute; au pouvoir.  On dansait dans la rue Prince Arthur  comme partout dans la province.   Pour une d&eacute;cennie, il semblait que la  souverainet&eacute; du Qu&eacute;bec &eacute;tait possible.  Aujourd&rsquo;hui il semble peu  probable.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;                   Nous vivons une dr&ocirc;le de p&eacute;riode.  Le monde arabe vit  une p&eacute;riode bouleversante aux mains de mouvements d&eacute;mocratiques tandis  qu&rsquo;au Qu&eacute;bec, les Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois semblent contents avec le statu quo.  Ce  n&rsquo;est pas la peine de secouer les affaires, apr&egrave;s tout, C&eacute;line joue &agrave;  Vegas.</p> 2011-07-06 00:00:00
6 y <h3>Cinco de mayo</h3>
<p>First lightening-bugs of the season,<br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; their  little beams<br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; random  decoration</p>
<p>For the velvet curtain of  night.</p>
<p>Aux Ch&ecirc;nes du Marais</p>
<p><em>Summer   arrives at full gallop on the hooves of vapor.&nbsp; Squadron of clouds  swept from the Gulf of Mexico bringing  humidity and laziness.&nbsp; Colaspis   beatles have invaded the cypress in their annual festival of ruin.&nbsp; My  father in his apocalype suit  spraying the trees in a futile effort to  control the damage.&nbsp; The &laquo;&nbsp;love bugs&nbsp;&raquo; blacken the  walls of the shed  and block my nostrils.&nbsp;  In Cajun French they are called &laquo;&nbsp;besson&nbsp;&raquo;  which means &laquo;&nbsp;twin&nbsp;&raquo;.&nbsp; They are small, black and spend their  short  lives connected one to another by the ass.&nbsp; The pairs are mixed, male  and female.&nbsp; The females are larger and thus able to  haul the males,  who spend their lives being pulled by the butt by a woman.&nbsp; Sounds  familiar.&nbsp; (No sexisme intended, y&rsquo;all, just a  little Cajun humor.&nbsp;)</em></p> <h3>Cinco de mayo</h3>
<p>Premi&egrave;res lucioles de la saison,<br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; leurs &eacute;tincelles d&eacute;corent<br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; le velour de la nuit</p>
<p>Laissant des traces de lumi&egrave;re</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;  virevoltant autour.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p>aux Ch&ecirc;nes du Marais</p>
<p><em>L&rsquo;&eacute;t&eacute;  arrive au grand galop sur les sabots d&rsquo;une cavalerie de  vapeur.&nbsp;  Escadron de nuages venus  du Mexique emmenant l&rsquo;humidit&eacute; et la  paresse.&nbsp;&nbsp; Les mouches ont envahi les cypr&egrave;s.&nbsp; Mon p&egrave;re dans son armure  apocalyptique  arrose les arbres de poison pour les emp&ecirc;cher de chiquer  toutes les nouvelles  feuille.&nbsp; Les bessons noircissent  les murs de  l&rsquo;habitation, et bouchent mes narines.&nbsp; &ldquo;Besson&rdquo; en parler Cadien veut  dire jumeau, et c&rsquo;est le nom  qu&rsquo;on donne &agrave; ses insectes qui sortent  deux fois par an.&nbsp; Ils sont petits, noirs, et passent leur  courte vie  attach&eacute;s les uns aux autres par le cul.&nbsp; Le pair consiste d&rsquo;une femelle  et d&rsquo;un m&acirc;le.&nbsp; Les femelles sont plus grandes et tirent  les m&acirc;les, qui   passent leur vie &agrave; se faire tra&icirc;ner par l&rsquo;arri&egrave;re.</em></p> 2011-05-04 00:00:00
7 y <p>For two years now, the  Mississippi River Gulf  Outlet, MR. GO, has been closed.&nbsp;  The promised  restoration of the marsh, however, has yet to begin.&nbsp; This canal was  built in the 1960s in  order to give oceans going vessels access to New  Orleans without having to pass  in the river.&nbsp; The canal, which   displaced as much earth in its construction as that of the Panama canal,  was  well suited to this purpose.&nbsp; Not  only was it hardly used for its  intended purpose, but it was the most important  element in the  flooding of New Orleans during Hurricane Katrina.&nbsp; This canal served as a  funnel bringing  the tidal surge from Lake Borgne into the heart of the  city.&nbsp; The now infamous London Street and 17th  Street canals were  ultimately connected to MR. GO and the floodwaters that  burst their  levees arrived directly from that canal.</p>
<p>In  spite of the repeated protests of the leaders of Saint Bernard  Parish  (including the cities of Chalmette, Arabi, Mereaux and Violette,  all hard hit  during Katrina) and the Lake Ponchartrain Basin  Foundation and a large  proportion of the scientific community, the  Louisiana delegation to Congress  supported its construction.&nbsp; In   Louisiana, money doesn&rsquo;t talk, it screams.&nbsp; MR. GO&nbsp; is  directly  responsible for the loss through erosion of more than 20,000 acres in   Saint Bernard.&nbsp; It continues to  strangle the ecosystem of Lake  Ponchartrain.</p>
<p>Since  the  canal&rsquo;s closing in January 2009, the U.S. Corps of Engineers has been  given  the responsibility of improving the area along the canal and  restoring  thousands of acres destroyed vy salt water intrusion.&nbsp; The  actual plan is intended to create additional protection  against a  storm-serge like that which crossed Lake Borgne and wound up in New   Orleans in 2005.&nbsp; In order to  accomplish this, the marshes must be  re-opened to the river, allowing fresh  water to bring in sediment.&nbsp;   According to the plan, 55,000 acres should be restored.&nbsp; The plan is a  step in the right  direction, but should be reinforced with several  additional elements:</p>
<ol>
<li>Oyster  beds should be used  instead of rocks in the restoration. Oyster beds are a  cost-effective  solution that improve water quality and create habitat for a  wide  variety of species.</li>
<li>Fixi the  banks: Remediating and  narrowing MRGO's banks would slow down storm surges and  would help  restore the natural balance of salt and fresh water.</li>
<li>Use  sediment intelligently:  Adding sediment is an important part of restoring  marshes, but the  Corps should dredge carefully, fully assessing and fully  accounting for  the impacts on wildlife. Sediment already dredged from the river   should be used in the place of that taken from the already over-stressed   marshes.</li>
<li>Monitor  the system: In order to  assess the long term effects of the planned  modifications, the Corps  needs to increase its monitoring in the MRGO  ecosystem.&nbsp; Otherwise it  will be  impossible to accurately measure the impact of the restoration  project over  time.</li>
</ol>
<p>MR. GO is   the living symbol of what can go wrong in the marshlands of Southern   Louisiana.&nbsp; Since the 1930s,  engineering projects like the Mississippi  River levees and the oil exploration  canals have altered the landscape  beyond recognition.&nbsp; Together they are responsible for tremendous  coastal erosion  which continues to destroy the marshes at an alarming  rate of 50 square miles a  year (down from 80 in the 1980s).&nbsp;  This  erosion is the result of the intrusion of salt water in the marshes  in  combination with the strangle hold on the river which prevents sediments   from replenishing the marshes during the spring floods.&nbsp; One of the  major players in the  environmental catastrophe is the U.S. Corps of  Engineers. During it&rsquo;s entire  history, the Corps has been thinking  inside the box, building big things and  then bigger thing, higher and  wider and farther.&nbsp; The madness of this approach is revealed by the  history of  MR. GO and by coastal erosion itself.&nbsp;  The question now is  can this traditional and highly politicized  institution (consult the  monthly reports of August, September &amp; October  2006) actually  incorporate the long term interests of the community in its  project.&nbsp;  Will the Corps be able to  resolve as opposed to create long term  problems.&nbsp; Another question: does anybody care?&nbsp; As proved the Deepwater  Horizon spill,  unless directly touched by an environmental  catastrophe, does any one give a damn.&nbsp; But that&rsquo;s a whole other story. <a href="https://secure2.edf.org/site/Advocacy?cmd=display&amp;page=UserAction&amp;id=1789"></a></p>
<p><a href="https://secure2.edf.org/site/Advocacy?cmd=display&amp;page=UserAction&amp;id=1789">Sign the petition </a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mississippi_River_%E2%80%93_Gulf_Outlet_Canal"><br />MR. GO</a><a href="http://www.mrgo.gov/MRGO_History.aspx"><br />US Corps of Engineers </a></p> <p>Depuis deux ans, le Mississippi  River Gulf Outlet  (Mr. Go) est ferm&eacute;, mais les am&eacute;liorations promises ne sont  toujours  pas mis en place.&nbsp; Ce  canal fut construit dans les ann&eacute;es soixante pour  permettre acc&egrave;s au golfe du  Mexique par les grands navires de la  marine marchande, sans avoir &agrave; passer par  le fleuve.&nbsp; Pour cela &ccedil;a  marche  magnifiquement bien.&nbsp; Mais on ne  pouvait pas mieux faire pour  assurer l&rsquo;inondation de la ville en cas d&rsquo;un  raz-de-mar&eacute;e traversant le  Lac Borgne, ce qui &eacute;tait le cas pendant Katrina en  2005.&nbsp; Le MRGO a  servi d&rsquo;entonnoir,  emmenant un mur d&rsquo;eau directement au centre de la  ville de Nouvelle-Orl&eacute;ans  avec les cons&eacute;quences qu&rsquo;on conna&icirc;t.&nbsp;  La  d&eacute;l&eacute;gation louisianaise au Congr&egrave;s am&eacute;ricain a soutenu la  construction  de ce canal industriel contre les plaidoyers des dirigeants de la   Paroisse Saint Bernard (qui englobe les villes de Chalmette, Arabi,  Mereaux, et  Violette, toutes catastroph&eacute;es par l&rsquo;ouragan), et le Lake  Ponchartrain Basin  Foundation, ainsi que la communaut&eacute; scientifique. Le  canal est responsable de  la perte par &eacute;rosion de 20,000 acres de la  Paroisse St. Bernard.&nbsp; Il continue &agrave; &eacute;trangler l&rsquo;&eacute;cosyst&egrave;me du  Lac  Ponchartrain et est directement responsable de l&rsquo;inondation de la ville  de  Nouvelle-Orl&eacute;ans.</p>
<p>Depuis sa fermeture en janvier   2009, le Corps de G&eacute;nie (U.S. Corps of Engineers) est charg&eacute; d&rsquo;am&eacute;liorer  les  environs du canal avec comme but la restauration des milliers  d&rsquo;acres d&eacute;truit  par l&rsquo;intrusion d&rsquo;eau saline.&nbsp; Le  plan actuel devrait  cr&eacute;er une protection suppl&eacute;mentaire contre l&rsquo;inondation de  la ville de  Nouvelle-Orl&eacute;ans via le raz-de-mar&eacute;e sur Lac Borgne, qui &eacute;tait le  cas  pendant Katrina.&nbsp; Pour cela, le  fleuve doit &ecirc;tre rattach&eacute; aux  mar&eacute;cages, permettant l&rsquo;eau douce &agrave; p&eacute;n&eacute;trer dans  les &laquo;marshes&nbsp;&raquo; ce qui  apportera les alluvions qui contreront l&rsquo;&eacute;rosion  c&ocirc;ti&egrave;re. Et 55,000  acres d&rsquo;habitat naturel doivent &ecirc;tre restaur&eacute;.&nbsp; Le plan est un pas dans  la bonne  direction, mais devrait &ecirc;tre renforc&eacute; par plusieurs &eacute;l&eacute;ments   additionnels&nbsp;:</p>
<ol>
<li>Utiliser des  bancs d&rsquo;hu&icirc;tres &agrave;  la place de pierres pour la restauration.&nbsp; Les hu&icirc;tres pourront  am&eacute;liorer la  qualit&eacute; de l&rsquo;eau et contribuer &agrave; la cr&eacute;ation d&rsquo;habitat  pour plusieurs esp&egrave;ces.</li>
<li>Restaurer les rives du canal.&nbsp;  En renfor&ccedil;ant et diminuant les rives &agrave; l&rsquo;&eacute;troit, on pourra  ralentir la  force des raz-de-mar&eacute;e &eacute;ventuels.&nbsp; La balance naturelle d&rsquo;eau douce et  d&rsquo;eau sal&eacute;e b&eacute;n&eacute;ficiera  &eacute;galement.</li>
<li>Utiliser  tr&egrave;s soigneusement  le s&eacute;diment.&nbsp; Le  syst&egrave;me naturel des alluvions a &eacute;t&eacute; rendu hors service  par les projets de  g&eacute;nie.&nbsp;&nbsp; Donc ajoutant du  s&eacute;diment est un &eacute;l&eacute;ment  crucial &agrave; restaurer les mar&eacute;cages, mais le dragage doit  &ecirc;tre fait avec  un souci fondamental des impactes sur toutes les esp&egrave;ces de  faune.&nbsp; On  devrait utiliser le  s&eacute;diment qui est d&eacute;j&agrave; dragu&eacute; du fleuve plut&ocirc;t que  de draguer dans les  mar&eacute;cages.</li>
<li>Veiller sur  le syst&egrave;me.&nbsp; La  seule fa&ccedil;on  d&rsquo;assurer que les modifications apportent les effets  souhait&eacute;s est de  surveiller continuellement le syst&egrave;me.</li>
</ol>
<p>Le MR. GO est le symbole de tout  ce qui peut aller &agrave; la  d&eacute;rive dans les basses terres de la Louisiane.&nbsp;  Depuis les ann&eacute;es 1930, les projets de g&eacute;nie civil ainsi que   l&rsquo;exploration p&eacute;troli&egrave;re ont occasionn&eacute; des modifications au paysage qui  sont  responsables d&rsquo;une &eacute;rosion c&ocirc;ti&egrave;re d&rsquo;une dimension difficile &agrave;  concevoir.&nbsp; Plus de 80 kilom&egrave;tres carr&eacute;s du  littoral disparaissent &agrave;  chaque ann&eacute;e caus&eacute; par l&rsquo;intrusion d&rsquo;eau sal&eacute;e et  l&rsquo;absence des  alluvions dor&eacute;navant apport&eacute;s par les inondations  printani&egrave;res.&nbsp; Un des  grands  joueurs de cette catastrophe environnementale est le Corps de  G&eacute;nie.&nbsp; Pendant toute son histoire, le U.S.  Corps of Engineer a agi  d&rsquo;une fa&ccedil;on traditionnelle, c&rsquo;est &agrave; dire en  construisant toujours plus  haut, plus fort et plus loin.&nbsp; La d&eacute;faillance de ce mode de pens&eacute;e est   prouv&eacute;e par la catastrophe du MR. GO et par l&rsquo;&eacute;rosion c&ocirc;ti&egrave;re.&nbsp; La  question qu&rsquo;on se pose est si cette  institution traditionnelle et  hautement politis&eacute;e (rapports ao&ucirc;t, septembre,  octobre 2006), est en  mesure, enfin, de pouvoir servir les int&eacute;r&ecirc;ts long terme  de la  communaut&eacute; louisianaise et d&rsquo;appliquer des projets qui vont r&eacute;soudre   plut&ocirc;t que de cr&eacute;er des probl&egrave;mes.&nbsp;  Autre question &agrave; se poser&nbsp;: est-ce  qu&rsquo;il y a des gens qui sont  concern&eacute;s.&nbsp; Comme l&rsquo;a prouv&eacute; la   catastrophe du Deepwater Horizon, hormis qu&rsquo;on est directement touch&eacute;  par une  catastrophe &eacute;cologique, on a souvent rien &agrave; foutre.&nbsp;</p>
<p><a href="https://secure2.edf.org/site/Advocacy?cmd=display&amp;page=UserAction&amp;id=1789">Signer la p&eacute;tition </a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mississippi_River_%E2%80%93_Gulf_Outlet_Canal"><br />MR. GO</a><a href="http://www.mrgo.gov/MRGO_History.aspx"><br />US Corps of Engineers </a></p> 2011-03-02 00:00:00
8 y <p>Chers amis, To you all, my very best wishes for a new year filled with  love and happiness.&nbsp; There are times when life poses great challenges.  These are times to reflect and renew. As says the IChing (hexagram 3):  for those climbing from the pit of adversity, determination to follow  the righteous course promises great success. I am faced with perhaps the  greatest challenge of my life, and nothing can be taken for granted. &nbsp; I  resolved to stay engaged and to do my best to spread beauty in this  world.&nbsp; In the words of my eleven year old grandson, &Eacute;mile, sometimes I  am deeply touched when I think of life.&nbsp;&nbsp; All the best in the new year.&nbsp;  Keep moving ahead.</p> <p>Chers amis, je voudrais vous souhaiter &agrave; tous et &agrave; toutes une nouvelle  ann&eacute;e remplie d'amour et de bonheur.&nbsp;&nbsp; Il y a des fois que la vie nous  rappelle &agrave; l'ordre en nous posant des grands d&eacute;fis.&nbsp;Comme dit le I Ching  (3e hexagram):&nbsp; pour ceux qui grimpe du bas fond de l'adversit&eacute;, la  d&eacute;termination de suivre le juste chemin promet grand succ&egrave;s.  J'ai&nbsp; la  grande chance dans cette nouvelle ann&eacute;e de pouvoir m'adresser aux  questions les plus essentielles.&nbsp; Je vais rester engag&eacute; et travailler  fort pour r&eacute;pandre le plus de beaut&eacute; dans ce monde &nbsp;Comme le dit mon  petit fils, &Eacute;mile, il y a des fois que je suis &eacute;mu en pensant &agrave; la vie.&nbsp;  N'arr&ecirc;tons pas d'avancer.</p> 2011-01-02 00:00:00
9 y <p><strong>Holy Martin&nbsp; (for Martin Billeaud)</strong></p>
<p>You are bending willow, Martin,<br /> You are porous in flow.</p>
<p>You know you are crazy,<br /> The stain of stigmata<br /> On your glove.</p>
<p>You say&nbsp;: &laquo;&nbsp;Go to the mountains,<br /> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The spirits will provide,"<br /> And you move like lizard,<br /> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Resemblance of reptile,<br /> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Breathing water and air.</p>
<p>You are shark in the ether, Martin,<br /> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Sky mantra ocean hawk,<br /> Your vision is clear at great distance.</p>
<p>You are chasm sailor, Martin,<br /> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Rope walker between spectrums,<br /> You cannot tell me about the edge<br /> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Of the world,<br /> You cannot touch the prophet's glory<br /> Because it is false.</p>
<p>And so, you will be found<br /> Asleep in some farmer's empty field,<br /> Prone near some drainage<br /> By children past return.</p>
<p>They will approach you cautiously,<br /> Whispering and awed.<br /> They will poke your shoulder with twigs,<br /> Then their toes.<br /> You will roll over <br /> And they will run home.</p>
<p>Holy Martin<br /> Holy Swallow<br /> Holy Sparrow<br /> Holy Hawk</p> <p><strong>Trois corbeaux</strong><br /> <br /></p>
<p>Trois corbeaux revenus,<br /> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; pos&eacute;s dans l&rsquo;orme d&eacute;nud&eacute;<br /> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; de cette fin d&rsquo;hiver.</p>
<p>Le calme perc&eacute;<br /> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; par leurs cris.</p>
<p>Ils &eacute;taient l&agrave; quand je me suis lev&eacute;,  faisant un gros frolic, volant autour de l&rdquo;arbre avant de se poser.&nbsp;  Plus tard, Ils restaient tranquilles, comme des paquets de linge sale  attach&eacute;s aux branches.&nbsp; &Agrave; la fin de l&rsquo;apr&egrave;s midi, ils sont partis avec  les nuages.<br /> <br /> 7 mars, 2001.&nbsp; Outre le Mont.</p> 2010-12-01 00:00:00
10 y <p>Last Saturday, my little hometown held an  election.&nbsp; Up for grabs was the mayor&rsquo;s office and several municipal  counselors.&nbsp; Of the three candidates, two were black.&nbsp; The best known of  the three is a black man who has been involved in local politics,  representing his neighborhood, for decades.&nbsp; The other candidates were  his cousin, likewise black and the owner of a local night club, a white  man.</p>
<p>According to rumor, the cousin in  question presented himself for the office just to spite his better known  and more successful relative.&nbsp; The bar owner ran because he believed  that he had an overwhelming advantage simply because he was white.&nbsp;  Logical.&nbsp; In my little town the vestiges of our racist past are present  and prevalent.&nbsp; We can no longer celebrate our racism like we did in the  good old days, but you would have to have your head way up your ass to  believe that racism no longer exists in Scott, Louisiana.&nbsp; Therefore, it  seemed to me and to most of my constituents, that the campaign strategy  of the white man bar owner who has absolutely no political experience,  was based on a good understanding of the social situation.</p>
<p>I believed that the race would be  close and I admitted the possibility of the defeat of the black  candidate who appeared to me also to be the best qualified.&nbsp; We have  never had a black mayor in my little town and it didn&rsquo;t seem to me that  this was going to change easily.&nbsp; Imagine my surprise to see the black  candidate win by an overwhelming majority, more than 60%.&nbsp; His rival  cousin did not receive but a few votes and the white man bar owner wound  up with less that 30% of the vote, which corresponded to the members of  his family, give or take a few.</p>
<p>I was more satisfied with this  election that with the election of Obama, because this time it happened  in my front yard.&nbsp; A few days after the election, I ran into one of my  cousins at the bank.&nbsp; This cousin of mine is a simple fellow, working  class, with all of its qualities and faults.&nbsp; He has never refrained  from telling my racist jokes and I think his attitude is very typical of  a certain part of the local population, maybe even the majority of  folks.&nbsp; On top of that, he is a close friend of the white candidate.&nbsp; I  mentioned that I was very surprised by the margin of victory that the  black candidate was able to obtain.&nbsp; I don&rsquo;t know for sure, but I would  guess that the African-american population of my town is about 10% or  less.&nbsp;</p>
<p>&ldquo;It&rsquo;s over,&rdquo; said my cousin, &ldquo;It&rsquo;s  completely over this business of &ldquo;race card&rdquo;.&nbsp; We have a black  president.&nbsp;&nbsp; The governor of Louisiana is a Hinud.&nbsp; No, it&rsquo;s completely  over.&rdquo;</p>
<p>I left him and walked out into the  bright sun, squinting my eyes and shaking my head, asking myself if  indeed this could be true.</p> <p>Samedi pass&eacute; dans mon petit village nous avons eu  une &eacute;lection.&nbsp; &Agrave; &eacute;lire&nbsp;: le maire ainsi que quelques conseillers  municipaux.&nbsp; Sur les trois candidats &agrave; la mairie, deux ont &eacute;t&eacute; noirs.&nbsp;  Le plus connu des candidats travaille dans le domaine de la politique  depuis plusieurs ann&eacute;es comme conseiller municipal repr&eacute;sentant le  quartier Afro Louisianais.&nbsp; Ses deux adversaires ont &eacute;t&eacute; son cousin,  &eacute;galement noir, et le tenancier d&rsquo;un bar local, qui lui est blanc.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Selon la rumeur, le cousin en question s&rsquo;est  pr&eacute;sent&eacute; par jalousie.&nbsp; Le tenancier de bar s&rsquo;est pr&eacute;sent&eacute; en pensant  qu&rsquo;il serait &eacute;lu du simple fait d&rsquo;&ecirc;tre blanc.&nbsp; Logique.&nbsp; Dans mon petit  village, les vestiges de l&rsquo;h&eacute;ritage raciste sont assez pr&eacute;sents.&nbsp;  &Eacute;videmment on est oblig&eacute; de dissimuler ce dont on aurait pu c&eacute;l&eacute;brer  ouvertement il y a quelques dec&eacute;nies, mais il serait t&ecirc;te-dans-le-cul de  pr&eacute;tendre que le racisme n&rsquo;existe plus.&nbsp; Alors le pari du blanc,  tenancier de bar, sans aucune exp&eacute;rience politique et aucune qualit&eacute;  apparente &agrave; part la couleur de sa peau, n&rsquo;&eacute;tait pas fantaisiste.&nbsp;</p>
<p>J&rsquo;imaginais que l&nbsp;&lsquo;&eacute;lection allait &ecirc;tre fort  serr&eacute; et je pr&eacute;voyais la d&eacute;faite du candidat noir bien qu&rsquo;il me semblait  &ecirc;tre le plus qualifi&eacute;.&nbsp; Nous n&rsquo;avons jamais eu un maire noir dans mon  village, et je ne pensais pas que cet h&eacute;ritage lourd allait se faire  renverser facilement.&nbsp; Imaginez donc ma surprise de voir le candidat  noir emporter la victoire avec une majorit&eacute; &eacute;crasante, plus de 60%.&nbsp; Son  cousin rival n&rsquo;a re&ccedil;u que quelques voix et le blanc tenancier de bar a  re&ccedil;u moins de 30% ce qui correspond &agrave; peu pr&egrave;s aux membres de sa  famille.&nbsp;</p>
<p>J&rsquo;ai &eacute;t&eacute; tr&egrave;s satisfait de cette &eacute;lection,  peut&ndash;&ecirc;tre encore plus que l&rsquo;&eacute;lection du pr&eacute;sident Obama, car cette fois  ci, &ccedil;a se passait dans ma cour.&nbsp; Quelques jours apr&egrave;s l&rsquo;&eacute;lection j&rsquo;ai  rencontr&eacute; un de mes cousins &agrave; la banque.&nbsp; Le cousin en question est un  homme simple, classe ouvri&egrave;re, avec les qualit&eacute;s et les d&eacute;fauts de sa  culture.&nbsp; Il ne s&rsquo;est jamais retenu de me raconter des blagues tendance  raciste.&nbsp; En plus il est copain du candidat blanc d&eacute;chu.&nbsp; Je lui ai  parl&eacute; de ma surprise par rapport &agrave; la majorit&eacute; &eacute;crasante que les  &eacute;lecteurs ont donn&eacute; au candidat noir.&nbsp; Je n&rsquo;ai pas de chiffres exactes,  mais il me semble que la population noire de mon village est en dessous  de 10%.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&laquo;&nbsp;C&rsquo;est fini&nbsp;&raquo; m&rsquo;a r&eacute;pondu mon cousin, &laquo;&nbsp;c&rsquo;est  compl&egrave;tement fini cette histoire de &laquo;&nbsp;race card&nbsp;&raquo;.&nbsp; On a un pr&eacute;sident  noir, le gouverneur de la Louisiane est Hindu.&nbsp; Non, c&rsquo;est fini cette  histoire.&nbsp;&raquo;</p>
<p>En le quittant je me suis secou&eacute; la t&ecirc;te en me&nbsp; demandant si c&rsquo;&eacute;tait bien vrai.&nbsp;</p> 2010-10-15 00:00:00
91 y <p>Lots to report this month. First of all on the Canadian prairies,  farmers are organizing to resist the imposition of genetically modified  wheat (Monsanto Round-up ready wheat). A heated conflict is brewing. The  multi-national chemical giant hopes to commercialize its OGM to go  along with its herbicide. As soon as one field is planted in &ldquo;Round-up  ready wheat&rdquo;, the entire Canadian prairie will be exposed as the pollen  is carried by the wind. Canadian farmers have already witnessed the  collapse of their market for canola. They fear, with reason, that the  same thing will happen to their market for wheat. The Canadian  government is caught in the middle. It has already permitted experiments  by Montsanto with OGM wheat at its agricultural facility. These tests  were done in secret but were halted when a scientist blew the whistle on  what could have been a disaster for the seed stock of Canadian red  wheat. The tests could have polluted the source of Canadian seed through  cross pollination. The Canadian farmers are against the introduction of  OGM wheat by an overwhelming majority. They are hardly what could be  called hard core environmentalists of the Jos&eacute; Bov&eacute; stripe. They are  however convinced that the introduction of OGM wheat could mean the end  of the Canadian wheat industry. France, Germany and Japan refuse  categorically the importation of any genetically modified agricultural  product. In contrast to the questionable policies of the U.S. and  Canada, those countries will allow their citizens to make the choice as  to whether they wish to consume genetically modified food products. The  governments of both the U.S. and Canada do not require any product  labeling of genetically modified foods, and thus prevent their citizens  from obtaining any knowledge of whether the food stuffs they consume has  been genetically modified or not. The recent rash of problems (allergic  reactions varying from the mild to life threatening) with &ldquo;Star-Corn&rdquo;  and OGM canola have not altered the policy. The introduction of OGM  wheat in Canada would result in the loss to Canadian farmers of their  primary markets and perhaps the end of the family farm. This would not  be contrary to the interests of Monsanto since its products are adapted  to industrial agriculture. The family farmer is largely unable to afford  the products which, in the case of &ldquo;Round-up ready wheat&rdquo; would  quadruple the per acre cost of cultivation. It remains to be seen  whether the government of Canada will defend the interests of its  citizens or cave in to the pressure of a multi-national giant.</p>
<p>While the farmers of the western prairie were  organizing to resist Monsanto, in Qu&eacute;bec, the new Liberal government of  Jean Charest was in the process of redefining the relationship between  Qu&eacute;bec and the Canadian confederation and thus redefining the Canadian  confederation itself in the process. The government of Jean Charest  proposes ceding significant provincial control in exchange of a larger  share to the federal pie. This political horse trade would include areas  of municipal control, here to fore the province of the provinces.  Qu&eacute;bec would lose its exceptional status within the Canadian  confederation, no longer to be considered a &ldquo;distinct society&rdquo;. In  exchange of which, the federal government would increase its subsidy. My  question is whether the political privilege which Qu&eacute;bec would  relinquish in the deal would be returned if ever the Canadian government  decided to reduce the subsidy in the future?</p>
<p>While these developments were developing, I joined the  Michot Brothers (Les Fr&egrave;res Michot) for their first Qu&eacute;becois tour. I  had the pleasure of producing their first album (&Eacute;lev&eacute;s &agrave; Pillette) ten  years ago and I was very happy to join the band (playing triangle) for a  few days. They played at St. Romuald near Qu&eacute;bec City and then farther  up the Saint Laurence at Tadoussac. While on the North Shore, we were  able to get in an afternoon of whale watching. At this time of the year,  the whales are migrating south. At a spot where the waters of the  Saguenay enter the Saint Laurence, a whirlpool of currents keeps  crustaceans and small fish trapped. It was there that we were able to  spot a herd of Minke Whales, rolling in the waves, the sound of their  spouts squealing in the chilly air.</p>
<p>The Michot Brothers are fairly representative of the  linguistic reality of the Cajun community. Rick and Tommy, the oldest  brothers, in spite of an ability to communicate in French, are none the  less primarily anglophone. Their grasp of French is conversational and  with a little practice could become very polished. The lack of practice,  however, restrains their ability to be at ease with the language and  although our conversations would often begin in French, there came a  point at which the inability to communicate nuance would deroute the  conversation and at that point we would begin speaking in English. The  youngest brother, David, was even more awkward in his attempts to speak  French although his pleasure in making the effort was apparent. The two  other members of the band are Tommy&rsquo;s sons, Louis and Andr&eacute;, both in  their twenties. Of all of the Fr&egrave;res Michot, Louis is the most fluent in  French, thanks to his Qu&eacute;b&eacute;coise wife. During our few days together, I  did not hear Andr&eacute; speak French. The language question aside, we had a  great time, reminiscing about the old days, as old friends tend to do.  The pleasure that I had in their company had a surprising effect on me.  It may seem very obvious, but in the context of my never ending search  for the essence of my anglo-franco-american-Cadien identity, the fact  that I identified more strongly with the primarily English speaking  Cajuns (the Michots) while being smack dab in the middle of a  monolingual French speakers (les Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois) with whom I feel great  solidarity, brought home to me the fact that language is only one  (although the most important) element of the composition of ethnic  identity. Of my generation of Cajuns, the French language is spoken only  by a select few. For the majority of my Cajun peers, the French  language has become an element of folklore. Our sharing of culture does  not rely on language, but on common experience and a wealth of reference  which goes beyond language. By the same token, even though I would  associate the notion of &ldquo;Cadien-Cajun&rdquo; with fluency in French, I am  certainly closer to the Cajuns of my generation (primarily anglophone),  than to the Cajuns of the previous generations (primarily francophone).  Belonging to the same generation would therefore seem more important  than speaking the same language when it comes to defining the group with  whom one shares a notion of group identity........ Interesting.</p>
<p>While I was pondering the depths of my identity  alongside the Fr&egrave;res Michot (accompanied by some hard core fans, the  Fr&egrave;res Heads, or Freds as referred to on the road), on the other side of  the Atlantic, research of another type was being held on the question  of linguistic identity. On October 4, the Minister of Culture of France  organized &laquo; Les Assises nationales des langues de France &raquo;, a conference  on the state of &ldquo;regional languages&rdquo;. Between 1989 and 2002, the number  of students studying in regional languages has increased ten fold. The  organization of the conference was designed to promote the idea that the  French government is not hostile to regional languages. The minister of  Culture is in fact mandated to &ldquo;preserve&rdquo; and &ldquo;valorize&rdquo; the &ldquo;languages  of France&rdquo;. &ldquo;Regional languages are the expression of cultural  diversity of which our country prides itself&rdquo;, explained the minister,  Jean-Jacques Aillagon. The conference had an evidently political  dimension: by organizing the conference, the government of Jacques  Chirac could retake the offensive in regards to the proponents of  regional language. In June of 1999, Chirac greatly disappointed the  partisans of regionalanguage by refusing to modify the constitution,  which is necessary if France is to ratify the European Convention on  Regional and Minority Languages.</p>
<p>Confronting the language question under the banner of  culture has the additional advantage of defusing some of the emotional  rhetoric which has characterized the debate. During the last two years,  the debate has focused on the integration of regional languages into the  public sector and into the public schools.<br /> In 2002, according to the Minister of Education of  France, nearly 250,000 students were being schooled in a minority  regional language. The progression is spectacular: in 1989 there were  only 27,000 students learning in a regional language in all of the  public and private schools in France.</p>
<p>There are significant differences between the regions.  The regional language with the greatest number of students is Alsatian  with 55,200 elementary students, 26,700 middle school students and 1,200  high school students. This success is due in part to the fact that  Alsatian is associated with the learning of German, a language skill  which is particularly helpful in the east of France. Other than  Alsatian, the regional language of France with the most students is  Occitan. Spoken in 30 of the 60 departments (states) of France,  schooling in Occitan regroups 48,400 primary students, 15,500 middle  school students and 3,700 high school students. An additional 1,800  students are schooled bilingually. In Corsica, teaching in the native  language continues to grow with 21,400 primary students, 7,400 middle  school students and 2,000 high school students. Breton (Gaelic) is the  regional language with the least students with 9,200 primary students,  6,400 middle school students and 1,000 high school students. The number  of students being taught in Breton is stagnant.</p>
<p>What strikes me about all of this is that in France  there exists the political will to support minority languages. The  argument is simple: since France promotes cultural diversity in the  world, it is only logical to do so at home. &ldquo;These languages are the  expression of the diversity of culture which is the pride of our  country&rdquo;, explains the Cultural Minister. I can only regret that this  point of view is inconceivable in my own country. In the good ole USofA,  the openness associated with cultural diversity is impossible to  imagine. Unfortunately (for us Americans) the political climate is  characterized by the opposite: a mistrust of other cultures and a close  minded attitude bordering on the xenophobic. American culture refuses to  acknowledge the value of any other linguistic culture other than  anglo-americain, even in the case of a linguistic culture which is part  of the American experience, such as Cadien French. This chauvinistic  vision of culture has resulted in our isolation from the rest of the  world.</p> <p>Beaucoup  de d&eacute;veloppements ce mois-ci. D&rsquo;abord au Canada, les fermiers  des  prairies s&nbsp;organisent pour r&eacute;sister l&rsquo;imposition du bl&eacute; OGM  (Round-up  ready wheat). Un bras de fer s&rsquo;annonce entre eux et le  multi-national  Monsanto. Monsanto d&eacute;sire commercialiser son bl&eacute; OGM.  D&egrave;s qu&rsquo;un seul  champ est plant&eacute; avec cette semence, toute la prairie  canadienne sera  infest&eacute;e, les graines de pollen des OGM transport&eacute;es  par le vent. Les  fermiers canadiens ont vu leur march&eacute; de canola  s&rsquo;effondrer. La France,  l&rsquo;Allemagne et le Japon refusent d&rsquo;accepter un  produit contenant les  OGM, et les fermiers canadiens craignent, avec  raison, que  l&rsquo;introduction du bl&eacute; OGM provoquera l&rsquo;effondrement de ces  march&eacute;s. Le  gouvernement canadien est pris entre le fer et le feu. Il a  conspir&eacute;  avec Monsanto, permettant des exp&eacute;riences OGM au site  d&rsquo;exp&eacute;rimentation  agricole f&eacute;d&eacute;rale, et cela en secret. Maintenant ces  exp&eacute;riences sont  arr&ecirc;t&eacute;es. Les fermiers canadiens, loin de l&rsquo;engagement  &eacute;cologiste style  Jos&eacute; Bov&eacute;, sont n&eacute;anmoins contre l&rsquo;introduction du  bl&eacute; OGM. Ils  craignent d&rsquo;&ecirc;tre entra&icirc;n&eacute;s vers la faillite si le bl&eacute; OGM  est  introduit. Ce qui fera l&rsquo;affaire de Montsanto, car leurs produits  sont  destin&eacute;s &agrave; la monoculture industrielle et sont trop co&ucirc;teux pour  les  fermes familiales. Il reste &agrave; voir si le gouvernement canadien   soutiendra ces citoyens ou bien va baisser les bras devant le pouvoir   d&rsquo;une multi-nationale am&eacute;ricaine.<br /> <br /> Pendant que les  fermiers de l&rsquo;Ouest s&rsquo;organisent pour  r&eacute;sister &agrave; Monsanto, au Qu&eacute;bec,  le nouveau gouvernement lib&eacute;ral est en  train de red&eacute;finir la relation  entre le Qu&eacute;bec et le Canada. En effet,  le gouvernement de Jean Charest  propose de c&eacute;der certains pouvoirs  provinciaux en &eacute;change d&rsquo;une  augmentation de la subvention f&eacute;d&eacute;rale. Y  compris dans le domaine des  affaires municipales. Le Qu&eacute;bec perdra  quelques aspects de son statut  exceptionnel pour une plus grande part  de la tarte. Mais si la part de  la tarte est r&eacute;duite &agrave; l&rsquo;avenir, est-ce  que les pouvoirs c&eacute;d&eacute;s seront  remis au Qu&eacute;bec?<br /> <br /> Pendant  que tous ses d&eacute;veloppements bouleversaient le  monde, je suis parti en  tourn&eacute;e avec mes amis les Fr&egrave;res Michot. Ce  groupe louisianais faisait  sa premi&egrave;re tourn&eacute;e qu&eacute;b&eacute;coise. J&rsquo;ai eu le  plaisir de r&eacute;aliser leur  premier album (&Eacute;lev&eacute;s &agrave; Pillette) et j&rsquo;&eacute;tais  tr&egrave;s heureux de les  accompagner pour quelques jours. Ils ont jou&eacute; &agrave; St.  Romuald, &agrave; c&ocirc;t&eacute; de  Qu&eacute;bec, et ensuite &agrave; Tadoussac. Nous avons profit&eacute;  de notre visite sur  la C&ocirc;te Nord pour une exp&eacute;dition sur le fleuve &agrave; la  recherche de  baleines. En ce moment les baleines sont en migration, et  nous avons pu  observer un grand nombre de Petit Rorquals (qui ne sont  pas petits du  tout). Les Fr&egrave;res Michot sont assez repr&eacute;sentatifs de la  communaut&eacute;  cadienne du point de vue linguistique. Rick et Tommy, les  plus vieux,  sont capables de se faire comprendre en fran&ccedil;ais, mais ils  sont,  cependant, plut&ocirc;t anglophone. Nos conversations commen&ccedil;aient  toujours  en fran&ccedil;ais, mais &agrave; moment donn&eacute;, faute de pouvoir s&rsquo;exprimer   facilement, nous finissons par parler en anglais. Le plus jeune des   fr&egrave;res, David, est encore moins &agrave; l&rsquo;aise fran&ccedil;ais. Les deux autres   membres du groupe, Louis et Andr&eacute;, sont les fils de Tommy. Dans leur   vingtaine, Louis parle tr&egrave;s bien le fran&ccedil;ais, le mieux de tous, gr&acirc;ce &agrave;   sa femme qu&eacute;b&eacute;coise, mais Andr&eacute; ne parle pas le fran&ccedil;ais du tout. La   question de la langue mise &agrave; part, nous avons eu un bon temps, et   c&rsquo;&eacute;tait pour moi une r&eacute;v&eacute;lation. Depuis longtemps je r&eacute;fl&eacute;chis &agrave; la   nature de mon identit&eacute; am&eacute;ricano-franco-anglo-Cadien, et l&rsquo;importance   de la langue comme &eacute;l&eacute;ment d&eacute;terminant d&rsquo;identit&eacute;. Bien qu&rsquo;il soit vrai   que l&rsquo;aspect fondamental de la culture cadienne est la langue   fran&ccedil;aise, il est aussi vrai que notre identit&eacute; n&rsquo;est pas uniquement   d&eacute;fini par la langue. Il para&icirc;t tr&egrave;s &eacute;vident ce que je dis ici, mais   pour moi cette rencontre poussait ma r&eacute;flexion encore plus loin, du   fait de me trouver en compagnie de louisianais plut&ocirc;t anglophone dans   un milieu francophone au Qu&eacute;bec. Je me sentais plus proche de mes amis   louisianais. Le fait d&rsquo;appartenir &agrave; la m&ecirc;me g&eacute;n&eacute;ration est plus   important que la capacit&eacute; de parler la langue pour ce qui est du   sentiment d&rsquo;appartenance. Int&eacute;ressant.<br /> <br /> Pendant que je  r&eacute;fl&eacute;chissais &agrave; ces questions  identitaires sur les bords du fleuve  Saint Laurent, une autre r&eacute;flexion  se poursuivait de l&rsquo;autre c&ocirc;t&eacute; de  l&rsquo;Atlantique.<br /> Le 4 octobre, le ministre de la culture de la R&eacute;publique  Fran&ccedil;aise a  organis&eacute; &laquo;&nbsp;Les Assises nationales des langues de France&nbsp;&raquo;.  Entre 1989  et 2002, le nombre d&rsquo;&eacute;l&egrave;ves qui suivent ces enseignements a  &eacute;t&eacute;  multipli&eacute; par dix. L&rsquo;organisation de cette conf&eacute;rence est destin&eacute;e  &agrave;  promouvoir l&rsquo;id&eacute;e que l&rsquo;&eacute;tat central n&rsquo;est pas l&rsquo;ennemi des langues   r&eacute;gionales. Le ministre de la culture a en charge la &laquo;&nbsp;pr&eacute;servation&nbsp;&raquo;   et la &laquo;&nbsp;valorisation&nbsp;&raquo; des &laquo;&nbsp;langues de France&nbsp;&raquo;. &laquo;&nbsp;Ces langues sont   l&rsquo;expression de la diversit&eacute; culturelle dont notre pays   s&rsquo;enorgueillit&nbsp;&raquo;, explique le ministre Jean-Jacques Aillagon.   L&rsquo;ensemble comprend &eacute;videmment une dimension politique&nbsp;: l&rsquo;organisation   de ces Assises permet au gouvernement de Jacques Chirac de reprendre   l&rsquo;offensive en direction des partisans des langues r&eacute;gionales. En juin,   1999, Chirac avait d&eacute;&ccedil;u ces derniers en refusant de modifier la   Constitution de la R&eacute;publique, d&eacute;marche indispensable pour permettre &agrave;   la France de ratifier la Convention europ&eacute;enne des langues r&eacute;gionales   et minoritaires. <br /> <br /> L&rsquo;approche par la culture pr&eacute;sente un second avantage  pour le  gouvernement fran&ccedil;ais&nbsp;: elle est cens&eacute;e limiter la dimension   passionnelle du d&eacute;bat. Ces deux derni&egrave;res ann&eacute;es, les pol&eacute;miques se   sont focalis&eacute;es sur l&rsquo;int&eacute;gration ou non dans le service public et dans   les &eacute;coles proposant un enseignement int&eacute;gral en langues r&eacute;gionales. En   2002, selon les statistiques du minist&egrave;re de l&rsquo;&eacute;ducation nationale,   environ 250,000 &eacute;l&egrave;ves ont suivi ce type d&rsquo;enseignement. La progression   est spectaculaire&nbsp;: en 1989, on comptait seulement 27,000&eacute;l&egrave;ves dans la   totalit&eacute; des &eacute;tablissements publics et priv&eacute;s. <br /> <br /> Il y a des diff&eacute;rences assez grandes entre les r&eacute;gions.  La r&eacute;gion avec  le plus d&rsquo;enseignement de la langue r&eacute;gionale est  l&rsquo;Alsace avec quelque  55,200 &eacute;l&egrave;ves du primaire, 26,700 coll&eacute;giens et  1,200 lyc&eacute;ens initi&eacute;s.  Ce succ&egrave;s est d&ucirc; en partie au fait que  l&rsquo;Alsacien s&rsquo;associe &agrave;  l&rsquo;apprentissage de l&rsquo;allemand. En dehors de ce  cas particulier de  l&rsquo;alsacien, l&rsquo;occitan reste la langue r&eacute;gionale la  plus enseign&eacute;e. <br /> <br /> Parl&eacute;e dans trente d&eacute;partements, elle rassemble 48,400  &eacute;l&egrave;ves du  primaire, 15,500 coll&eacute;giens et 3,700 lyc&eacute;ens. Environ 1,800  &eacute;l&egrave;ves  suivent des cours bilingues. En Corse, l&rsquo;enseignement de la  langue  continue de se d&eacute;velopper. La derni&egrave;re estimation fait &eacute;tat de  21,400  &eacute;l&egrave;ves du primaire, 7,400 coll&eacute;giens, et 2,000 lyc&eacute;ens. Le  breton est  la derni&egrave;re des quatre grandes langues r&eacute;gionales enseign&eacute;es  en  m&eacute;tropole. Avec 9&nbsp;200&nbsp;&eacute;l&egrave;ves au primaire, 6&nbsp;400 au coll&egrave;ge, 1&nbsp;000  au  lyc&eacute;e, selon les statistiques du minist&egrave;re, le nombre d'&eacute;l&egrave;ves  stagne.<br /> <br /> Ce que je voudrais signaler c&rsquo;est qu&rsquo;en France, il  existe une volont&eacute;  politique de soutenir les langues secondes.  L'argumentaire est simple&nbsp;:  puisque la France d&eacute;fend la diversit&eacute; dans  le monde, elle doit  &eacute;galement la promouvoir &agrave; l'int&eacute;rieur de ses  fronti&egrave;res. "Ces langues  sont l'expression de la diversit&eacute; culturelle  dont notre pays  s'enorgueillit", explique le minist&egrave;re dans son  introduction au d&eacute;bat.  Je ne peux que me lamenter du fait que ce point  de vue est inconcevable  dans mon pays. Aux USA l&rsquo;ouverture d&rsquo;esprit qui  est &agrave; la base d&rsquo;une  politique de diversit&eacute; est absente.  Malheureusement (pour nous les  Am&eacute;ricains) le climat politique est  caract&eacute;ris&eacute; par le contraire&nbsp;: une  m&eacute;fiance des autres cultures et un  refus d&rsquo;ouverture envers le monde,  m&ecirc;me si ce monde comprend des  ethnies comme les Cadiens qui vivent sur  le territoire et cela depuis  bien avant que le territoire soit devenu  am&eacute;ricain. La vision chauvine  de notre politique internationale et  notre isolement de la communaut&eacute;  des nations en est la cons&eacute;quence.</p> 2003-11-05 00:00:00
92 y <p>Near the Porte d' Orl&eacute;ans on the south side of Paris France is a  peaceful corner, hidden away. The Parc Montsouris is a refuge for birds  and joggers and young mothers with their babies. The site upon which the  park was built was called &ldquo;Moquesouris&rdquo; because of the mice which  inhabited the abandoned windmills thereon. In the great upheaval of  urban renewal performed by the Baron Haussmann in the mid19th century,  four parks were created at the four cardinal points of the city:</p>
<p>in the North, les Buttes de Chaumont, in the East, le  bois de Vincennes, in the West, le bois de Boulogne and in the South, le  Parc Montsouris. Montsouris is the smallest and the most charming of  them all.</p>
<p>Upon entering from the North via Avenue Ren&eacute; Coty, one  arrives at a stone column upon which stands a statue of winged victory.  Behind the column stretches a large lawn surrounded by trees. There are  over 1400 trees in the park, many of which are over 100 years old: a  Virginia poplar, Lebanese cedar, Siberian elms, Ginko Biloba. There are  several species native to my home state: Bald Cypress and Sweetgum. Upon  entering the park,there are three ways to go, left, right and straight  ahead. The center path plunges into the heart of the park, amongst the  baby carriages, and the benches filled with groups of old men and  whispering lovers. To the right is rue Nansouty with its small stone  houses. Following the path to the top of the hill, one arrives at the  meteorological station and the southern boundary of the park. Continuing  on the path, one descends the hill following the eastern edge of the  park and comes upon the lake, the favorite spot for exotic water fowl  and preschool children (Jungle Gym, Merry-Go-Round). Just before the  lake, hidden on a small knoll under the pines, is a small monument to  the memory of Pierre Durand, killed, like so many young people in Paris,  in the month of August, 1940. Paris is filled with markers such as this  one, on nearly every street, in every neighborhood, one can find a  small plaque discreetly bearing witness to the death of a resistance  fighter during the liberation of &ldquo;Paname&rdquo;.</p>
<p>Last March during the anti-French hysteria which  gripped the USA like an rabies attack, I witnessed an interview on  national television which shocked and saddened me. On the Late Show,  Paul Schaeffer was filling in for David Letterman and he interviewed  Senator Bob Dole. French bashing was the order of the day. What was so  profoundly distressing to me was the cheap demagoguery to which both  Schaeffer and Dole fell prey. Paul Schaeffer is better off sticking to  his keyboard, his over exuberant witless remarks a foil for Letterman.  He was clearly out of his element. The ex-Senator, ex-Presidential  candidate, however, made a pitiful spectacle of himself. A political  figure should conduct himself with a little more class, it seems to me,  and particularly a WWII veteran, but Bob Dole was clearly playing to the  basest sentiment of the crowd. Give &lsquo;em what they want. Even if it&rsquo;s  shit. I was ashamed. The highlight went something like this: Dole tells  joke (after all this is a comedy show) &ldquo;How many Frenchmen does it take  to defend Paris? Answer, &ldquo;None, it&rsquo;s never been tried.&rdquo; In response to  such a pathetic case of stupidity, allow me to offer a few historical  facts.</p>
<p>In the months of May and June, 1940, over 100,000  civilians were killed by the Nazis on the roads of France. An equivalent  number of French soldiers died in the same period in defense of their  country. Following a campaign of terror unequaled in the history of the  world, millions of Frenchmen, Belgians and Dutch fled the barbaric Nazi  invasion. For weeks before the Germans rolled into France, Europe had  been bombarded with images Warsovie and Rotterdam, reduced to ashes. The  images of Nazi brutality were burned into the collective conscious of  all of the people of France. Even in the most isolated areas, the rumors  of German savagery had a tremendous impact. A feeling of insecurity  spread like an epidemic. Everyone feared the worse. The Nazi invasion of  France was a masterpiece of psychological warfare. The civilian  population was utilized like a weapon, sending it fleeing to the South,  choking the roads and effectively preventing the French army from  passing.</p>
<p>The French general staff was particularly incompetent.  It stuck to a strategy of containment mired in the thinking of the first  World War. In the face of blitzkrieg, the strategy of defense inherent  in the Maginot Line was totally ineffective. With an overwhelming  superiority of tanks and aircraft, the Nazis were able to speed past the  French positions. The border with neutral Belgium was violated by the  Nazis to the complete surprise of the French. While the German tanks  penetrated deeper and deeper into French territory, and while the  Luftwaffe unleached destruction from the air, the French generals  attempted to define a battle front like that of the Great War. The  French army was totally unprepared for the nature of the threat.</p>
<p>With the roads of Northern France clogged by civilians  fleeing the oncoming invasion, German aircraft attacked, massacring  thousands. This was not an orderly retreat, but a riot of automobiles,  carts, wheel barrows, people, horses, cattle, chickens and goats fleeing  pell mell. In many cases the French civilian leaders simply  disappeared, being among the first to flee. The countryside as well as  the city was emptied, a whirlpool of terrorized men, women, and children  desperately attempting to get out of harm&rsquo;s way. Onto this scene of  desperation, the stukas would fall like falcons on their prey. There was  a siren on the stuka which served no other purpose than to terrorize.  Upon beginning his descent, the pilot would begin the siren, with no  other purpose than to spread panic and fear.</p>
<p>Although the war in France was a disaster, pockets of  resistance sprung up immediately. There were desperate attempts to hold  back the invading army, by isolated military units, valiantly fighting  to the end. The story of the flight of Charles de Gaulle and his role in  the war is well known. Fleeing arrest in Bordeaux, de Gaulle fled to  England where he would organize the French resistance. In the cites and  towns, fighters organized themselves and began to conduct a clandestine  geurilla was, the famous Maquis. During the war, France was a sinister  place, lives lived in shadow, a society in which fear and mistrust  dominated. Much of the population was simply relieved that the war was  over feeling little solidarity with the political class. Many continued  to resist and thousands gave their lives, thousands like Pierre Durand.</p>
<p>I went to Parc Montsouris on August 26, 2003 to place a  bouquet of flowers and to pay tribute to the young man who died here  under these same pines. Under a clear blue sky, I saluted his courage  and his sacrifice.</p>
<p>www.mesbalades.com/ppied000.htm<br /> www.proactivate.com/photo_album/france/montsouris/index.shtml<br /> www.parisparis.com/fr/jardin/montsour.html<br /> www.montsouris.net/index.htm</p> <p>Non  loin de la Porte d&rsquo;Orl&eacute;ans se trouve un petit havre de paix,  abri pour  oiseaux, et promeneurs et joggeurs, le Parc Montsouris. Le  nom  Montsouris viendrait de "Moquesouris", comme on appelait jadis le  site  o&ugrave; des moulins&nbsp;laiss&eacute;s &agrave; l'abandon attiraient les petits rongeurs.  Le  Baron Haussmann, en recr&eacute;ant la ville de Paris a plac&eacute; quatre  espaces  verts aux quatre points cardinaux de la m&eacute;tropole. Au nord, les  Buttes  de Chaumont, &agrave; l&rsquo;est, le bois de Vincennes, &agrave; l&rsquo;ouest, le bois  de  Boulogne, et au sud, le Parc Montsouris. Le Parc Montsouris est le  plus  humble, et le plus joli de tous. &nbsp;</p>
<p>En entrant par le  Nord, par l&rsquo;Avenue Ren&eacute; Coty, on  arrive face &agrave; une colonne en pierre  sur laquelle est pos&eacute;e une statue  de Victoire ail&eacute;e. Derri&egrave;re la  colonne s&rsquo;&eacute;tire un champ entour&eacute;  d&rsquo;arbres. Le parc contient plus de  1400 arbres dont des sujets  centenaires&nbsp;: peuplier de Virginie, c&egrave;dre  de Liban, orme de Sib&eacute;rie,  ginko biloba, et quelques esp&egrave;ces de mon  pays&nbsp;: copalm, et cypre rouge.  En allant tout droit, on plonge dans le  c&oelig;ur du parc, entre les  poussettes et les amoureux. En montant &agrave;  droite, on longe la rue  Nansouty. En haut de la c&ocirc;te, se trouve le  pavillon de m&eacute;t&eacute;o France. Si  on continue, on surplombe la voie ferr&eacute;e,  la Cit&eacute; Universitaire de  l&rsquo;autre c&ocirc;t&eacute; de l&rsquo;avenue. Par la suite, le  chemin descend, et l&rsquo;on  arrive au lac, rep&egrave;re de retrait&eacute;s et de  canards exotiques. Un peu plus  loin, on arrive devant la st&egrave;le &eacute;rig&eacute;e &agrave;  la m&eacute;moire de Pierre Durand,  tu&eacute;, comme autant de jeunes r&eacute;sistants,  pendant le mois d&rsquo;ao&ucirc;t 1944.  Paris est parsem&eacute; de plaques  comm&eacute;moratives comme celle-l&agrave;, cach&eacute;es  discr&egrave;tement le long des murs,  d&eacute;di&eacute;es &agrave; la m&eacute;moire de ses combattants  qui ont surgi dans les rues de  Paname, carabines de fortune &agrave; la main,  pour lib&eacute;rer leur ville.</p>
<p>Un  soir de mars pass&eacute;, pendant que la fr&eacute;n&eacute;sie  anti-fran&ccedil;aise battait son  plein au d&eacute;but de la guerre d&rsquo;Iraq, j&rsquo;ai  assist&eacute; &agrave; une sc&egrave;ne &agrave; la  t&eacute;l&eacute;vision am&eacute;ricaine qui m&rsquo;a profond&eacute;ment  choqu&eacute;. Au Late Show  starring David Letterman, le pauvre Paul  Schaeffer, qui rempla&ccedil;ait  Dave, faisait l&rsquo;entrevue du politicien Bob  Dole. Le &laquo;&nbsp;French Bashing&nbsp;&raquo;  &eacute;tait &agrave; l&rsquo;ordre du jour. Ils se sont lanc&eacute;s  dans une harangue  hyst&eacute;rique anti-fran&ccedil;aise qui aurait &eacute;t&eacute; d&eacute;rangeante  venant de la part  de n&rsquo;importe quel idiot, mais qui &eacute;tait d&rsquo;autant  plus choquante venant  de la part d&rsquo;un homme politique sens&eacute; &ecirc;tre  mesur&eacute;. La connerie &eacute;tait  d&rsquo;autant plus grotesque qu&rsquo;elle passait &agrave; la  t&eacute;l&eacute;vision nationale. Les  propos d&eacute;magogiques de l&rsquo;ex-Senateur,  ex-candidat &agrave; la Maison Blanche,  me faisaient mal. N&rsquo;importe quoi. Dans  un spasme de connerie virulente,  Bob Dole a manifest&eacute; une stupidit&eacute;  incroyable. J&rsquo;avais honte. Le pire&nbsp;:  &laquo;&nbsp;Question&nbsp;: Combien de Fran&ccedil;ais  est-ce que &ccedil;a prend pour d&eacute;fendre  Paris&nbsp;? R&eacute;ponse&nbsp;: Z&eacute;ro, on n&rsquo;a jamais  essay&eacute;.&nbsp;&raquo; Alors, en r&eacute;ponse &agrave; cet  affront &agrave; la raison et &agrave;&nbsp;l&rsquo;histoire,  je propose quelques faits  historiques.</p>
<p>Pendant les mois de mai et juin, 1940, plus  de 100,000  civils ont &eacute;t&eacute; tu&eacute;s sur les routes de la France par l&rsquo;arm&eacute;e  Nazi. Un  nombre &eacute;quivalent de soldats fran&ccedil;ais sont morts &agrave; la m&ecirc;me  &eacute;poque pour  d&eacute;fendre leur pays. Suite &agrave; une campagne de terreur tr&egrave;s  bien r&eacute;ussie,  des millions de Fran&ccedil;ais, Belges, et Hollandais ont fui  l&rsquo;invasion  barbare. Pendant les semaines qui ont pr&eacute;c&eacute;d&eacute; la guerre en  France, la  population a &eacute;t&eacute; bombard&eacute;e par des images de Varsovie et de  Rotterdam  r&eacute;duites en cendres. Les images de la brutalit&eacute; des Nazis  faisaient  partie de la conscience collective. Toute la population avait  vu les  images des villes an&eacute;anties par les Nazis.. M&ecirc;me dans les  campagnes les  plus recul&eacute;es, on &eacute;tait au courant. Et tout le monde  craignait le  pire. L&rsquo;invasion allemande fut un chef d&rsquo;&oelig;uvre de  manipulation  psychologique. Pour emp&ecirc;cher l&rsquo;arm&eacute;e fran&ccedil;aise de riposter   efficacement, les Allemands ont mis en &oelig;uvre un plan de guerre qui   utilisait la population civile comme une arme. La fuite de la   population civile, reculant devant les chars allemands, a effectivement   bloqu&eacute; les routes et a servi &agrave; emp&ecirc;cher l&rsquo;arm&eacute;e fran&ccedil;aise de remonter   vers le nord.</p>
<p>Il faut bien dire que l&rsquo;&eacute;tat-major fran&ccedil;ais  a&nbsp;&eacute;t&eacute;  particuli&egrave;rement d&eacute;faillant. Le strat&egrave;ge de contenance, vestige  de la  premi&egrave;re guerre mondiale, r&eacute;duisait l&rsquo;arm&eacute;e fran&ccedil;aise &agrave; un  strat&egrave;ge de  d&eacute;fense de ligne totalement d&eacute;pass&eacute; par le blitzkrieg.  Cach&eacute;e derri&egrave;re  la ligne Maginot, elle etait incapable d&rsquo;agir  efficacement en face  d&rsquo;une invasion rapide qui contournait les  emplacements fortifi&eacute;s. Les  chars allemands plongeaient dans  l&rsquo;arri&egrave;re-pays semant le d&eacute;sarroi et  occupant le territoire. Et pendant  que les chars les contournaient, les  Fran&ccedil;ais essayaient d&eacute;sesp&eacute;r&eacute;ment  d&rsquo;&eacute;tablir un front. L&rsquo;arm&eacute;e  fran&ccedil;aise &eacute;tait totalement incapable de  r&eacute;sister au strat&egrave;ge nazi.</p>
<p>Pendant que les chars  roulaient &agrave; travers le pays sans  entrave, les avions allemands, les  fameux stukas, bombardaient les  routes, massacrant les civils, dans un  strat&egrave;ge destin&eacute; &agrave; semer la  panique et &agrave; faire fuir la population. Ce  qui a provoqu&eacute; un exil  d&eacute;sordonn&eacute; engorgeant les routes d&rsquo;automobiles,  de charrettes, de  brouettes, de gens &agrave; pied, de fermiers, et de leurs  bestiaux, tout un  charivari effray&eacute;, paniqu&eacute;, avec une seule id&eacute;e&nbsp;:  &eacute;chapper &agrave; la mort.&nbsp;:  Les villes comme les campagnes, &eacute;taient vid&eacute;es de  leurs habitants qui  se poussaient sur les routes du sud. Un tourbillon  de monde et  d&rsquo;animaux terroris&eacute;s qui se trouvaient p&ecirc;le-m&ecirc;le entre  l&rsquo;envahisseur et  l&rsquo;arm&eacute;e fran&ccedil;aise. Hommes, femmes, enfants, chats,  chiens, b&oelig;ufs et  chevaux, fuyant en panique. Des milliers d&rsquo;entre eux  sont morts sous  les mitraillettes des stukas. Ces petits avions ultra  rapide &eacute;taient  munis de sir&egrave;nes qui s&rsquo;allumaient d&egrave;s que l&rsquo;avion  piquait en descente.  Ces sir&egrave;nes n&rsquo;avaient aucune utilisation &agrave; part de  terroriser les gens  qui se trouvaient en dessous..</p>
<p>Bien  que la guerre en France fut une d&eacute;b&acirc;cle, des  poches de r&eacute;sistance se  formaient d&egrave;s l&rsquo;armistice. L&rsquo;histoire de la  fuite du G&eacute;n&eacute;ral DeGaulle  en l&rsquo;Angleterre et sa lutte d&eacute;termin&eacute;e sont  bien connues. En France,  les patriotes s&rsquo;unissaient et une guerre  clandestine s&rsquo;engageait dans  le maquis. La France durant la guerre  &eacute;tait un pays d&rsquo;ombre et de  grisaille, et bien que &ccedil;a soit vrai qu&rsquo;une  partie de la population a  collabor&eacute; avec les occupants, il est aussi  vrai qu&rsquo;il y avait des  milliers d&rsquo;hommes et de femmes qui ont r&eacute;sist&eacute;.  Beaucoup d&rsquo;entre eux  ont pay&eacute; de leur vie, tel Pierre Durand.</p>
<p>Je suis all&eacute;  au Parc Montsouris le 26 ao&ucirc;t, 2003,  poser une gerbe de fleurs et  rendre hommage &agrave; ce jeune homme mort sous  ces m&ecirc;mes arbres. Sous un  ciel bleu clair, je saluais son courage et  son sacrifice.</p>
<p><a href="http://www.mesbalades.com/ppied000.htm">www.mesbalades.com/ppied000.htm</a><br /> <a href="http://www.proactivate.com/photo_album/france/montsouris/index.shtml">www.proactivate.com/photo_album/france/montsouris/index.shtml</a><br /> <a href="http://www.parisparis.com/fr/jardin/montsour.html">www.parisparis.com/fr/jardin/montsour.html</a><br /> <a href="http://www.montsouris.net/index.htm">www.montsouris.net/index.htm</a></p> 2003-10-01 00:00:00
93 y <p>27 July. Today the flag of the Great State of Texas floated over the  H&ocirc;tel de Crillon, Place de la Concorde in the heart of Paris, France.  This was obviously in tribute to Lance Armstrong, native of the &ldquo;Lone  Star State,&rdquo; one of a very exclusive number of racers to have won the  Tour de France five times. along with Bernard Hinault, Jacques Anquetil,  Eddie Merclcx, and Miguel Indurain. I could not help but wonder if  there was not some political undercurrent to the gesture, a tribute to  the home state rather than the home country of the mighty Lance. Flag  waving aside, the day was magnificent, a joyful crowd gathered on the  Champs Elys&eacute;es to welcome the rainbow colored peloton of two-wheel  heroes. They passed my spot ten times, the tires hissing on the asphalt,  the faces of the riders contorted by the effort, flashing past in a  flood of color. A wave of applause preceded each passage of the peloton,  breaking past me and spilling down the avenue. It was a beautiful day  for a bike ride, temperature in the 70s and clear skies. Everybody  seemed to be having a good time. While Lance Armstrong mounted the  podium wearing the traditional yellow jersey, I departed on my own Tour  the France.</p>
<p>1 August. Capbreton. It seems fitting that the biggest  (i.e. the only) music festival in France dedicated to the French  language culture of North America is held in this port town from which  departed the sailors who would discover the Saint Laurence valley.  Before Christopher Columbus landed in Santo Domingo, Basque fishermen  were bar -b-queing on the shore of the River Saguenay near Tadoussac.  There is not much remaining from that period apart from a Basque  tradition in Saint Pierre et Miquelon and Qu&eacute;bec street in this French  town, but thanks to the Festival les D&eacute;ferlantes Francophones, the  French public and the French language singers and poets of North  America, have a venue in which to make acquaintance. Attending were many  friends, Nova Scotian fiddler Johnny Comeau, poet G&eacute;rald LeBlanc and  songwriter Ronald Bourgeois. In the middle of a record breaking heat  wave, we lived in the ghetto of a &ldquo;Little Acadie&rdquo; . I had the pleasure  of presenting the French language version of my documentary, &ldquo;Contre  vents, contre mar&eacute;es&rdquo; at the opening of the festival. The French public  is very open to North American francophone culture, but suffers from a  lack of information due largely to the indifference of the French media.  Here&rsquo;s hoping that this little festival will plant the seeds of a  bountiful harvest for the French language poets and singers of North  America in the hearts of the French. Robert Charlebois performed for the  closing of the festival. I shared a moment with him on the beach amidst  the local surfers and a horde of tourists. His show was energetic and  well received. I was happy to visit with my friend, drummer Justin  Allard.</p>
<p>5 August. Saint Jean pied de Port. Once you have left  behind the flat land of Les Landes and its ubiquitous pine forests, and  climbed into the Pyranees, it is clear that you are in Basque country.  All of the road signs are in the two languages, French and Basque, with  the French as often as not, painted over in black. There is  independantiste graffiti abounding, the slogans more or less virulent.  It was impossible for me to avoid comparing the situation of the Basque  minority with that of the French language minorities of North America,  the Cajuns of Louisiana, and the Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois. The total Basque population  is 2.9 million with 262,640 living in France. Three of the seven Basque  provinces are north of the border. In spite of the bucolic image of  sheep herders in red berets, only 6% of the population works in  agriculture. 22% work in industry and 72% work in the service sector  which includes the very important tourist industry. The image of the  Basques, for the outside world as well as for the members of the  community themselves, is that of a people of the land, even though most  of the community lives in an urban environment. Given the fact that  Basque country is not a nation state, the question of identity resembles  that which we know in Louisiana. According to Jean Haritschelhar,  president of the Academy of the Basque language, &ldquo;To be Basque is to  consider oneself Basque, even though one might be a citizen of Spain or  France or even the United States. It is to be conscious of being part of  people, of a community, social, spiritual and emotional to which one is  attached by blood or spirit or heart.&rdquo; Sounds a lot like the definition  of Cajun: &ldquo;A Cajun is someone who considers himself to be Cajun.&rdquo; As  with the Cajuns of Louisiana, the challenge for the Basque people is to  be able to create a viable future for the community in the context of a  culture which is often reduced to a caricature. How to surpass the image  of a country rich in shepherds, sailors, jai alai players? How to go  beyond the folklore of a festive tradition? The problem is compounded by  the media in France (them again) who have a tendency to reduce the  Basque question at best to the struggle for independence or at worst to  the phenomena of political violence.</p>
<p>The political question is all the more confused by the  real threat of terrorism posed by the ETA, just across the border. Ten  times more Basques reside in Spain than in France, and the relation  between each respective Basque community and each respective national  state is profoundly different. It is important to understand that during  the 19th and 20th centuries, the Basque of Spain fought three wars  against the central power (the 2 Carlist wars of the 19th century and  the Spanish Civil war of 1936-1939) while the Basques of France fought  in three wars for the central power (the Franco-Prussian war of 1870 and  the two world wars). The Basques in France did suffer a severe  repression during the French revolution, primarily because of their  attachment to the Catholic clergy. During the &ldquo;Terreur&rdquo; many villages  were declared &ldquo;inf&auml;mes&rdquo; and thousands of villagers were deported to  other departments, with hundreds dying from cold, hunger and disease.  (The Deportation of the Acadians took place only 35 years before.) The  enlistment of the Basques in the French army during the First World War  marked the turning point for the community in terms of its identity, the  beginning of a strain of French nationalism, conservative and Catholic  in essence. 6000 Basques died in the trenches of the First World War,  and the community came out of the experience with their traditional  values integrated into the dominant political ideology of France at that  time. It was not before the 1930s that there existed an independence  movement. Today the existence of political militants does oblige the  traditional political parties to take into account a certain number of  demands: the creation of a Department (State) of the Pays Basque, the  creation of Basque university in Bayonne, and the teaching and  institutionalization of the Basque language. In the Pays Basque, 26.4%  of the population speaks the language, 9.3% understand without speaking  and 64.2% do not speak Basque. The ability to speak the language is  particularly weak in the 15-35 age group. The percentage of bilingual  French-Bascophones falls from 35% for those over 65 years to 11% for the  young. In Bayonne, the largest city, Bascophones represent less than 1%  of the population 16-25 years old. This decline, which is the mirror  image of the situation in Louisiana, takes place in the family, parents  not transmitting the language to their children. The question is whether  it is too late to save the language or whether it will be relegated to  the ghetto of folklore as seems to be the case with the French community  of Louisiana.</p>
<p>In terms of the survival of minority culture, the Pays  Basque fits in somewhere between Acadian Louisiana and Qu&eacute;bec. It  resembles most the situation of the Acadians in New Brunswick, first of  all by demography (approximately 250,000 Basques in France,  approximately 300,000 Acadians in New Brunswick), and by the rate of  assimilation. While in Louisiana, the rate of assimilation can be  considered at just about 100%, the rate of assimilation in New Brunswick  and the Pays Basque, while threatening, is not nearly as dramatic. The  challenge for each of these communities, Acadian, Cajun, as well as  Basque, is to be able to offer the possibility of a contemporary  expression in the traditional language. To remain viable, the younger  generations must be able to satisfy their desire for modernity within  the native language, and to be able to go beyond a simple repetition of  folklore. In Qu&eacute;bec, the demographic situation assures the survival of  the French language in way that neither the Acadians, nor the Basques,  nor particularly the Cajuns can take for granted. The similarly between  the Pays Basque and Qu&eacute;bec is closest regarding the question of  independence. Although the political will for separation from the  Canadian confederation is at a low point in Qu&eacute;bec, the Parti Qu&eacute;becois,  obliges the political discourse to take into account the question of  independence. The desire for a specifically Basque department with the  French nation state resembles the actual relationship between Qu&eacute;bec and  Canada. The history of Qu&eacute;bec and that of Pays Basque are significantly  different, yet each community shares a deep desire for political  autonomy. All of these communities, Basque, Cajun, Acadian, Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois  share the hope of preserving their respective cultures and of  transmitting to future generation their linguistic heritage.</p>
<p>8 August. Col de Organbexterka. Migration in Europe for  shore birds and water fowl takes place largely via the Atlantic coast.  For the songbirds and birds of preys, however there are a few  possibilities, via Italy and Sicily and onto Africa, or via the Iberian  peninsula, and across the straight of Gibraltar. Before arriving in  Spain, however, the birds must cross the Pyranees mountains, which  present themselves like a wall to all of the migrants. There are several  passes which allow the birds to continue south, one of the most  important of which is the Col de Organbbexterka. On top of the challenge  of crossing the mountains, the birds are confronted with another  difficulty, the wall of lead thrown up by hunters waiting in the passes.  Unlike North America, where environmentalists and hunters have  established a solid relationship based on their mutual desire to  preserve migratory species and the habitat upon which they depend, the  situation in Europe is characterized by antagonism. (Which is not to say  that migratory species in North America are not stressed:  Ornithologists estimate a 50% decline in passerine species in the last  20 years due largely to loss of habitat). In Europe, the protection of  migratory species is complicated by the national borders over which the  birds have to travel. There is a general lack of effectiveness in the  wildlife protection service which suffers from a lack of means and a  lack of will in restraining the hunting population. Each year hunters in  Europe kill 1.8 million (1,800,000) &ldquo;palombes&rdquo;, wood pigeons (Columba  palumbus) and stock doves (Columba oenas) during the fall migration. A  number which menaces the survival of the species. (The passenger pigeon  which dominated the skies of North America prior to the arrival of the  Europeans was hunted to extinction in the 19th century). In 1979, a  group of militant environmentalists &ldquo;liberated&rdquo; the Col de  Oragnbexterka. Every year from June to November, the mountain is  &ldquo;occupied&rdquo; by bird watchers. A scientific census of birds of prey and  &ldquo;palombes&rdquo; is performed. From dawn to dusk, the bird watchers are on  duty, counting the migrants, and at the same time, protecting the site  from the hunters. They are none the less unable to prevent more than 2  tons of lead from falling into the environment from the nearby peaks  during the hunting season. In order to occupy the space, the  organization must pay over 20,000 Euros per year. To support their cause  visit http://www.organbidexka.org</p>
<p>In the twilight, we left our new friends, the moon in  three quarters climbing in the sky above the peaks. The road descending  from the Col d&rsquo;Iraty was completely covered with graffiti. &ldquo;Lance is  God&rdquo;. and &ldquo;ETA&rdquo; and complete sentences in Basque.
