The bicycle Tour de  France had just passed here. We drove down to the valley under the  starry sky, our trip slowed down by the herds of sheep and goats  crossing the road.</p> <p>27  juillet. Paris. Aujourd&rsquo;hui le drapeau du Texas flottait sur l&rsquo;H&ocirc;tel  de  Crillon, Place de la Concorde o&ugrave; normalement flotte le pavillon de  la  France. C&rsquo;&eacute;tait certainement en hommage &agrave; Lance Armstrong,  originaire  du &laquo;&nbsp;Lone Star State&nbsp;&raquo;, un des cinq coureurs &agrave; gagner le  Tour de France  cinq fois, avec Bernard Hinault, Jacques Anquetil, Eddie  Merckx et  Miguel Indurain. Je n&rsquo;ai pas compris la signifiance de ce  geste  (drapeau du Texas plut&ocirc;t que drapeau am&eacute;ricain) et je me  demandais s&rsquo;il  ne pouvait pas y avoir de sous-entendu politique. Cela  dit, les Champs  Elys&eacute;es &eacute;taient remplis d&rsquo;une foule joyeuse dans  laquelle je me  trouvais pour accueillir ce peloton de coureurs sveltes,  habill&eacute;s de  toutes les couleurs. Un arc-en-ciel d&rsquo;&eacute;clair qui nous  passait sous les  yeux dix fois de suite, nous donnant &agrave; chaque fois  juste le temps de  savoir qu&rsquo;ils &eacute;taient pass&eacute;s. &Ccedil;a faisait un bruit de  schuss, les pneus  des v&eacute;los l&eacute;chant l&rsquo;asphalte, les visages de coureurs  crisp&eacute;s d&rsquo;effort,  leurs r&acirc;lements noy&eacute;s dans un torrent d&rsquo;&eacute;nergie  folle. Une vague  d&rsquo;applaudissements montait l&rsquo;avenue avant de se casser  sur le rocher de  mon regard, la cr&ecirc;te d&rsquo;&eacute;cume me frappant entre les  yeux avant de rouler  encore plus loin. Il faisait beau sur les Champs  Elys&eacute;es et tout le  monde &eacute;tait content. Pendant que Lance Armstrong  montait sur le podium  pour recevoir le bouquet de roses traditionnel,  je partais sur mon  propre tour de France.<br /> <br /> 1 ao&ucirc;t. Capbreton. Il me  semble tr&egrave;s &agrave; propos que le  plus grand, voir le seul festival d&eacute;di&eacute; &agrave;  l&rsquo;Am&eacute;rique francophone en  France se passe dans cette ville d&rsquo;o&ugrave; sont  partis les marins qui  allaient d&eacute;couvrir la vall&eacute;e du Saint Laurent.  Avant que Christophe  Colomb arrive &agrave; Saint Domingue, les p&ecirc;cheurs  basques faisaient des  bar-b-ques au bord de la rivi&egrave;re Saguenay &agrave;  Tadoussac. Il reste peu de  cette histoire &agrave; part une tradition basque &agrave;  St. Pierre et Miquelon et  la rue Qu&eacute;bec sur le port de cette ville  fran&ccedil;aise, mais gr&acirc;ce &agrave;  Maurice Segall, l&rsquo;organisateur du festival Les  D&eacute;ferlantes  Francophones, les artistes francophones nord am&eacute;ricains et  le public  fran&ccedil;ais peuvent se d&eacute;couvrir mutuellement. J&rsquo;ai retrouv&eacute; des  vieux  amis, Johnny Comeau, G&eacute;rald LeBlanc, Ronald Bourgeois et tout un   contingent de po&egrave;tes et de musiciens de notre bord &agrave; nous de   l&rsquo;Atlantique. Sous une chaleur &eacute;crasante, nous habitons une petite   Acadie outre mer. J&rsquo;ai &eacute;t&eacute; invit&eacute; au festival pour pr&eacute;senter le   documentaire Contre vents, contre mar&eacute;es, sur grand &eacute;cran. Le public   fran&ccedil;ais est tr&egrave;s ouvert &agrave; la culture des francophones am&eacute;ricains, mais   il faut dire qu&rsquo;en France, la diffusion de la culture fran&ccedil;aise nord   am&eacute;ricaine souffre d&rsquo;un manque d&rsquo;acc&egrave;s au m&eacute;dias. Esp&eacute;rant que ce petit   festival plantera les graines d&rsquo;une r&eacute;colte abondante dans le c&oelig;ur des   Fran&ccedil;ais de France pour nous les po&egrave;tes et musiciens de langue   fran&ccedil;aise en Am&eacute;rique. Robert Charlebois a fait la cl&ocirc;ture du festival   J&rsquo;ai pu partager un moment avec lui sur la plage, froliquant dans les   vagues entre les surfeurs locaux et les touristes en vacance. Il a   donn&eacute; un spectacle plein d&rsquo;&eacute;nergie. J&rsquo;ai &eacute;t&eacute; heureux de retrouver   Justin Allard qui l&rsquo;accompagnait. <br /> <br /> 5 ao&ucirc;t. Saint Jean pied de Port. Une fois qu&rsquo;on quitte  la plaine des  Landes et ses for&ecirc;ts de pins, et qu&rsquo;on monte dans les  Pyr&eacute;n&eacute;es, on se  rend bien compte qu&rsquo;on est au pays Basque. Toutes les  pancartes  routi&egrave;res sont dans les deux langues, et le plus souvent, la  version  fran&ccedil;aise est effac&eacute;e par une couche de peinture noire. On voit  des  affiches ind&eacute;pendantistes un peu partout, avec des slogans plus ou   moins virulents. On ne peut pas s&rsquo;emp&ecirc;cher de faire la comparaison  avec  la Louisiane, et &eacute;galement avec le Qu&eacute;bec. D&rsquo;abord les  statistiques&nbsp;:  La population basque est de 2.9 millions dont 262, 640  habitent en  France. Trois des sept provinces basques se trouvent au  Nord de la  fronti&egrave;re. Bien que l&rsquo;image du pays basque soit plut&ocirc;t  bucolique, genre  troupeaux de brebis gard&eacute;s par berger en b&eacute;ret rouge,  seulement 6% de  la population travaille en agriculture. 22 % travaille  en industrie,  avec 72% travaillant dans le secteur des services qui  comprend  l&rsquo;industrie touristique. Les Basques s&rsquo;identifient, cependant,  comme un  peuple de la terre, bien que la plupart habitent en zone  urbaine. Mais,  &eacute;tant donn&eacute; que le pays basque n&rsquo;est pas un &eacute;tat, la  question  identitaire ressemble beaucoup &agrave; celle que nous connaissons en   Louisiane. Selon Jean Haritschelhar, pr&eacute;sident de l&rsquo;Acad&eacute;mie de la   langue basque, &laquo;&nbsp;Etre Basque, c&rsquo;est se consid&eacute;rer comme membre de la   nation basque, m&ecirc;me si l&rsquo;on est de citoyennet&eacute; fran&ccedil;aise, espagnole, ou   am&eacute;ricaine. C&rsquo;est avoir pleine et claire conscience de faire partie   d&rsquo;un peuple, d&rsquo;une communaut&eacute; sociale, spirituelle et affective &agrave;   laquelle nous attachent des liens de sang ou d&rsquo;esprit ou de c&oelig;ur.&nbsp;&raquo; Ce   qui ressemble &agrave; la meilleure d&eacute;finition d&rsquo;un Cadien, soit &laquo;&nbsp;Un Cadien   est quelqu&rsquo;un qui pense qu&rsquo;il est Cadien.&nbsp;&raquo; Comme en Louisiane, on   trouve en pays basque le d&eacute;fi de se cr&eacute;er une modernit&eacute; dans le   contexte d&rsquo;une culture qui est souvent r&eacute;duite &agrave; la caricature. Comment   d&eacute;passer l&rsquo;image r&eacute;ductrice et rassurante d&rsquo;un pays fort de ses   bergers, de ses marins d&eacute;couvreurs, de ses joueurs de pelote et de sa   tradition festive&nbsp;? Le probl&egrave;me est d&rsquo;autant plus compliqu&eacute; par les   m&eacute;dias qui ont tendance &agrave; r&eacute;duire la question basque &agrave; l&rsquo;&eacute;piph&eacute;nom&egrave;ne   de la violence, au mieux &agrave; la seule revendication nationaliste. La   question politique est d&rsquo;autant plus perdue dans la brume, parce que de   l&rsquo;autre c&ocirc;te de la fronti&egrave;re, en Espagne, o&ugrave; vivent plus de 10 fois   plus de Basques qu&rsquo;en France, l&rsquo;ETA continue &agrave; poser une menace   terroriste. La relation entre les communaut&eacute;s basques et l&rsquo;&eacute;tat dans   lequel elles se trouvent est tr&egrave;s diff&eacute;rente des deux c&ocirc;t&eacute;s de la   fronti&egrave;re. &Agrave; savoir que pendant les 19e et 20e si&egrave;cles, les Basques   espagnols se sont battus trois fois contre l&rsquo;Espagne (les deux guerres   carlistes, et la guerre civile de 1936-1939) et que pendant la m&ecirc;me   p&eacute;riode, les Basques en France ont fait trois guerres avec la France   (la guerre de 1870 et les deux guerres mondiales). Cela dit, les   Basques ont subi une r&eacute;pression s&eacute;v&egrave;re pendant la R&eacute;volution Fran&ccedil;aise  &agrave;  cause surtout de leur attachement au clerg&eacute; catholique, et leurs   relations famili&egrave;res avec l&rsquo;Espagne qui ont &eacute;t&eacute; durement sanctionn&eacute;es.   Sous la Terreur, plusieurs communes ont &eacute;t&eacute; d&eacute;clar&eacute;es &laquo;&nbsp;inf&acirc;mes&nbsp;&raquo;, et   des milliers d&rsquo;habitants ont &eacute;t&eacute; d&eacute;port&eacute;s dans les d&eacute;partements   voisins, des centaines d&rsquo;entre eux p&eacute;riront de froid, de faim et de   maladie. (La d&eacute;portation des Acadiens n&rsquo;a eu lieu que 35 ans plus t&ocirc;t).   L&rsquo;engagement des Basques dans l&rsquo;arm&eacute;e fran&ccedil;aise lors de la premi&egrave;re   guerre mondiale marque le d&eacute;but d&rsquo;un nationalisme fran&ccedil;ais,   conservateur et catholique dans la communaut&eacute;. 6000 Basques p&eacute;rissent   dans les combats. Comme les Cadiens suite &agrave; la deuxi&egrave;me guerre   mondiale, les Basques sortent du conflit avec une identit&eacute; red&eacute;finie   par l&rsquo;exp&eacute;rience. Leurs valeurs traditionnelles sont int&eacute;gr&eacute;es et ne   servent qu&rsquo;&agrave; renforcer l&rsquo;id&eacute;ologie dominante. Il faut attendre les   ann&eacute;es trente pour voir le nationalisme basque se montrer en France.   Aujourd&rsquo;hui les militants basques obligent les partis politiques   traditionnels &agrave; prendre position sur un certain nombre de probl&egrave;mes   concrets&nbsp;: revendication d&rsquo;un d&eacute;partement Pays basque, d&rsquo;une universit&eacute;   de plein exercice &agrave; Bayonne, et l&rsquo;enseignement et l&rsquo;officialisation de   la langue basque. <br /> <br /> Au Pays basque, 26.4% des habitants connaissent et  utilisent la langue,  9.3% la comprennent sans la pratiquer et 64.2%  sont non bascophones. La  comp&eacute;tence linguistique est particuli&egrave;rement  faible chez les 16-34 ans.  Le pourcentage des bilingues chute de 35%  parmi les plus de 64 ans &agrave;  11% chez les jeunes. &Agrave; Bayonne, la  m&eacute;tropole, les bascophones ne  repr&eacute;sentent que 1% de la population de  16 &agrave; 24 ans. Ce d&eacute;clin  s&rsquo;explique par la d&eacute;faillance familiale, et  ressemble comme une image  miroir &agrave; ce qui s&rsquo;est pass&eacute; en Louisiane  depuis que je suis n&eacute;. La  question qu&rsquo;on se pose est de savoir si ce  n&rsquo;est pas trop tard pour  sauver la langue ou bien si elle sera rel&eacute;gu&eacute;e  au folklore comme cela  se passe actuellement chez nous.<br /> <br /> Par rapport &agrave; la question de la survie de sa culture  minoritaire, le  pays Basque se trouve &ecirc;tre quelque part entre le Qu&eacute;bec  et la  Louisiane. Il ressemble plus &agrave; l&rsquo;Acadie, d&rsquo;abord par sa  d&eacute;mographie,  ensuite par une attitude fondamentalement non s&eacute;paratiste,  et par son  taux d&rsquo;assimilation. Tandis qu&rsquo;en Louisiane le taux  d&rsquo;assimilation est  pr&egrave;s de 100%, au Nouveau Brunswick bien q&ugrave;&rsquo;il soit  inqui&eacute;tant, il n&rsquo;est  pas catastrophique. Le d&eacute;fi pour toutes ces  communaut&eacute;s, autant  cadienne, acadienne, que basque, est de pouvoir  offrir la possibilit&eacute;  d&rsquo;une expression contemporaine &agrave; sa jeunesse, et  non pas de rester fig&eacute;  dans un folklore aussi attrayant qu&rsquo;il soit. La  situation d&eacute;mographique  du Qu&eacute;bec assure la survie de la langue  traditionnelle de la Belle  Province d&rsquo;une fa&ccedil;on que ni les Acadiens, ni  les Cadiens ni les Basques  peuvent prendre pour acquis. C&rsquo;est sur la  question d&rsquo;ind&eacute;pendance que  le Pays Basque et le Qu&eacute;bec se ressemblent.  Bien que la volont&eacute; de se  s&eacute;parer du Canada paraisse &ecirc;tre en &eacute;clipse  pour le moment, le Parti  Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois, m&ecirc;me en situation minoritaire au  gouvernement, oblige que le  discours politique tienne compte de la  question d&rsquo;ind&eacute;pendance. Les  ind&eacute;pendantistes basques vont-ils pouvoir  arriver &agrave; une situation  institutionnalis&eacute;e telle qu&rsquo;elle existe au  Qu&eacute;bec. Bien que les  histoires des deux peuples soient tr&egrave;s  diff&eacute;rentes, ils partagent,  cependant, l&rsquo;espoir d&rsquo;une autonomie  politique r&eacute;elle. Ce qui n&rsquo;est pas  le cas ni en Acadie, ni en  Louisiane. Malgr&eacute; les diff&eacute;rences de  situation, toutes ces communaut&eacute;s  esp&egrave;rent maintenir leurs cultures  uniques et transmettre aux prochaines  g&eacute;n&eacute;rations leurs h&eacute;ritages  linguistiques respectifs. <br /> <br /> 8 ao&ucirc;t. Col de Organbexterka. La migration d&rsquo;oiseaux en  Europe passe,  pour les limicoles, ainsi que les canards et les oies,  par le couloir  du littoral Atlantique. Pour les autres, il reste  quelques  possibilit&eacute;s&nbsp;: par l&rsquo;Italie et la Sicile, ou bien par la  p&eacute;ninsule  Ib&eacute;rique et le d&eacute;troit de Gibraltar. Avant d&rsquo;arriver en  Espagne, il  faut survoler les Pyr&eacute;n&eacute;es. La cha&icirc;ne des montagnes se  dresse comme un  mur devant les migrateurs, mais il existe quelques  passages dont un des  plus importants et le Col de Organbexterka. En  plus de la difficult&eacute; de  contourner les montagnes, les oiseaux sont  confront&eacute;s &agrave; un mur de  plomb. &Agrave; l&rsquo;aff&ucirc;t sur les pics par lesquels les  oiseaux sont oblig&eacute;s de  passer, un nombre important de chausseurs  attendent. Au contraire de  l&rsquo;Am&eacute;rique du Nord o&ugrave; la relation entre  chasseurs et amateurs d&rsquo;oiseaux  est plut&ocirc;t bonne, bas&eacute;e sur un d&eacute;sir  partag&eacute; de pr&eacute;server la sant&eacute; des  esp&egrave;ces ainsi que l&rsquo;habitat sur  lequel ils d&eacute;pendent, en Europe cette  relation est plut&ocirc;t tendue. (Ce  qui ne veut pas dire que la situation  des oiseaux en Am&eacute;rique est  particuli&egrave;rement bonne, au contraire, on  constate une r&eacute;duction  d&rsquo;environ 50% des populations des oiseux  passereaux depuis seulement  les derniers 20 ann&eacute;es, d&ucirc;e essentiellement  &agrave; la destruction  d&rsquo;habitat),. En Europe la protection des esp&egrave;ces  migratrices est  compliqu&eacute;e par les fronti&egrave;res nationales qu&rsquo;ils sont  oblig&eacute;s de  traverser. Le manque de discipline dans le domaine du  contr&ocirc;le de la  chasse est aussi un probl&egrave;me s&eacute;rieux. Les gardes de  chasse n&rsquo;ont pas  toujours le pouvoir ou bien la volont&eacute; de confronter  les chasseurs. On  estime que tous les ans&nbsp;1,8 million (1,800,000) de  &laquo;&nbsp;palombes&nbsp;&raquo;  (pigeons ramiers et colombins), sont tu&eacute;es lors de leur  migration. Un  nombre qui menace la survie de ces deux esp&egrave;ces. En  r&eacute;ponse &agrave; cette  perte consid&eacute;rable, depuis&nbsp;1979 on a &laquo;&nbsp;lib&eacute;r&eacute;&nbsp;&raquo; le Col  de  Organbexterka. Chaque ann&eacute;e pendant l&rsquo;&eacute;t&eacute; et l&rsquo;automne, le col est   occup&eacute; par un groupe de miroiseurs engag&eacute;s. Ils font un recensement   tr&egrave;s pointu des esp&egrave;ces en migration, notamment les &laquo;&nbsp;palombes&nbsp;&raquo; et les   oiseaux de proie. De l&rsquo;aube jusqu&rsquo;au couch&eacute; du soleil, ils guettent la   vall&eacute;e, comptant les migrateurs, et en m&ecirc;me temps emp&ecirc;chant l&rsquo;acc&egrave;s du   site aux chasseurs. Pourtant, ils n&rsquo;arrivent pas &agrave; emp&ecirc;cher la chasse   dans les collines avoisinantes, o&ugrave; plus de deux tonnes de plomb tombent   dans la nature chaque ann&eacute;e &agrave; cause des chasseurs. Les miroiseurs   d&eacute;fendent courageusement ce couloir migrateur et attirent l&rsquo;attention   du monde sur la protection des oiseaux migrateurs. Ils sont oblig&eacute;s de   louer l&rsquo;espace sur la colline au co&ucirc;t de plus de 20.000 Euros par an.   Pour soutenir cette action, visitez&nbsp;<a href="http://www.organbidexka.org/" target="_blank">http//:www.organbidexka.org</a><br /> <br /> Au cr&eacute;puscule, j&rsquo;ai quitt&eacute; mes nouveaux amis, la lune au  trois quarts  grimpant dans le ciel au dessus des pics. Le chemin qui  descend du col  d&rsquo;Iraty &eacute;tait compl&egrave;tement couvert de graffitis, &laquo;&nbsp;Lance  is God&nbsp;&raquo;,  aussi &laquo;&nbsp;ETA&nbsp;&raquo;, et des phrases enti&egrave;res en basque. Le tour de  France  version bicyclette venait de passer. On descendait sous la  vo&ucirc;te  &eacute;toil&eacute;e vers la vall&eacute;e, notre voyage ralenti par les troupeaux de   brebis qui traversaient la route.</p> 2003-08-27 00:00:00
94 y <p>July 6. Vienne. The Jazz Festival of Vienne is held in the old Roman  amphitheater. Quite a sight the stone bleachers climbing halfway to the  sky. And to think that the amphitheater has been here for centuries.  There was a towering wall, as high as the highest benches, where the  stage now stands, which reverberated the sound allowing the spectator in  the last bench to hear the dialogue. The wall was torn down, no longer  necessary in an age of power amps. It was our first performance of the  tour and we were victim to the usual technical problems, but all in all,  it was a good show. The evening was dedicated to Louisiana music and I  had the pleasure of meeting some old friends. Bobby Michot and his  Franco-american Cajun band heated up the crowd in the afternoon. Chef  Dwight Landreneau regaled the festival goers with some Louisiana  cuisine. He had saved two boxes of Tony Chachere&rsquo;s creole spice mix,  which he presented to me. But of all of the homefolks that I saw, none  touched me more than Rick Sebastien. Rick and I played together over  twenty years ago in New Orleans. He is originally from Lafayette but has  been living in New York City for years. He was playing with Los Hombres  Calientes, a New Orleans group playing an afro-caribean salsa mix. He  was very chic in his Jazz Man attire, although suffering a little from  hair-space-itis. In the days we played together, Rick had hair like an  azalea bush. Now adays his coif is a little more sedate, but his spirit  is as exuberant as ever. It was great to see him. And Nicole Boudreaux  as well. Nicole is an adopted Louisianienne who is originally from here.  She was in town visiting her own homefolks. She is a very devoted  French teacher and the president of the Consortium of French Immersion  schools. Nicole gave me the sad news that Richard Guidry is retiring.  Richard is the director of the French and Spanish immersion programs for  the Department of Education in Louisiana, and as such is responsible  for the hundreds of foreign teachers who are leading the struggle to  preserve our cultural and linguistic heritage. Having spent thirty years  fighting the good fight, Richard Guidry has decided to pass the torch.  We will miss him dearly, and we wish him all the best in his new  endeavors. As far as our endeavor was concerned, in this old Roman town ,  it finished in the dressing room underneath the old Roman stage,  reminiscing with old friends. A good and tender moment.</p>
<p>July 7. We left the hotel at 9AM and plunged into one  of the horrendous traffic jams which plague the highways of France in  the tourist season. After a wild ride through the small streets on the  edge of town, we were able to make the train station in Lyon with only  seconds to spare. Weighed down with a considerable quantity of baggage,  our equipment and personal bags, we were none the less able to jump  aboard the TGV (Train Grande Vitesse. i.e. fast damn train) and settle  in for the two hour ride to Paris. I love traveling by train, the  hypnotic clippity clop of the wheels whacking the rails, a view of the  country side unavailable any where else, and a sense of being detached  from the world. Plus the food aboard the TGV is edible. Looking out over  the gently rolling hills covered with golden wheat, the stalks swaying  gently in the breeze, with here and there a stone farm house punctuating  the landscape, I lapsed into a state suspended between reality and the  dream. Once arrived in Paris, however, the dream was over. Descending  from the train, we were catapaulted into a pool of noise and agitation.  Trailing our still considerable quantity of gear, we made off for the  New Morning. Hidden in a small street in the bowels of Paris, the New  Morning is &ldquo;the&rdquo; show club in town. But like most of the show clubs in  most of the towns in the world, it is far from fancy. Particularly the  dressing room. But I have seen worse. The sound system, however, is very  good. With our debut gig behind us, and a lively crowd in the house, we  were able to enjoy a good show.</p>
<p>July 8. Given the late night and the excitement which  always follows a show, it is no wonder that we were unable to get to  sleep before the wee wee hours. Which made for a less than pleasant wake  up call. On top of which, the taxi was late in coming, making for an  anxious ride to the airport. Welcome to on the road. With our still  considerable baggage in tow, and the usual hassles attendant upon  airplane travel, it was not until we actually were seated on the plane  that we were able to relax. Once we did climb aboard, however, we were  already in Italy. The cabin personnel, with their Roman noses, their  elegant style, extravagant gestures and pearly white teeth, created a  definitely Latin ambiance. Everyone spoke Italian except the pilot who  expressed himself in three foreign languages, all of which were  incomprehensible to me: Italian, airplane French and airplane English.  Once we arrived in Naples, we were greeted by Tomaso and his staff, all  wearing the black t-shirts of the Festival de Blues del Liri. Isola del  Liri is a small town halfway between Rome and Naples. Perched on the  mountainside, it is known for the small river (Liri) along the banks of  which are scattered the old stone buildings of the town, and a small  island (Isola) in the middle of the river which is home to a family of  forlorn looking geese. Given the lack of sleep from the previous night,  we were anxious to get to the hotel for some rest. But not before we  took time to &ldquo;mangare&rdquo;. We stopped on the roadside in one of those  ubiquitous restaurants which looks as though it was built a hundred  years ago and has not been renovated since, but which serves a fare as  simple as it is delicious. And the Caff&eacute;. As any coffee lover will tell  you, the best espresso in the world is in Italy. Why this is the case,  remains one of the great mysteries of life. The espresso machine, the  level of steam pressure, the coffee and its roasting, all could  certainly be reproduced elsewhere, but nowhere else but Italy is the  espresso as luxurious and as good. And this is true for even the most  pitiful looking bistro in the most out of the way place. I would have  spent my afternoon drinking cup after cup of the thick-as-mud elixir,  just listening to the Italians talk, but duty called.</p>
<p>We checked in and headed right to bed. During the  siesta, a violent thunder storm burst upon the valley. Thunder groaned  as though the mountains were shouting basso profondo. The rain fell in  buckets. A continuous hard rain which fell to the delight of the local  farmers, suffering as they are from one of the worst droughts in over  one hundred years, but which was a bane to the festival organizers. The  Blues Festival Isola del Liri is a very special event. It is one of the  only if not the only major free-to-the-public festival in Italy. And as  such it is an event that touches the community as a whole. Watching  Tomaso and his colleagues wringing their hands in the very demonstrative  manner of the Italians, their anxiety was palpable. We finally decided  to go down to the site. In spite of the plastic roof over the stage, the  entire surface was drenched. The equipment was covered in black  plastic, the color of death. The technicians were huddled under one  corner of the roof in make shift raincoats. Their hands were immobile at  their sides. There are few things which are of an aspect as sad as an  Italian who is standing still, his hands, so used to gesticulation,  abandoned useless at his side. Realizing that it would be a while before  the stage could be made ready, we decided to take a tour of the town.  During which the sun burst from behind the clouds. A good sign. Lost in  the labyrinth of the old town, we found a trattoria. Spaghetti al  pomodoro, pollo paillarde, tira misu. Heaven.</p>
<p>Finally the stage dried up enough to allow the  technicians to set up. Even though we did not have enough time for a  sound check, the show started as scheduled. Thanks to a father (Mario)  and son (Manuel) crew, the sound was very good. The square was chock  full of Italians. They were stacked up on the wall and the crowd risked  spilling into the river. All Isola was there, having come from  kilometers around to dance to the rhythm of our Louisiana style songs.</p>
<p>July 12. After returning to Paris with two days off, we  headed back south. Around 1 o&rsquo;clock in the morning we met up with the  bus in which we were to travel. Catastrophe. Instead of the bus that we  had ordered, with bunks and sheets and pillows for all, we found  ourselves aboard a tourist transport bus. The driver kept insisting that  this was the bus we ordered, brandishing an order form on which it was  marked &ldquo;couchettes&rdquo; i.e. bunks. He folded down the seats to make a row  of back busting &ldquo;bunks&rdquo;. &ldquo;These are bunks&rdquo; ,he said, &ldquo;If you had wanted  &ldquo;beds&rdquo; you should have ordered &ldquo;beds&rdquo;. There was not much point in  arguing with him in the middle of the night in the middle of the busiest  season of the year. Evidently the bus company had found a client who  was prepared to rent our bus for a longer period, and so we were  confronted with a bad situation and no wriggle room. In Europe there are  no partitions between sections of a tour bus as there are in the USA,  this due to fire regulations. There are wonderful double deckers,  however, which solve the problem by having a sleeping section below and a  lounge above. One of which we had ordered. But instead of which we  found ourselves aboard a tourist bus with one fold down stem to stern  &ldquo;bunk&rdquo;. No sheets, no pillows, and curtains too thin to keep out the  light. Once we got to Bagnols, around 11 AM, in spite of the assurances  that we had obtained from the hotel that our rooms would be ready, they  were not, and we were told that we could not have access until after  check out time, 1 PM. Then our friendly driver informed us that we had  to unload all of our gear because he was going to sleep and did not want  to be disturbed. Ass hole. So we found ourselves seated atop our gear  in the hotel parking lot, a hotel which had no restaurant. Welcome to on  the road. At least the surroundings were pleasant enough, hidden away  in a little park, with cicadas singing to beat all hell. Finally we were  able to slither into our rooms. One of the festival drivers had a  brother in law with a pizza parlor and he was able to finagle a table  for us even though it was Sunday and every restaurant in town was  packed.</p>
<p>I spent the rest of the afternoon sleeping like a tired  black dog. We had a little dip in the pool before heading off to dinner  downtown. We ate outside, the odor of the bar b que wafting on the  breeze. All around us the lilting accent of the south of France, le  Midi. Here the people talk like the cicadas sing. We played at midnight,  the responsive crowd making up for all of the shit we had to go through  to get there. While we were pulling out, Otis Taylor was beginning his  set. Traveling blues.</p>
<p>14 July. Rather than climbing back on board the  one-bunk-bus-from-hell, we bade the driver fare thee well and made other  arrangements. The driver became very friendly of a sudden, wishing us a  safe trip and apologizing much too profusely to be sincere. Ass hole.  After a short night in a real bed with sheets and a pillow, we headed to  Avignon to catch the TGV. Us and half of the population of Europe. Otis  Taylor and his group as well, looking very much like strangers in a  strange land. We took them under our wing and guided them through the  quick sand of the train station. The TGV pulled in, staying only a few  short minutes before pulling out again like the proverbial bat out of  hell. With our large quantity of large cases we were at a slight  disadvantage amidst the aggressive train travelers. Parisians on their  way back home. Of all of the behaviorial traits of the French, the most  aggravating is the general lack of discipline and civility whenever  waiting on line. For most Frenchmen and women, a queue does not inspire  patience or respect for those that have arrived earlier, but an  irresistible desire to cut in. As soon as there is enough space to stick  in an elbow or a knee, the average Frenchman will wade in with abandon,  smirking gleefully if he or she is able to manage to get in front of  somebody else. Lines in banks or at the cinema or anywhere else for that  matter are always a pain for me, conditioned, as are most Americans, to  appreciate a certain amount of space with which to surround my person .  In spite of the pushing and pulling, however, we were able to get  aboard with all of our gear, occupying the last remaining centimeters on  the train. In the next car, i could see Otis Taylor and his band, swept  along the human tide, their eyes wide with panic. &ldquo;We ain&rsquo;t in Colorado  any more, Otis&rdquo; I heard someone call. It was the last I ever saw of  them.</p>
<p>Once arrived at the Gare de Lyon in Pairs, we  transferred to another bus, direction Orl&eacute;ans. With just enough time for  a quick shower nearby, we made the downbeat at 7PM. Before we hit, a  parade band (fanfare) had been playing in the street. Wearing colorful  shirts and bouncing to the music in glee, the band was great fun. On the  big bass drum, however, a printed message played a sour note.</p>
<p>&ldquo;Endangered species of musician&rdquo; it said. From the  beginning of this tour, we had encountered the &ldquo;intermittent&rsquo;s&rdquo; strike,  the strike of occasion performance art workers. Everywhere we had  played, the concerts were threatened with cancellation. In several  places, the strikers had been able to read tracts before or after the  performance. At the New Morning, they blocked the front door, in a foul  mood, refusing to look me in the eye as I squeezed past. At first I had  but little sympathy for the hard core strikers who had brought down  several of France&rsquo;s most established festivals, Aix, Avignon and the  Francofolies of La Rochelle. I had watched my friend Jean-Louis  Foulquier, the president of the festival, nearly in tears, in a  television interview castigating the strikers union. After nearly twenty  years, the Francofolies may never be held again, a blow to the economy  of La Rochelle and to the hundreds if not thousands of people who depend  on the festival. But as with many social questions, the problem is  complex. Finally, I came to the conclusion, the same as that proposed by  the strikers, that the bad guy is the government. The abuses of the  system are well known: film production studios who declare only a part  of the work days of the &ldquo;occasional workers&rdquo;, the balance of their time  paid for by unemployment insurance, the ASSEDIC, or the stars of French  cinema who are eligible for unemployment insurance once they have  finished a project, in spite of their astronomical fees, Etc. etc.. It  was evident from the start of the system in the 70s that there was  potential for abuse. To understand the mentality involved you just need  to try to jump aboard the TGV in Avignon on July 14, i.e. it&rsquo;s every man  woman for him or herself. None the less, the thinking behind the plan  is good. In order to allow a class of performance artists and  technicians to pursue their craft, and due to the occasional nature of  the work, a safety net of unemployment insurance was created. By  achieving a set minimum of hours employed, the worker in question could  continue to ply his or her craft with the relative assurance of being  able to make a living. The general culture of France would therefore  benefit from a class of workers who otherwise would not be able to make  ends meet. Unfortunately, the system was corrupted, and not by the  people it was designed to help, but by the big production houses which  include French national television itself. The government has chosen to  reduce the amount of benefits available, penalizing the least affluent  workers while leaving in place the potential for abuse inherent in the  system. Simply put, the government does not have to political courage to  take on the big producers, and so will penalize the smallest of the  small. Nobody knows what will happen. With a summer festival season  sabotaged by the unions, the general public and the government are  seemingly insensitive to the plight of the rank and file performance  artists and technicians. The future of well established festivals like  the Francofolies of La Rochelle is in question. None the less, the  concert of French rock god and Elvis wannabee, Johnny Hallyday, attended  by French president Jacques Chirac and his wife, went on without any  trouble , thanks to a healthy deployment of CRS (National police goons)  who kept the strikers at bay. The future of the parade band in the  streets of Orl&eacute;ans is another story.</p>
<p>I had plenty of time to mull over these and other  critical social questions on the way back from Orl&eacute;ans to Paris. The  regular one and one half hour ride turned into a mega marathon, caught  as we were in the 14 of July national holiday traffic jam. What better  way to spend the national holiday than stuck in traffic until 2AM. In  spite of all of that time to ponder, I was none the less unable to  figure out whether France will in fact be able to reconcile its social  ideals with the conflicting interests of the various social classes of  its population. Sounds like it could be just about anywhere. Stay tuned.  Vive la France</p> <p>6  juillet, Vienne. Le festival de Jazz de Vienne se passe dans   l&rsquo;amphith&eacute;&acirc;tre romain. C&rsquo;est tr&egrave;s impressionnant de voir ces gradins en   pierre qui dominent la sc&egrave;ne et de penser qu&rsquo;ils &eacute;taient l&agrave; il y a des   si&egrave;cles et des si&egrave;cles. Comme c&rsquo;&eacute;tait le premier spectacle de la   tourn&eacute;e, nous avons eu quelques probl&egrave;mes techniques, mais le tout   s&rsquo;est d&eacute;roul&eacute; assez bien. Comme c&rsquo;&eacute;tait une soir&eacute;e dite louisianaise,   j&rsquo;ai pu rencontrer plusieurs personnes de mon pays. Il y avait une   d&eacute;l&eacute;gation du D&eacute;partement de tourisme, venu pour r&eacute;pandre la bonne   parole, parmi laquelle se trouvait le chef de cuisine, Dwight   Landreneau. Le chef m&rsquo;a confi&eacute; quelques boites d&rsquo;&eacute;pices qu&rsquo;il avait   soigneusement prot&eacute;g&eacute;es pendant son voyage. Cela m&rsquo;a fait un grand   plaisir, mais la rencontre qui m&rsquo;a le plus touch&eacute; fut celle que j&rsquo;ai   eue avec mon ami batteur Rick S&eacute;bastien. Rick et moi avons jou&eacute;   ensemble voil&agrave; plus de vingt ans. Il est originalement de Lafayette,   mais il habite depuis des ann&eacute;es &agrave; New York. Ce jour-l&agrave;, il jouait avec   Los Hombre Calientes, un groupe de Nouvelle-Orl&eacute;ans qui s&rsquo;inspire des   traditions afro-caribiennes, autant de New Orleans que de Cuba et du   Br&eacute;sil. Il &eacute;tait tr&egrave;s chic dans son habit de jazz-man. Il souffre d&rsquo;un   d&eacute;garnissement crini&egrave;rdesque (perte de cheveux&mdash;&agrave; l&rsquo;&eacute;poque qu&rsquo;on   travaillait ensemble, il portait une coupe de cheveux genre buisson   d&rsquo;azal&eacute;e), mais autrement il se porte tr&egrave;s bien. C&rsquo;&eacute;tait une belle   retrouvaille. J&rsquo;ai &eacute;t&eacute; tr&egrave;s heureux de voir Nicole Boudreaux aussi.   Nicole est une louisianaise d&rsquo;adoption, en visite dans son pays   d&rsquo;origine. Elle est pr&eacute;sidente du consortium des programmes d&rsquo;immersion   fran&ccedil;aise en Louisiane et elle occupe un poste tr&egrave;s important charg&eacute; de   la coordination entre les divers programmes d&rsquo;immersion fran&ccedil;aise.  Elle  m&rsquo;a appris la triste nouvelle que Richard Guidry prend sa  retraite.  Richard s&rsquo;occupait des &eacute;trangers (Belges, Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois,  Acadiens,  Fran&ccedil;ais, Antillais et Africains) enseignant dans les  programmes  d&rsquo;immersion fran&ccedil;aise et espagnole au D&eacute;partement de  l&rsquo;Education de la  Louisiane. Ayant eu une carri&egrave;re de plus de trente  ans d&eacute;vou&eacute;e &agrave;  l&rsquo;&eacute;ducation des jeunes louisianais et &agrave; la langue  fran&ccedil;aise, il a  d&eacute;cid&eacute; de passer le flambeau. Bien qu&rsquo;il va nous  manquer beaucoup, on  lui souhaite beaucoup de chance dans ses nouvelles  aventures. Pour ce  qui est de notre aventure, la partie viennoise a  fini dans la loge en  dessous de l&rsquo;ancien th&eacute;&acirc;tre romain, avec des  bisous pour tous nos vieux  amis, avec qui j&rsquo;ai pu partager un petit  moment sympathique.<br /> <br /> 7 juillet. Nous sommes partis de l&rsquo;h&ocirc;tel vers 9h du  matin pour se jeter  au beau milieu d&rsquo;un embouteillage p&eacute;nible sur  l&rsquo;autoroute. Apr&egrave;s un  p&eacute;riple de d&eacute;mon, coupant &agrave; travers les ruelles  de la ville sur les  chapeaux des roues, nous avons gagn&eacute; la gare de  Lyon en manque  d&rsquo;haleine. Arriv&eacute;s de justesse avec notre &eacute;quipement sur  les bras,  apr&egrave;s un sprint surexcit&eacute;, nous nous sommes install&eacute;s  confortablement  dans le TGV direction Paris, gare de Lyon. J&rsquo;aime  beaucoup le voyage en  train, le bruit hypnotisant des roues frappant  les rails, le paysage  qu&rsquo;on ne pourrait voir autrement, et l&rsquo;impression  d&rsquo;&ecirc;tre d&eacute;tach&eacute; du  monde dans une esp&egrave;ce d&rsquo;&eacute;loignement d&rsquo;espace et de  temps. En plus on  mange assez bien au bord les TGVs. Regardant les  collines couvertes de  bl&eacute; et d&rsquo;orge, les tiges dor&eacute;es ondulant  doucement, avec des petites  maisons en pierre distribu&eacute;es comme des  virgules au milieu de phrases  chuchot&eacute;es, je somnolais dans un &eacute;tat  r&ecirc;veur. Arriv&eacute; &agrave; Paris, le r&ecirc;ve  fut rompu. Descendu du train, comme  projet&eacute;s sous une douche de bruit  et d&rsquo;agitation, tra&icirc;nant toujours  notre quantit&eacute; de bagages, nous nous  sommes dirig&eacute;s vers le New  Morning. Cach&eacute; dans les tripes de Paris, au  c&oelig;ur d&rsquo;un quartier assez  folklorique, le New Morning est &laquo; le &raquo;  show-club de la ville. Mais  comme tous les show-clubs de toutes les  villes, il est d&rsquo;aspect assez  d&eacute;labr&eacute;. Surtout dans la loge. Mais j&rsquo;en  ai vu pires. Le syst&egrave;me de  son, cependant, est excellent. Avec  l&rsquo;assurance gagn&eacute;e la veille, moi  et mes coll&egrave;gues musiciens, nous  avons droit &agrave; un beau spectacle bien  re&ccedil;u. <br /> <br /> 8 juillet. Avec toute l&rsquo;excitation de la soir&eacute;e, il  &eacute;tait impossible de  s&rsquo;endormir avant les petites heures du matin. Ce  qui a fait un r&eacute;veil  difficile. Le taxi &eacute;tait tr&egrave;s en retard ce qui  nous a fait un autre  voyage &agrave; l&rsquo;a&eacute;roport assez stressant. Bienvenue on  the road. Arriv&eacute; &agrave;  Roissy avec autant de bagages que la veille, nous ne  pouvons pas nous  reposer qu&rsquo;une fois dans l&rsquo;avion. D&eacute;j&agrave; on &eacute;tait en  Italie. Le personnel  de cabine avec leurs nez romains et leur style  gracieux, leurs gestes  extravagants et leurs dents tr&egrave;s blanches,  installait l&rsquo;ambiance. On ne  parlait que l&rsquo;Italien &agrave; part le pilote qui  s&rsquo;acharnait &agrave; nous expliquer  tout en trois langues totalement  incompr&eacute;hensibles pour moi :  l&rsquo;italien, le fran&ccedil;ais d&rsquo;avion, et  l&rsquo;anglais d&rsquo;avion. Quel plaisir  cette culture latine. Arriv&eacute; &agrave; Napoli,  nous &eacute;tions accueillis par  Tomaso et ses deux coll&egrave;gues, tous les trois  avec leurs t-shirts noirs  Festival de Blues del Liri. Isola del Liri  est un petit village &agrave;  mi-chemin entre Rome et Naples. Perch&eacute; aux  flancs des montagnes &agrave;  l&rsquo;int&eacute;rieur des terres, il est connu pour sa  petite rivi&egrave;re (Liri) qui  coule &agrave; travers son c&oelig;ur, et une petite &icirc;le  qui se trouve en plein  milieu (Isola) qui sert d&rsquo;habitation &agrave; plusieurs  oies aux plumes  hirsutes. Vu la nuit charg&eacute;e que nous avons connue,  nous souhaitons  passer &agrave; l&rsquo;h&ocirc;tel pour nous reposer un peu. Mais d&rsquo;abord  il fallait  mangare. Nous sommes arr&ecirc;t&eacute;s au bord de la route dans un de  ses  magnifiques restaurants &agrave; l&rsquo;aspect indiff&eacute;rent qui pars&egrave;me le  paysage  comme autant de oasis d&eacute;labr&eacute;es et qui servent une nourriture  simple et  d&eacute;licieuse. Bonheur. Et le caf&eacute;. C&rsquo;est un grand myst&egrave;re, mais  tout  voyageur amateur de caf&eacute; qui a goutt&eacute; un espresso en Italie le   confirmera. Il n&rsquo;y a rien de tel. Je ne sais pas &agrave; quoi c&rsquo;est d&ucirc;. La   pression vapeur de la machine, la moulure du caf&eacute;, la qualit&eacute; du caf&eacute;   etc. sont facilement r&eacute;produisable ailleurs, mais nulle part ailleurs   on peut trouver un caf&eacute; aussi somptueux qu&rsquo;on trouve dans n&rsquo;importe   quel bistro pitoyable d&rsquo;Italie. J&rsquo;aurais pass&eacute; mon apr&egrave;s-midi &agrave; boire   du caf&eacute; et &agrave; &eacute;couter parler les gens, mais je me suis retenu &agrave; deux,   histoire de rester s&eacute;rieux. <br /> Pendant la sieste est arriv&eacute; un orage magnifique. Le  tonnerre r&eacute;sonnait  autour comme si les montagnes grognaient aux voix  basso profondos. Et  la pluie tombait en cordes. Cette pluie abondante  et continuelle  faisant le bonheur des agriculteurs, mais faisant aussi  le chagrin des  organisateurs de festivals. Le festival de Blues d&rsquo;Isola  del Liri est  un &eacute;v&eacute;nement culturel tr&egrave;s sp&eacute;cial. C&rsquo;est un des rares  sinon le seul  festival important en Italie qui est gratuit pour le  public. Ce qui  fait que ce festival est un &eacute;v&eacute;nement qui touche la  soci&eacute;t&eacute; locale au  complet. De voir Tomaso et ses coll&egrave;gues regardant la  pluie  torrentielle, se tordant les mains comme seuls les Italiens  peuvent le  faire, je sentais leur angoisse. Finalement nous avons  d&eacute;cid&eacute; de  descendre sur le site. Bien qu&rsquo;il y ait un toit, les planches  de la  sc&egrave;ne &eacute;taient compl&egrave;tement mouill&eacute;es. L&rsquo;&eacute;quipement &eacute;tait cach&eacute;  sous des  feuilles de plastique noires de chagrin. Les techniciens se  tenaient &agrave;  l&rsquo;&eacute;cart sous un bout de toit qui leur donnait un peu d&rsquo;abri.  Ils  avaient les mains coll&eacute;es aux c&ocirc;tes. Et comme tout Italien qui ne   gesticule pas, ils avaient l&rsquo;air bien triste dans leurs imperm&eacute;ables de   fortune. Sachant qu&rsquo;il n&rsquo;y avait rien &agrave; faire, nous sommes parti faire   le tour du village. Pendant notre promenade, le soleil est sorti en  bon  augure. Cach&eacute; dans le labyrinthe du centre ville, on a trouv&eacute; une   petite trattoria. Spaghetti al pomodoro, pollo paillarde, tira misu.   Bonheur. <br /> <br /> Finalement la sc&egrave;ne a s&eacute;ch&eacute; suffisamment pour que les  techniciens  puissent faire l&rsquo;installation. Bien que nous n&rsquo;ayons pas  suffisamment  de temps pour faire une balance, le spectacle a pu  commencer presque &agrave;  l&rsquo;heure, vers onze heures du soir. Gr&acirc;ce &agrave; une  &eacute;quipe technique  familiale, de p&egrave;re (Mario) et fils (Manuel) on a  profit&eacute; d&rsquo;un son assez  agr&eacute;able. La place &eacute;tait pleine d&rsquo;Italiens &agrave; un  tel point qu&rsquo;ils  risquaient de d&eacute;border la cl&ocirc;ture et tomber dans la  rivi&egrave;re. Le tout  Isola y assistait, dansant dans un style retenu sur  les airs de ma  Louisiane. <br /> <br /> 12 juillet. Apr&egrave;s un retour sur Paris, et deux jours de  repos, nous  sommes partis au Sud. Vers 1 heure du matin, on avait  rendez-vous avec  le bus qui devait nous transporter. Catastrophe. Au  lieu du bus que  nous avons command&eacute;, avec couchettes et draps et  oreillers, &agrave; la place  nous avons trouv&eacute; un autobus de tourisme avec  bancs, sans couchettes,  sans draps et sans oreillers. Par contre, les  bancs se pliaient pour  faire une esp&egrave;ce de banquette de torture  caboss&eacute;e, certain de casser le  dos des plus insensibles. En Europe, &agrave;  cause des r&egrave;glements concernant  le feu, il est interdit d&rsquo;avoir des  s&eacute;parations comme on trouve dans  les &laquo; touring bus &raquo; aux USA. Cela dit,  on trouve des autobus &agrave; deux  &eacute;tages avec un &eacute;tage consacr&eacute; aux  couchettes, ce qui fait un moyen de  transport assez agr&eacute;able. Par  contre, nous &eacute;tions confront&eacute;s &agrave; autre  chose. &Eacute;videmment, la compagnie  de transport avait lou&eacute; notre bus &agrave; un  client qui allait le prendre  pour une p&eacute;riode plus longue, pensant  qu&rsquo;en faisant ainsi nous ne  pouvions rien y faire. Le chauffeur  insistait d&rsquo;appeler la banquette de  torture une &laquo; couchette &raquo;,  s&rsquo;obstinant avec nous. De toute fa&ccedil;on, nous  n&rsquo;avons peu de recours au  milieu de cette nuit au milieu de la p&eacute;riode  la plus courue de l&rsquo;ann&eacute;e.  Ce qui fait que nous avons pass&eacute; une nuit  assez d&eacute;sagr&eacute;able. Une fois  rendu &agrave; Bagnols, malgr&eacute; les assurances  donn&eacute;es par t&eacute;l&eacute;phone, le  personnel de l&rsquo;h&ocirc;tel refusait de nous laisser  occuper les chambres  avant l&rsquo;apr&egrave;s-midi. En plus le chauffeur s&rsquo;est  r&eacute;v&eacute;l&eacute; un trou du cul,  insistant qu&rsquo;on d&eacute;charge tout l&rsquo;&eacute;quipement pour  ne pas le d&eacute;ranger plus  tard. Alors on s&rsquo;est trouv&eacute; devant l&rsquo;h&ocirc;tel  apr&egrave;s une nuit p&eacute;nible,  assis sur les caisses de notre &eacute;quipement,  &eacute;coutant les cigales  chanter, isol&eacute; de la ville dans cet h&ocirc;tel sans  restaurant. Bienvenue on  the road. Heureusement le cadre &eacute;tait fort  joli, au milieu d&rsquo;un petit  bois charmant, et les cigales chantaient  assez bien. Finalement nous  avons pu gagner nos chambres apr&egrave;s un  d&eacute;jeuner de pizza dans le  restaurant du fr&egrave;re d&rsquo;un des organisateurs  qui a accept&eacute; de nous servir  bien que son restaurant soit complet ce  dimanche midi. J&rsquo;ai pass&eacute;  l&rsquo;apr&egrave;s-midi &agrave; dormir comme un voyageur ayant  trop voyag&eacute;. Nous avons  soup&eacute; centre ville en plein air, l&rsquo;odeur du  barbeque saturant l&rsquo;air de  cette petite ville du Sud. Autour de nous,  l&rsquo;accent chantant du Midi.  Ici les gens parlent au rythme des cigales.  C&rsquo;&eacute;tait une autre soir&eacute;e  tardive. Nous n&rsquo;avons pas jou&eacute; avant minuit,  mais notre peine fut  soulag&eacute;e par l&rsquo;enthousiasme du public. Nous sommes  partis pendant que  le groupe d&rsquo;Otis Taylor commen&ccedil;ait leur prestation.  Blues du voyageur.<br /> <br /> 14 juillet. Plut&ocirc;t que de remonter dans l&rsquo;autobus  d&rsquo;enfer, nous avons  cong&eacute;di&eacute; le chauffeur, qui du coup feignait une  courtoisie bien trop  exag&eacute;r&eacute;e pour &ecirc;tre vrai. Apr&egrave;s une courte nuit  pass&eacute;e dans un lit avec  draps et oreillers, nous avons pris le chemin  d&rsquo;Avignon et sa gare de  TGV. Nous et la moiti&eacute; de la population  d&rsquo;Europe. Les musiciens d&rsquo;Otis  Taylor &eacute;taient l&agrave; aussi, perdus comme  des touristes am&eacute;ricains. Nous  les avons pris sous l&rsquo;aile, les guidant &agrave;  travers les sables mouvants  de la gare d&rsquo;Avignon. Le moment de monter &agrave;  bord &eacute;tait tr&egrave;s  folklorique. Avec notre quantit&eacute; de bagages grand  gabarit nous &eacute;tions  mal pris au milieu de cette foule impatiente. Des  Parisiens en retour  de vacance. De tous les comportements culturels que  l&rsquo;on peut  consid&eacute;rer comme &eacute;tant caract&eacute;ristiques des Fran&ccedil;ais, le  plus  insupportable est le manque de discipline voire gentillesse lors  d&rsquo;une  attente en queue. Pour beaucoup de Fran&ccedil;ais, une queue d&rsquo;attente   inspire ni la patience, ni le respect de ceux et celles qui sont   arriv&eacute;s en premier, mais plut&ocirc;t le d&eacute;sir de couper devant tout le   monde. D&egrave;s qu&rsquo;il y a un espace suffisant pour laisser p&eacute;n&eacute;trer un coude   ou un genoux, le Fran&ccedil;ais va tenter de s&rsquo;y introduire. Ce qui est tr&egrave;s   choquant pour des Am&eacute;ricains comme moi, habitu&eacute; &agrave; garder un espace bien   &eacute;tabli autour de sa personne. Ce qui fait que les queues de banque ou   de cin&eacute;ma o&ugrave; de n&rsquo;importe quoi sont souvent tr&egrave;s p&eacute;nibles Surtout quand   on est charg&eacute; d&rsquo;un surplus consid&eacute;rable de bagages grand gabarit.   N&eacute;anmoins, nous avons r&eacute;ussi &agrave; monter &agrave; bord, occupant les derniers   centim&egrave;tres disponibles. Dans la voiture devant, je voyais les regards   paniqu&eacute;s des musiciens d&rsquo;Otis Taylor, propuls&eacute;s dans cette mar&eacute;e   humaine comme au bord d&rsquo;un bateau &agrave; la d&eacute;rive. <br /> Une fois arriv&eacute; &agrave; la gare de Lyon, nous sommes mont&eacute;s  dans un autre  autocar, direction Orl&eacute;ans. Sans temps pour une balance  de son, avec  seulement le temps d&rsquo;une douche rapide dans l&rsquo;h&ocirc;tel &agrave;  c&ocirc;t&eacute;, on a d&eacute;but&eacute;  le spectacle &agrave; 7 heures du soir. Avant nous, une  fanfare jouait dans la  rue. Sur le gros tambour &eacute;tait affich&eacute; un mot  amer, &laquo; Musicien en voie  de disparition &raquo;. Habill&eacute;s en chemises  color&eacute;es, faisant une  chor&eacute;graphie &eacute;nergique et une musique chaude, ils  proclamaient leur  m&eacute;contentement d&rsquo;une fa&ccedil;on discr&egrave;te. Depuis le d&eacute;but  de cette petite  tourn&eacute;e, nous avons &eacute;t&eacute; confront&eacute;s &agrave; la gr&egrave;ve des  intermittents du  spectacle. Partout o&ugrave; nous jouons, il y avait eu  menace d&rsquo;annulation et  ambiance g&ecirc;n&eacute;e. Dans plusieurs endroits, les  intermittents avaient  r&eacute;ussi &agrave; pr&eacute;senter un texte avant le spectacle.  Au New Morning, ils  attendaient dehors sous leurs pancartes, sans  conviction, sans me  regarder quand je suis entr&eacute;. Au premier abord  j&rsquo;avais peu de sympathie  pour ces purs et durs qui n&rsquo;h&eacute;sitaient pas &agrave;  foutre en l&rsquo;air des  festivals &eacute;tablis telle Aix ou Avignon et les  Francofolies de La  Rochelle, tra&icirc;nant &agrave; la d&eacute;rive des centaines sinon  des milliers de gens  qui en d&eacute;pendent. Mais comme toute question  sociale, la r&eacute;alit&eacute; s&rsquo;av&egrave;re  plus complexe. Finalement je crois que le  vilain dans cette situation  est le gouvernement. Les abus de ce syst&egrave;me  sont connus : maisons de  productions de film et de t&eacute;l&eacute;vision y  compris la t&eacute;l&eacute;vision de l&rsquo;Etat  qui profite du syst&egrave;me pour faire payer  une partie des salaires de  leurs employ&eacute;es, en les consid&eacute;rant &laquo;  intermittents &raquo; bien qu&rsquo;ils aient  travaill&eacute; &agrave; plein temps et depuis  longtemps aussi. Les vedettes du  cin&eacute;ma qui re&ccedil;oivent l&rsquo;ASSEDIC, une  fois qu&rsquo;un tournage est termin&eacute;,  malgr&eacute; leurs revenus personnels  consid&eacute;rables. Etc. etc.<br /> C&rsquo;est &eacute;vident qu&rsquo;il allait y avoir des abus. Pour  comprendre la  mentalit&eacute; d&rsquo;une partie des gens concern&eacute;s, il s&rsquo;agit  d&rsquo;assister au  d&eacute;part du TGV de la gare d&rsquo;Avignon un 13 juillet. Mais il  est aussi  certain que le concept de base est bon : de donner une  chance &agrave; une  partie de la communaut&eacute; artistique de se r&eacute;aliser en leur  assurant  suffisamment de revenu pour rejoindre les deux bouts et de  continuer &agrave;  pratiquer leur art dans le but d&rsquo;enrichir la culture  commune de la  France. Malheureusement le syst&egrave;me a &eacute;t&eacute; corrompu et non  pas par les  plus petits, mais par les plus grands. Plut&ocirc;t que de  s&rsquo;adresser aux  fraudes et de confronter les abus scandaleux des maisons  de production,  le gouvernement a choisi d&rsquo;attaquer les plus petits en  r&eacute;duisant les  subventions, en laissant en place toutes les possibilit&eacute;s  d&rsquo;abus. Ce  qui &eacute;tait une superbe id&eacute;e : de soutenir toute une classe  d&rsquo;artistes et  d&rsquo;ouvriers du spectacle, a finalement d&eacute;riv&eacute; vers un  syst&egrave;me corrompu  qui sert surtout les grandes maisons de production. En  face des  d&eacute;ficits de plus en plus importants, le gouvernement a d&eacute;cid&eacute;   d&rsquo;attaquer les plus petits. Ce qui indique son manque de courage. On  ne  sait pas ce qui va se passer. Cet &eacute;t&eacute; a &eacute;t&eacute; marqu&eacute; par des   confrontations difficiles qui ont troubl&eacute; tout le paysage culturel de   la France. Le public comme le gouvernement semble peu sensible au sort   des petits intermittents. Plusieurs grands festivals ont &eacute;t&eacute; annul&eacute;s et   pour plusieurs, comme celui de La Rochelle, la survie para&icirc;t   incertaine. N&eacute;anmoins le spectacle de Johnny Hallyday auquel ont   assist&eacute; le pr&eacute;sident de la R&eacute;publique et sa femme a pu se d&eacute;rouler dans   le calme gr&acirc;ce &agrave; un dispositif important de CRS qui gardait les   intermittents tr&egrave;s &agrave; l &lsquo;&eacute;cart. En partant d&rsquo;Orl&eacute;ans, je me demandais si   cette fanfare enivrante survivra. <br /> <br /> J&rsquo;avais beaucoup de temps de penser &agrave; cela pendant le  retour sur Paris.  Nous &eacute;tions emprisonn&eacute;s dans l&rsquo;embouteillage  monstrueux du 14 juillet.  Cela me permettait une r&eacute;flexion sur le fond  de la question,  c&rsquo;est-&agrave;-dire si la France sera capable de r&eacute;concilier  ses belles id&eacute;es  socialistes avec les divers int&eacute;r&ecirc;ts de tous ses  citoyens et une  bureaucratie engloutie dans un marasme d&rsquo;inefficacit&eacute;. &Agrave;  suivre. Vive  la France.</p> 2003-07-30 00:00:00
95 y <p>On board the French airliner hurrying us to Paris, voil&agrave; the usual  semi-lingual blah blah. Following his welcoming announcement explaining  flight time and weather conditions, the pilot presented us ostensibly  the same message, but in a sort of pidgin English totally  incomprehensible. &ldquo;Lads un gin, hi tell zoo zat info am shogunaux sank  you ver mush.&rdquo; During the jet lag induced insomnia of my first night in  France, I discovered the latest realit&eacute;-show. Something called &ldquo;Nice  People&rdquo;. A collection of losers with nothing better to do with their  lives are all bunched together in a &ldquo;nice house&rdquo;. Every week, the  television audience calls in to vote for their favorite &ldquo;nice people&rdquo;,  and the &ldquo;nice People&rdquo; with the least amount of votes has to leave the  &ldquo;nice house&rdquo; and go back to his or her idiotic life. Given the amount of  times that the announcerette uses the term &ldquo;Nice People&rdquo; (pronounced  Naz Pee Pole) the phrase is surely destined to become part of the daily  lexicon and will most likely be in the dictionary in a few years. Once,  that is, that the Acad&eacute;mie Fran&ccedil;aise has approved it. Imagine the scene  as the fifty or so very old farts in their brocade jackets discuss ad  infinitum the real meaning of &ldquo;Nice People&rdquo;. In this particular context,  the phrase does not mean what it would seem to, but can be loosely  translated as, &ldquo;Butt hole with nothing to do in life, but who none the  less winds up on national television acting the ass in front of millions  who have even less going for them and spend their time watching stupid  reality shows and phoning in to vote for their favorite nobody.&rdquo; The  wave of anti-american sentiment has apparently not reached the popular  lexicon, nor popular television. Nor the flight decks of French  airlines.</p>
<p>Paris herself is unchanged. And this to my great  satisfaction. The people in the street are as stressed and impatient as  ever, but with the latest wave of general strikes recently terminated,  there is a sense of d&eacute;tente in the air. Recently, the whole country was  paralyzed by a mean series of strikes. Bad, but according to my sources,  not as bad as &lsquo;95. I was in the middle of the strikes of 1995. During  the autumn of that year, I was recording the album Cap Enrag&eacute;. The  studio was in a little town north of Paris, La Frette, about 45 minutes  drive. But during the strikes, the 45 minutes quickly became 2 or 3 or  even 4 hours. At the beginning I would pick up every hitch hiker  (auto-stoppeur) that I found. There were so many people stranded without  public transport, just hard working people trying to muddle through the  mess. At first I would converse with them. Later on, I stopped talking  to them, and finally I stopped picking them up at all. The conversation  was always the same, and always as absurd. We always talked about the  same thing: the strike. And they always said the same thing, expressing a  blind and unconditional support of the strike and the strikers who were  so obviously turning their lives upside down. Everybody blamed the  government. Ever since the French Revolution, the French have replaced  the king with the government. Which is to say that the people expect  from the government what they expected from the king: somebody to solve  all of the problems of society and to make life better for all. With  this attitude comes the assumption that one can reap havoc in the world  at any time that one is not pleased with the situation. This time the  fuss is over the question of retirement. With the aging of the general  population, life expectancy continuing to increase, the pension funds of  the government are not longer sufficient to feed everybody they are  supposed to. The government has therefore proposed to extend the  retirement age to make up for the shortfall. (In France the work week is  currently 35 hours). Evidently the governments proposed solution was  not acceptable. In 1995, the strike question was very similar. It all  started with the railroad workers. Out of sympathy, the entire public  sector went on strike, government workers having the right to strike in  France. In spite of the ensuing mess, the general public supported the  strike all the way, at least according to my very unofficial hitch hiker  poll. Everybody was obliged to get up hours earlier than usual in order  to walk to work, in spite of which I never heard any criticism of the  strikers. All of the public ire was directed at the government. In fact  there was often a light hearted ambiance in the street, or at least a  more humane aspect to daily life, much like that one finds during a  natural disaster. The strike was perceived much like a hurricane or a  flood, more like an act of God than the decision of a few people. The  bad guy was the government. That there was more emotion than rational  thought in this attitude never seemed to dawn on anybody at the time  except me. Down with the government. Down with the king.</p>
<p>I am not sure what to think. I am sympathetic to the  cause of the working man. And yet, the phenomenon of the work strike in  France seems more like a caricature of what it is meant to be.  Everybody&rsquo;s lives are turned upside for a few days or even weeks, but  nothing much seems to change. The government will put its proposal in  place and everybody will adapt and get on with their lives. At least the  strike allows some people to express their anger. In a very real way,  the strikes bring people together. Having to cope with the near  impossibility of simply getting from one place to the next, people are  obliged to look at their lives in a very different way, and to  reevaluate just what is important to them. There is a strike currently  looming in the entertainment sector. The technical unions associated  with the concert business are threatening to walk out. Several large  festivals have been canceled. I am sure that the strikers have a valid  point, but it is the concert going public and the artists who will  suffer. For the time being, none of my shows have been canceled. Vive la  France.</p>
<p>None of this really disturbs me. I am used to it by  now. A shrug of the shoulders and get on with it. The surly attitude of  Parisian drivers and the ever impending transportation strike are part  of the folklore of France. Like wine and cheese. Paris remains a  beautiful town, perhaps the most beautiful city in the world. Walking  along the Seine with the summer light shining on the facades of the  beige stone buildings, the Eiffel tower piercing the bright blue sky,  one is part of a living post card. The city is irresistible. Even the  Parisians, with all of their stress and their never ending street  squabbling, are ever ready to share a smile and a tender moment. I love  this town and its crazy people, their pushing and pulling and yelling  and screaming, their foibles and their charm and their feelings strong  like old cheese. Strong like cognac.</p>
<p>Vive la France. Vive Paris. Down with the king.</p> <p>A  bord de l&rsquo;avion fran&ccedil;ais qui nous emmenait &agrave; Paris, nous &eacute;tions  sujets  au m&ecirc;me babillage. Suite &agrave; son annonce habituelle, le pilote a  fait la  m&ecirc;me annonce dans une esp&egrave;ce de semblant d&rsquo;anglais totalement   incompr&eacute;hensible. &laquo;&nbsp;Lads et gen hi tell you zis zafo ma shogunaux sank   you ver mush.&nbsp;&raquo; En ouvrant la t&eacute;l&eacute;vision la nuit dans mon insomnie   d&eacute;calage-horaire, je d&eacute;couvre le dernier &laquo;&nbsp;r&eacute;alit&eacute; show&nbsp;&raquo; qui fait   fureur&nbsp;: &laquo;&nbsp;Nice People&nbsp;&raquo;. Il s&rsquo;agit de plusieurs pauvres cons qui n&rsquo;ont   a rien &agrave; faire dans la vie et qui se trouvent dans une maison &agrave; vivre   ensemble et &agrave; jouer des jeux compl&egrave;tement d&eacute;biles. Toutes les semaines,   le public t&eacute;l&eacute;phone pour voter pour leur &laquo;&nbsp;nice people&nbsp;&raquo; pr&eacute;f&eacute;r&eacute;. La pr&eacute;sentatrice utilise cette nouvelle   phrase emprunt&eacute;e &agrave; l&rsquo;anglais et destin&eacute;e bient&ocirc;t au Petit Robert. &laquo;&nbsp;Ils   font nice people&nbsp;&raquo;, elle dit. &laquo;&nbsp;Voil&agrave; les nice people&nbsp;&raquo;. &laquo;&nbsp;Ils font   nice people&nbsp;&raquo;, prononc&eacute; dans un accent tr&egrave;s fran&ccedil;ais, genre &laquo;&nbsp;naz   piepo&nbsp;&raquo;. Ce qui ne veut pas dire &laquo;&nbsp;gens gentils&nbsp;&raquo; telle une traduction   plus stricte, mais qui se traduit dans ce contexte par, &laquo;&nbsp;&nbsp;genre de con   qui ne fait rien dans la vie et n&rsquo;a pas de qualit&eacute; particuli&egrave;re ni de   talent visible, mais qui arrive &agrave; solliciter le plus de voix   t&eacute;l&eacute;phoniques de la part d&rsquo;un public encore plus d&eacute;bile qui a encore   moins &agrave; faire dans la vie.&nbsp;&laquo;&nbsp;&nbsp; La vague anti-am&eacute;ricaine n&rsquo;est pas   arriv&eacute;e jusqu&rsquo;au vocabulaire moderne de la langue fran&ccedil;aise, et encore   moins &agrave; la t&eacute;l&eacute;vision, Ni &agrave; la cabane de pilotage.<br /> <br /> Paris n&rsquo;a pas chang&eacute;, et cela &agrave; ma grande satisfaction.  Les gens sont  aussi stress&eacute;s,&nbsp;et impatients, mais, vu que la derni&egrave;re  gr&egrave;ve vient de  se terminer, il y a une sorte de d&eacute;tente qu&rsquo;on sent  bien. R&eacute;cemment, la  France a &eacute;t&eacute; paralys&eacute;e par une vague de gr&egrave;ves  g&eacute;n&eacute;rales. Elles &eacute;taient  mauvaises, mais pas aussi mauvaises que celles  de 1995. J&rsquo;ai connu les  gr&egrave;ves de 1995. &Agrave; cette &eacute;poque, j&rsquo;enregistrais  l&rsquo;album Cap Enrag&eacute;. Le  studio se trouvait &agrave; La Frette, un petit  village au Nord de Paris &agrave; 45  minutes de route environ. Mais &agrave; cause la  gr&egrave;ve des transports en  commun et l&rsquo;affluence gargantuesque qui  &eacute;tranglait des nice highways,  &ccedil;a me prenait au moins deux heures et  parfois trois ou m&ecirc;me quatre pour  y aller. Au d&eacute;but de la gr&egrave;ve, je  prenais tous les auto-stoppeurs que  je trouvais sur mon chemin, des  gens sans automobile qui &eacute;taient en  panne s&eacute;rieuse &agrave; cause de l&rsquo;absence  de transports publics. Au d&eacute;but je  leur faisais un peu la  conversation. Par la suite, j&rsquo;ai arr&ecirc;t&eacute; de leur  parler, et, &agrave; la fin,  j&rsquo;ai arr&ecirc;t&eacute; de les prendre. J&rsquo;en avais assez  d&rsquo;entendre toujours le  m&ecirc;me baratin, et finalement je pr&eacute;f&eacute;rais bouder  seul dans ma voiture.  Ce que je trouvais tr&egrave;s &eacute;trange c&rsquo;est que tous me  tenait les m&ecirc;mes  propos. Ils &eacute;taient tous solidaires avec les  gr&eacute;vistes, bien que la  gr&egrave;ve leur occasionn&acirc;t bien des tracas. Ils  reconnaissaient le droit de  tout individu de foutre la merde dans la  vie de tout le reste de la  soci&eacute;t&eacute;. Ils bl&acirc;maient le gouvernement.  Depuis la R&eacute;volution de 1789,  on a tendance &agrave; attendre du gouvernement  ce qu&rsquo;on attendait du roi.  C&rsquo;est-&agrave;-dire r&eacute;gler tous nos probl&egrave;mes et  assurer que la qualit&eacute; de vie  continue &agrave; s&rsquo;am&eacute;liorer. Avec cette fa&ccedil;on  d&rsquo;imaginer la vie sociale,  c&rsquo;est normal qu&rsquo;on pr&eacute;sume avoir le droit de  foutre la merde si le  gouvernement nous d&eacute;&ccedil;oit. Alors pour combler  le vide, le gouvernement a  propos&eacute; de prolonger le temps de travail  avant de pouvoir prendre sa  retraite. (N&rsquo;oubliez pas qu&rsquo;on ne travaille  que 35 heures par semaine  d&eacute;j&agrave;). &Eacute;videmment &ccedil;a n&rsquo;a pas plu &agrave; certains,  et voil&agrave; la gr&egrave;ve. Bien qu&rsquo;oblig&eacute;s de  partir au  travail &agrave; pied et &agrave; des heures plus t&ocirc;t que normales et de  rentrer chez  eux de la m&ecirc;me fa&ccedil;on, les Parisiens ont soutenu les  gr&eacute;vistes jusqu&rsquo;au  bout. En fait l&rsquo;ambiance dans la rue &eacute;tait plut&ocirc;t  bonne. Comme lors  d&rsquo;une catastrophe naturelle, les gens se sont mis  ensemble pour passer &agrave;  travers. Car bien que je  sois tout &agrave; fait  sympathique &agrave; la cause, je constate que finalement la  gr&egrave;ve n&rsquo;arrive  jamais &agrave; changer grand chose. Les changements propos&eacute;s  par le  gouvernement seront mis en vigueur, et les gens vont continuer  leurs  vies en s&rsquo;adaptant &agrave; la nouvelle situation. Au moins ils ont pu   exprimer leur col&egrave;re. Apparemment, la gr&egrave;ve sert surtout &agrave; &ccedil;a.   Maintenant se sont les gens du spectacle qui menacent de faire la   gr&egrave;ve, les machinistes, les &eacute;clairagistes, les r&eacute;gisseurs, etc. Je   pense que leurs revendications sont tout &agrave; fait valables, mais c&rsquo;est le   public qui va en souffrir. Et les artistes. Pour le moment je n&rsquo;ai pas   eu de spectacles annul&eacute;s. Vive la France.<br /> <br /> C&rsquo;est curieux, mais &ccedil;a ne me d&eacute;range pas. D&rsquo;une fa&ccedil;on assez r&eacute;elle, les gr&egrave;ves   obligent les gens de se serrer les coudes et de re-&eacute;valuer ce qui est   important. Paris reste une magnifique ville, peut &ecirc;tre la plus   magnifique du monde. En se promenant le long de la Seine avec la   lumi&egrave;re d&rsquo;&eacute;t&eacute; scintillant contre les fa&ccedil;ades des b&acirc;timents du temps des   rois, la tour Eiffel &agrave; l&rsquo;horizon, on se croit dans la carte postale de   r&ecirc;ve vivante. Et m&ecirc;me ces Parisiens si stress&eacute;s et si impolis sont   pr&ecirc;ts &agrave; partager un sourire et un moment de tendresse. J&rsquo;aime cette   ville et ses gens avec leurs bousculades et leurs engueulades et leurs   faiblesses, avec leur charme et leurs grands sentiments. Vive la   France. Vive Paris. A bas le roi.</p> 2003-07-02 00:00:00
96 y <p>One evening lately I was surprised to discover a small flock of  purple martins flying in place in front of one of their cages. They were  flying as they do when the fledglings are on the verge of leaving the  nest for the first time, beating their wings wildly and calling  incessantly. I made nothing of it at the time although it was weeks  before the chicks would be ready to take off. It was only two days later  that I understood what all of the ruckus was about, when I saw a large  snake sunning itself underneath the cages. It was a Texas rat snake  (Elaphe obsoleta lin&eacute;airementi), about three feet long. Just a baby. The  adults can reach over six feet in length. These snakes are very useful  as they can consume large quantities of rats and mice, but they also  have a penchant for small birds and eggs. Before I realized what was  happening, the rat snake had reduced our purple martin colony from  twelve adults to four, taking with them an unknown quantity of chicks  and eggs. He would climb up the pole in the night and corner the birds  in their cabins. I don&rsquo;t know if he was able to capture them all or  frightened away some of the birds, but the result was a population  implosion approaching catastrophic proportions.</p>
<p>I decided that I had to protect the birds at all costs,  but I was at a loss to discover how I would solve the problem. The  snake came out at night, and now that he was aware that I was on the  lookout, he would certainly become even more wary and harder to find.  Plus I did not really want to kill it. First of all the snake is  beneficial, consuming unwanted rodents. It poses no danger to humans  apart from the possibility of a nasty though otherwise harmless bite. I  am not a snake lover, but neither do I feel the revulsion which seems to  characterize many people&rsquo;s feelings about snakes. In fact it seemed  quite a handsome animal. And in any event I am loathe to kill any living  being.</p>
<p>This dilemma troubled me, not only because I had to  figure out some way to solve the problem with the least amount of pain  and suffering, but also because the situation symbolized for me the  difficult relation between man and nature. How to leave the smallest  footprint. Never the less, my mind was made up. I would protect my  purple martins at all costs. I have been nurturing the colony for many  years, taking delight in their annual return and their acrobatic  swirling as well as their babbling song. I still had no idea how I was  to accomplish the proposed eradication, but I had made up my mind to  intervene in Mother Nature&rsquo;s way.</p>
<p>The natural balance is something that mankind has  proven itself unable to respect and the consequences menace all of the  species with which we share the planet as well as our own species  itself. In a study published in England last week, the notion, so dear  to biotechnical companies, that genetically modified food will save the  third world, was refuted. The large chemical companies pretend that OGMs  will allow poor farmers to raise crops which are better suited to the  harsh conditions under which they live, allowing them to feed themselves  finally. The study showed that, in fact, the opposite will be the case.  Unable to afford the more expensive modified grain and the chemical  products necessary for their cultivation, poor farmers will descend a  spiral of debt, and ultimately will be driven from their land. The only  agricultural beneficiaries will be the large monoculture farms, and the  four companies that dominate the market: Montsanto, Syngenta, Bayer  CropScience and Dupont. According to the study, the real motivation of  these companies is not to help poor farmers in third world countries,  but to increase their profits. The information they propagate is  destined not to inform, but to influence, advancing the economic  interests of the companies and nothing else.</p>
<p>Here is yet another example of information, or rather  disinformation, used to advance a particular agenda. This is reminiscent  of the use of information, or rather disinformation, by the US  government to justify its recent invasion of Iraq. It is no surprise  that the current US administration is one of the greatest, if not the  greatest proponent of the use of OGMs. The US is currently badgering the  European Union to allow the importation of OGMs, menacing to take the  case into the international legal arena. Europe seems to have caved in  to the pressure, insisting only that all OGM products be labeled, which  seems to be a strict minimum. In the USA and Canada, there is no  labeling of OGM products! American consumers have no way of knowing what  foods they purchase and consume are genetically modified. This policy  is as reckless as the military adventure in Iraq, by a government  subservient to big money and big business.</p>
<p>It is getting harder and harder to know just what to  believe. The first responsibility of any government should be the  protection of its citizens and the advancement of their well being. The  current policies of the American government, however, seem devoted to  the interests of large corporations rather than to interests of the  citizens it was elected to serve. Regarding the use of pesticides etc. I  do admit that the question is very complex, and plead guilty to the use  of chemical pesticides, at least in the past. A few years ago, we  experienced an invasion of colaspis or pine beetles. They emerged during  the second week of the New Orleans Jazz Festival (first week of May).  The effect on the cypress and pine trees is devastating. They eat the  spine of each needle, causing the leaf to die, leaving the tree brown  and burnt looking as though it has been caught in a fire or doused with  herbicide.</p>
<p>The tree is not killed by this activity but the result  is very depressing. Amidst the reckless verdant springing of spring, the  cypress and the pines look as though they have died. In order to combat  this intrusion upon our sense of well being, we would put on our  astronaut garb and spray the trees with chemical pesticides. Although we  were able to put a crimp in their style, we were never able to stop the  colasp&icirc;s beetles completely, and finally we gave up. Every year now we  simply grin and bear it and hope that a flock of chickadees will one day  discover this insectivore&rsquo;s paradise and take up residence in late  April on their way back from Cuba.</p>
<p>The experience with the pine beetles has proven to me  that there are no cut and fast rules when it comes to dealing with  Nature. What seems to be a good thing may effect some other part of the  chain with consequences as dire as those we are attempting to avoid.  Take whole wheat bread, the harvesting of the grain of which kills  multitudes of rabbits and meadow larks and quail who have taken up  residence in the tall wheat. Or blow dryers in public washrooms for  drying hands. You would think that the resulting economy of all the  paper not used to dry all those hands would be a good thing, were it not  for the pollution caused by the plants that make the hand dryers. Etc.  etc. We are obliged to make choices in dealing with the natural  environment around us. To make the best choice, we need the best  information which is where the problem lies, particularly when one is  governed by an administration such as the current one which is prepared  to compromise the quality of the national parks, which belong to all of  the citizens of the USA, for the benefit of a few timber companies. Or  the Alaska Refuge which it is prepared to sacrifice for the sake of a  very insignificant amount of oil. How about conservation? How about fuel  economy? How about alternative fuel? How about Haliburton contracts in  Iraq?</p>
<p>In any event I will admit that old habits are hard to  break. And this from a reformed pesticide addict. Just try convincing  your neighbor that nitrate and herbicide are a bad thing for the  environment in spite of how good he or she feels about his or her  uniformly green and smooth as a carpet new mowed lawn. Our esthetics  have been so influenced by the marketing of uniformity that we have  become a nation of lawn mower freaks. My grandfather&rsquo;s yard, with its  plethora of randomly scattered flowers and so called weeds was a haven  for bees and a multitude of insects which fed a multitude of birds. All  of that has gone by the wayside in an effort to control nature, even  though nature is best left to control herself. But we are part of Nature  and must therefore make choices that will impact not only our lives,  but the lives of all things living around us.</p>
<p>We can only hope to act in the most positive or at  least in the least negative way possible. As in the case of my Texas rat  snake. Finally his appetite did him in. One night after supper, I spied  his sinuous shape slithering up the purple martin pole. I am not sure  what he had in mind since he had emptied that particular housing project  days before. Maybe he thought the little houses just kept filling up  with delectable feathered creatures. Seizing the moment, I ran out and  shone my flashlight on the snake, cornering him in the empty cage.  Claude and I wound up pulling out the lawn chairs and just watching him,  waiting for some inspiration. Finally, Claude came up with the idea.  She suggested that we throw a plastic bag over the cage, which I  promptly did, imprisoning the snake and securing him with a double twist  of left-over-from-the-terrorist-attack duct tape.</p>
<p>The next morning we woke to find our rat snake coiled  up near the bottom of his plastic prison. He was agitated early on, but  became more and more docile as the morning wore on, overcome by the heat  and the lack of air. We, on the other hand, remained in a frenzy. Now  that we had the snake, I was still unsure about what to do.
